201 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Elliott


No. 10575


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


89 N.M. 305; 1976-NMSC-030; 551 P.2d 1352; 1976 N.M. LEXIS 811



June 25, 1976 



DISPOSITION:  Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State sought a writ of certiorari to challenge a decision of the New Mexico Court of Appeals, which reversed defendant's conviction for sodomy in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-9-6 (1972) and held the sodomy statute to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sodomy under the state statute. The court of appeals reversed the conviction and held that the statute was unconstitutional. At the request of the State, a writ of certiorari was issued to the New Mexico Court of Appeals. The court reversed the opinion of the Court of Appeals insofar as it held to be unconstitutional N. M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-9-6 (1972), which was the sodomy statute in effect at the time of the crime but which had since been repealed and replaced by N. M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-9-21 (Supp.1975). The court noted that the Court of Appeals based its holding on the ground that the statute embraced and proscribed sodomitic conduct on the part of the consenting adults, contrary to the rights guaranteed to them under the United States Constitution. In light of United States Supreme Court decisions on the subject, the New Mexico sodomy statute was constitutionally valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Court of Appeals and remanded the case to the Court of Appeals for further consideration.

 

202 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Robinson


No. 10837


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


89 N.M. 199; 1976-NMSC-019; 549 P.2d 277; 1976 N.M. LEXIS 802



April 27, 1976 



DISPOSITION:  Decision of the Court of Appeals reversed; decision of trial court affirmed; case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a judgment from the New Mexico Court of Appeals, which reversed a district court decision and held that the State was required to provide the identity of a confidential informant to defendants. The State's petition for a writ of certiorari presented several questions including the issue of when an informant and a police officer were both witness to the crime was the informer privilege rendered inapplicable.


OVERVIEW: Defendants filed a motion requesting the State to identify and produce a confidential informant who was a witness along with a police officer in the sale of narcotics, which formed the basis for the prosecution of defendants. The trial judge held an in camera hearing and denied the disclosure. Defendants appealed to the Court of Appeals. The Court of Appeals reversed and remanded for new considerations. A second trial judge held an in camera hearing and denied the disclosure. The Court of Appeals reversed and ordered disclosure. The court disagreed and noted that two trial judges held separate in camera hearings. Both concluded that, based upon the particular circumstances of this case, the state should not have been required to disclose the informer's identity, since his testimony would not be relevant and helpful to the defense of the accused, or necessary to a fair determination of the issue of their guilt or innocence. The court noted that it had reviewed the record, including the transcript of the second in camera proceeding and concluded that the trial court was correct and clearly did not abuse its discretion.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Court of Appeals was reversed and the decision of the trial court was affirmed.

 

203 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Tsiosdia v. Rainaldi


No. 10456


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


89 N.M. 70; 1976-NMSC-011; 547 P.2d 553; 1976 N.M. LEXIS 789



March 23, 1976 



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant individuals challenged the decision of the district court (New Mexico), which denied the individual's motion to alter or amend a judgment discharging a writ of prohibition, that prohibited respondent judge from hearing the cases charging the individuals with violating municipal codes prohibiting disorderly conduct, resisting arrest, assault, and battery.


OVERVIEW: The individuals contended that allowing non-attorney court judges to preside over criminal cases arising from violations of municipal ordinances which were punishable by incarceration violated rights guaranteed by the state constitution to defendants in these proceedings. The court rejected the individuals' contentions that all non-attorney judges inherently could not have been fair and impartial. The court reasoned that fairness was not so inextricably tied to the education of an attorney that without such an education a municipal court judge could not have been fair. The court further rejected the individuals' contention that a statutory scheme, which allowed defendants in two municipalities to have been tried before an attorney judge but allows defendants in other municipalities to have been tried before non-attorney judges, denied them the equal protection of the law under the state and federal constitutions. The court held that beyond merely asserting this argument, the individuals failed to show that they were correct in concluding that an equal protection problem arose when municipalities, pursuant to powers given to them by the legislature, enacted different ordinances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

204 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Ealey v. Bureau of Revenue


No. 10738


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


89 N.M. 160; 1976-NMSC-010; 548 P.2d 440; 1976 N.M. LEXIS 793



March 22, 1976 



DISPOSITION:  Order and decision of Bureau of Revenue reversed, and case returned to that body.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Bureau of Revenue of the State of New Mexico, petitioned for a writ of certiorari to challenge a two-to-one decision of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico) in favor of appellant taxpayer in the taxpayer's appeal from the Bureau's denial of her request for a refund of taxes paid to the State of New Mexico on gross receipts derived from the transmission of interstate telegraphic messages.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a telegraph company agent who transmitted interstate and intrastate messages. She was paid a set rate per message or money order sent or received. She filed an informal protest of a denial of her claim for a refund of taxes assessed against her, and the Bureau denied the request. Two judges of the intermediate appellate court held that her income fell within the definition of "gross receipts" in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16A-3(F) (Supp.1975), but one of those judges and the third judge denied the applicability of the deduction in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16A-14.10 (Supp.1975) for receipts from transactions in interstate commerce. The court reversed the Bureau's order and decision. The language of § 72-16A-14.10 was clear and unambiguous, and it applied to the taxpayer insofar as she transmitted interstate messages. The court held that the taxpayer's activities constituted interstate commerce when she sent messages bound for another state because interstate messages, once transmitted, were part of a national communications network. The taxpayer was therefore allowed to deduct from her gross receipts amounts she obtained from messages bound for points outside New Mexico.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Bureau's order and decision. The case was returned to the Bureau for the purpose of defining the percentages of the taxpayer's gross receipts derived from interstate and intrastate commerce and levying the tax on the intrastate portion.

 

205 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Trivitt


No. 10159


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


89 N.M. 162; 1976-NMSC-004; 548 P.2d 442; 1976 N.M. LEXIS 794



February 17, 1976 



DISPOSITION:  Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District in Colfax County (New Mexico), entered after a jury trial, that convicted him of first degree murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant's motion for severance of his trial from that of a co-defendant was granted, as was his motion for a change of venue from another county.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of felony murder after a service station robbery. The court reversed the judgment. The exclusion of three veniremen because of their opposition to the death penalty did not violate defendant's rights under U.S. Const. amend. VI, XIV or deprive him of his right to an impartial jury. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-29-2 (Supp. 1973), requiring a death sentence for conviction of a capital felony, did not violate N.M. Const. art. IV, § 18. The legislature was presumed to know that first degree murder was the only offense to which it applied. The title of the bill that enacted § 40A-29-2 did not violate N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16, and the reference in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-2-(A)(3) to "any felony" gave sufficient notice of the statute's true import to satisfy N.M. Const. art. IV, § 18. No showing was made that defendant's counsel did not use a normal and customary degree of skill. Reversal was required because the trial court improperly instructed the jury that it could find defendant guilty of first degree murder if it found that he committed any kind of willful, deliberate, and premeditated killing. No such charges were made in the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment and remanded the action to the district court for a new trial.

 

206 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Prince v. Bd. of Educ.


No. 10061


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


88 N.M. 548; 1975-NMSC-068; 543 P.2d 1176; 1975 N.M. LEXIS 863



December 22, 1975 



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant residents challenged an order from the San Juan County District Court (New Mexico), which dismissed their claim seeking to set aside a school board election and the approval of a bond issue. The residents also challenged a judgment finding appellee school district could legally construct or improve buildings on Indian reservation land that was not owned by it or under its exclusive jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The school district contained lands both on and off an Indian reservation. Lands within the reservation were not subject to state property taxes. The residents sought to have a school board election during which a bond issue was passed set aside alleging reservation residents had illegally cast votes. The residents also sought a declaratory judgment that the school district could not construct or improve buildings on reservation lands. The trial court found against the residents. On appeal, the court affirmed. The reservation residents were properly included in the election. N.M. Const. art. IX, § 11, restricting the right to vote in school district bond elections to real estate owners and those who paid a property tax on property in the school district, violated the equal protection clause of the United States Constitution.Navajo tribal self-government and federal rights did not conflict with the State's operation and exclusive control of schools on reservation lands leased by the school district. The State was required to provide public education to all of its citizens and the location of schools a long distance outside reservation lands would have been a denial of that right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the residents' action seeking to set aside the election and the approval of the bond issue, and the finding that the school district could construct or improve buildings on Indian reservation land.

 

207 of 795 DOCUMENTS


McGeehan v. Bunch


No. 10223


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


88 N.M. 308; 1975-NMSC-055; 540 P.2d 238; 1975 N.M. LEXIS 851



September 23, 1975 



DISPOSITION:  Cause remanded with instructions to vacate order granting motion to dismiss, and to allow plaintiff to proceed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passenger brought a negligence action against defendant driver. The Court of Appeals (New Mexico) affirmed the decision of the district court, which granted the driver's motion to dismiss the passenger's action on the ground that the facts as stated in the complaint fell within the terms of New Mexico's "guest statute," N.M. Stat. Ann. § 64-24-1. The passenger then petitioned for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The passenger claimed that she was injured while a guest in the driver's car, alleging that he failed to use due and ordinary care while operating his vehicle. The driver replied that the New Mexico guest statute barred the passenger's complaint. In turn, the passenger attacked the constitutionality of the guest statute as violative of N.M. Const. art. II, § 18 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV, in that it arbitrarily and unreasonably discriminated between paying and nonpaying guests. Agreeing with the driver, the district court dismissed the passenger's complaint. The court of appeals affirmed. The passenger sought certiorari review. The court held that the guest statute was void because it denied equal protection of the law. Applying rational basis review, the court reasoned that the classification imposed by the guest statute was unreasonable, arbitrary, and did not rest upon some ground of difference having a fair and substantial relation to either of the objects of the legislation. In sum, the classifications did not bear a substantial and rational relation to the statute's purposes of protecting the hospitality of the host driver and preventing collusive lawsuits.


OUTCOME: Finding that the New Mexico guest statute was unconstitutional and void as a denial of equal protection of the law, the court remanded the passenger's cause to the district court with instructions to vacate its order granting the driver's motion to dismiss and to allow the passenger to proceed with her negligence action.

 

208 of 795 DOCUMENTS


De Vargas Sav. & Loan Ass'n of Santa Fe v. Campbell


No. 10053


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


87 N.M. 469; 1975-NMSC-026; 535 P.2d 1320; 1975 N.M. LEXIS 822



May 21, 1975 



DISPOSITION:  Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, four savings and loan associations located in Santa Fe, challenged the dismissal by a district court (New Mexico) of their petition seeking review of an order of appellee, the Savings and Loan Supervisor of the New Mexico Department of Banking (supervisor), which had approved a branch office of intervenor building and loan association under § 48-15-133 of the Savings and Loan Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 48-15-45-142 (1953, Supp. 1972).


OVERVIEW: The supervisor granted authority to the intervenor to operate a branch office in Santa Fe, and the district court denied appellants' petition for judicial review. The appeals court then certified the case directly to the court. The court reversed and remanded, overruling Ruidoso State Bank v. Brumlow, 81 N.M. 379, 467 P.2d 395 (1970) and its progeny to find that appellants had standing to seek judicial review of the supervisor's order. To attain standing in an action arguing the unlawfulness of a governmental action, a complainant had to allege that he was injured in fact or was imminently threatened with injury, economically or otherwise. Appellants had standing to seek review of the supervisor's order as parties "aggrieved and directly affected" by the order under § 48-15-133. Appellants asserted they would suffer from undue competitive injury if another branch was permitted in Santa Fe because there was not sufficient business and demand to assure and maintain the solvency of existing associations. They also asserted that another branch would not be to the advantage of the community. The protection of such interests was explicitly recognized in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 48-15-61(A).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's dismissal of appellants' petition for review of the supervisor's order allowing intervenor to operate a branch in Santa Fe.

 

209 of 795 DOCUMENTS


City of Albuquerque v. Jones


No. 10033


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


87 N.M. 486; 1975-NMSC-025; 535 P.2d 1337; 1975 N.M. LEXIS 827



May 14, 1975 



DISPOSITION:  Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipality sought review of a judgment of the district court (New Mexico), which affirmed a municipal court ruling that an ordinance under which appellee motorcyclist was charged with violating, which required the operator of a motorcycle to wear an approved safety helmet, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in municipal court with violating a city ordinance that required the operator of a motorcycle to wear a safety helmet meeting standards specified by the motor vehicle department (DMV). The municipal court held the ordinance to be unconstitutional and the district court affirmed. On appeal by the municipality, the court reversed, explaining that the subject matter of the ordinance did not lie beyond the reach of the municipality's police power in that a rational basis for the ordinance was easily discernible. Not only would the measure protect the life and limb of the citizenry, but it would keep citizens out of hospitals and off the relief rolls. The court observed that ordinances, like statutes, were presumed to be valid and that defendant failed to sustain his burden of establishing its invalidity. Moreover, the ordinance's delegation to the DMV of the power to determine what type of helmet should be worn did not deprive defendant of due process, as delegated standards needed not be specific as long as they were capable of reasonable understanding. The court noted that the testing methods for arriving at the DMV standards had not been challenged.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court ruling that the ordinance was unconstitutional, and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

210 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Gonzales v. Manzagol


No. 10038


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


87 N.M. 230; 1975-NMSC-002; 531 P.2d 1203; 1975 N.M. LEXIS 789



January 31, 1975 



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant councilman challenged the decision of the trial court (New Mexico), which found in favor of appellee State in the councilman's action to prevent the State from terminating him from his state job.


OVERVIEW: The councilman was employed by the State as a Water Resource Assistant. The councilman then ran for office and was elected to the position of councilman. The State sought to discharge him from his position and the councilman filed an action against the State to prevent the discharge. The trial court found in favor of the State. On review, the court found that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 5-4-42(B) provided that no person in the personnel office could hold political office during his or her employment. Furthermore, the court found that the position of councilman was a political office. The court reasoned that the councilman ran as a member of an organized slate of candidates who adopted a name and a platform, solicited funds to support the election of the slate, and advertised as a slate. Furthermore, it was the councilman's burden to show that persons similarly situated were treated differently in an impermissible manner, which he failed to do. Therefore, the trial court's decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that found in favor of the State was affirmed.

Moya v. Chilili Coop. Ass'n


No. 9716


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


87 N.M. 99; 1974-NMSC-100; 529 P.2d 1220; 1974 N.M. LEXIS 1486



December 20, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs resident sought review of a judgment of the district court (New Mexico), in favor of defendant association in a action in which the residents sought among other things, injunctive relief, dissolution of the association, the appointment of a receiver to administer the assets of the association, and a determination of the heirs to a land grant.


OVERVIEW: A land grant gave to 20 families a certain tract of land, including the land upon which a town was located. The grant was confirmed by the United States Congress and patented by the United States to the town in 1909. The lands had been deeded to the state to satisfy delinquent taxes. Quitclaim deeds were executed by which all grant lands were conveyed to the association. One of the deeds was executed by the town as grantor through its board of trustees. The deed was executed after the effective date of 1943 N.M. Laws ch. 47, § 67. The other deed was executed by many of the residents of the town. The association paid the taxes and redeemed the land. The residents filed an action in which they sought, among other things, injunctive relief and a determination of the heirs to the land grant. The lower court granted a judgment in favor of the association. On review, it was alleged that the residents were vested with property and participatory rights in the common lands of the grant by the 1909 patent. The court affirmed. The court held that based on previous case law no property interest in the common lands were conveyed to the individual residents of the grant by the 1909 patent.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

212 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Dillon v. King


No. 9895


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


87 N.M. 79; 1974-NMSC-096; 529 P.2d 745; 1974 N.M. LEXIS 1482



December 6, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant election candidate sought review of a judgment rendered by the trial court (New Mexico) in favor of appellees, the governor and other state officials in the candidate's action challenging the constitutionality of election laws.


OVERVIEW: The candidate claimed that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-8-24.1 was an unconstitutional burden to his right to run for political office by requiring them to obtain a number of signatures from election party members. The trial court ruled against the candidate and he appealed the ruling. The court held that the requirements that a candidate obtain a number of signatures before being placed on the ballot was not a denial of due process because the State had a legitimate interest in regulating the size of the ballot so as to minimize voter confusion and to prevent the overwhelming of voting machines. The court also determined that the requirement of obtaining signatures was not unreasonable or obtrusive. Further, the court stated that the legislation would not be deemed unconstitutional under N.M. Const. art. 4, § 5 on the grounds that the legislature was not authorized to pass the law because that argument could only be made prospectively from the date of this decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

213 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Martinez v. Jaramillo


No. 9721


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


86 N.M. 506; 1974-NMSC-069; 525 P.2d 866; 1974 N.M. LEXIS 1433



August 23, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, owners and operators of valid dispenser's licenses and Sunday sales permits, sought injunctive relief from the enforcement of the Sunday liquor sales provision of N.M. Stat. Ann. §46-10-14.1 (1953), by defendants, the New Mexico Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control and its Director. Defendants sought review of the temporary restraining order issued by the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico).


OVERVIEW: After local option elections failed to approve Sunday sales in their districts, appellants notified appellees that they could no longer sell alcoholic beverages on Sunday, and that the Liquor Control Act would be enforced against each of them. The trial court declared that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 46-10-14.1(D) of the Act was unconstitutional because the title to that Act did not include local option elections and was not broad enough to give notice of the subject matter actually contained in § 46-10-14.1(D), as required by N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16. On appeal, the court held that examination of the title of the Act led to the conclusion that the title was a restrictive one and limited the broad subject of alcoholic liquors. The title was restrictive in nature, the matter of local option district elections could not be considered germane to the subject matter expressed in the title. There was nothing contained in the title that could alert the reader that elections were contemplated. The court held that local option district elections did not have a logical and natural connection with the hours and days of business for the sale of alcoholic beverages.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

McDaniel v. N.M. Bd. of Med. Exam'rs


No. 9798


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


86 N.M. 447; 1974-NMSC-062; 525 P.2d 374; 1974 N.M. LEXIS 1427



August 2, 1974 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 19, 1974.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent New Mexico Board of Medical Examiners challenged a decision from the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which reversed two decisions and an order from the Board that revoked the license of petitioner doctor to practice medicine in New Mexico.


OVERVIEW: The doctor had his license revoked and reinstated with a term of probation for unlawfully prescribing controlled substances to himself. During the probation it was discovered that he had prescribed another controlled substance to himself. The Board determined that the drug was a dangerous substance and that the doctor had prescribed it for his own use. The Board ordered the doctor to surrender his license. The doctor initiated a judicial review and the trial court reversed the Board's decision because it determined that the actions of the Board were arbitrary and capricious and were not based on substantial evidence. The Board asserted that its decision was based on substantial evidence and the terms of the probation were not vague. The court reversed the decision and remanded the case with directions to reinstate the decision from the Board because it determined that the Board had not acted arbitrarily and capriciously since it had acted on substantial evidence and the knowledge of the Board members in revoking the probationary period and the probation had adequately informed the doctor of the conduct that was prohibited during the probation period.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision from the trial court that reversed two decisions and an order from the Board that revoked the license of appellee doctor to practice medicine and remanded the case to reinstate and give effect to the decisions and order from the Board.

 

215 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Sego v. Kirkpatrick


No. 9973


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


86 N.M. 359; 1974-NMSC-059; 524 P.2d 975; 1974 N.M. LEXIS 1418



July 19, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  Peremptory writ of mandamus issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizen initiated an original proceeding in mandamus concerning respondent governor's vetoes and attempted vetoes of certain language contained in the General Appropriations Act of 1974 (House Bill 300), 1974 N.M. Laws 3. The court undertook to issue a written opinion after it had issued a peremptory writ commanding respondents, the governor and other state officials, to permanently treat as nullities certain of the attempted vetoes.


OVERVIEW: Under the claimed authority of N.M. Const. art. IV, § 22, the governor vetoed certain language in three contingent appropriations and an appropriation that established a revolving fund. The governor also struck a phrase from the general provisions section of House Bill 300, and struck from ten separately designated categories, including the higher education category, language relating to the legislature's purported appropriations of non-state funds. The court held invalid the vetoes involving the three contingent appropriations because they would have affirmatively appropriated the sums involved without conditions. The court upheld the veto concerning the revolving fund because it did not change the stated purpose of the fund. The court upheld the veto of certain language from the higher education category that did not alter or effect the remaining portions of that part of House Bill 300, but invalidated the governor's remaining vetoes because they conditionally appropriated additional funds to the state agencies not included in the ten categories. The court also held that the legislature lacked authority to appropriate non-state funds available to institutions of higher learning.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed its previously issued peremptory writ of mandamus.

 

216 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Cooper v. Albuquerque City Comm'n


No. 9774


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


85 N.M. 786; 1974-NMSC-006; 518 P.2d 275; 1974 N.M. LEXIS 1355



January 18, 1974 



DISPOSITION:  Affirmed in part, reversed in part and writ of mandamus quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor municipal judge appealed from that portion of the district court's (New Mexico) judgment commanding defendants, municipality's governing body and its members, to order a recall election of the municipal judge. Plaintiff voter cross-appealed from that portion of the judgment permitting the intervention.


OVERVIEW: After the trial was concluded and the district court announced the substance of the judgment it proposed to enter, the municipality's governing body and its members indicated they had no intention of appealing from that judgment commanding them to conduct a recall election. The municipal judge filed a motion to intervene, which was granted. On appeal, the court affirmed the district court's action in permitting the intervention. The district court did not abuse its discretion in granting the intervention because the municipal judge filed a motion to intervene promptly after the municipality's governing body and its members announced that they did not intend to appeal from the threatened adverse ruling. Before that announcement he had no reason to intervene, as his interests were protected. The municipal judge did not waive his right to intervene. The court reversed the judgment commanding the municipality's governing body and its members to conduct a recall election because it was fairly implied from N.M. Const. art. VI, § 32, which created a Judicial Standards Commission, that no legislatively created means of disciplining judicial officers should be recognized.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's action in permitting the intervention. The court reversed its action in commanding the calling of a recall election. The court reversed the judgment making the alternative writ of mandamus permanent and thereby commanding the municipality's governing body and its members to conduct a recall election. The court quashed the permanent writ of mandamus.

 

217 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Las Cruces Urban Renewal Agency v. El Paso Elec. Co.


No. 9644


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


86 N.M. 305; 1974-NMSC-004; 523 P.2d 549; 1974 N.M. LEXIS 1410



January 11, 1974 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 18, 1974.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Urban Renewal Agency filed a declaratory judgment action against appellant utilities, in which appellee city was joined as an involuntary plaintiff, to determine the obligations of the parties for a portion of the costs associated with an urban renewal project. The trial court (New Mexico) held that the utilities were not entitled to compensation by appellees. The utilities appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city, by ordinance, granted, and the utilities accepted, a franchise for the construction and maintenance of overhead lines and facilities over streets and alleys including those within the urban renewal project. According to the franchise agreement, the utilities agreed to "encourage and promote" underground cables and facilities and the city was to be "agreeable in supporting the cost differential" for the project. The court held that the ordinance was so vague, ambiguous, indefinite and uncertain as to be unenforceable. The court also noted that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 14-47-9.1, which provided for the payment by municipalities of the expense of relocation of facilities in urban renewal projects, was not applicable because the statute explicitly did not apply to existing urban renewal projects. Since the urban renewal project had been fully approved prior to the effective date of the statute, even though there were subsequent amendments to the project, that statute was ineffective. The court, after finding that there were no misrepresentations or concealments, held that the defense of estoppel was inapplicable. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which found that the utilities were not entitled to compensation by appellees, was affirmed.

 

218 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Gomez v. Bd. of Educ.


No. 9763


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


85 N.M. 708; 1973-NMSC-116; 516 P.2d 679; 1973 N.M. LEXIS 1314



November 30, 1973 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: November 30, 1973


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF RIO ARRIBA COUNTY, FELTER, Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bus owner challenged a judgment of dismissal rendered by the District Court of Rio Arriba County (New Mexico) in favor of appellees, school district, school board members, and state transportation director, in an action brought by the bus service seeking damages from appellees as a result of their decision to cancel or, in the alternative, not renew the school district's bus service contract with the bus owner.


OVERVIEW: The bus owner claimed the school district and school board made oral representations that his contract to provide service would be renewed; however, after he and others filed an election contest, he was told his contract would not be renewed. The letter sent to the bus owner by the school board stated that the bus owner's legal actions against the school board constituted cause for nonrenewal. The bus owner brought suit against defendants, claiming their actions were unreasonable and constituted a deprivation of his rights of free speech and association. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss and the court reversed. It found that although there was no actual contract involved, that alone did not defeat the bus owner's claim that the nonrenewal of his contract violated his rights to free speech and association. Further, the bus owner's participation in a lawsuit against the school board was a constitutionally protected right that fell under the rights covered by 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. As to defendants' liability, the court determined that the application of the doctrine of qualified immunity was appropriate if the was a showing of good faith on their part.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court holding that the bus owner's complaint failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted and found that the determination of defendants' good faith for purposes of their qualified involved development and evaluation of the facts.

 

219 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Huey v. Lente


No. 9777


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


85 N.M. 597; 1973-NMSC-098; 514 P.2d 1093; 1973 N.M. LEXIS 1295



September 28, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a married couple, appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which reversed a judgment rendered in favor of the married couple in their action to terminate respondent mother's parental rights to her infant son pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-2-23 (Supp. 1971).


OVERVIEW: The appellate court reversed the judgment that terminated the mother's parental rights to her infant son and held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-2-23 (Supp. 1971) was unconstitutional because it violated N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16. The court held that: (1) the appellate court erred because it was not necessary to hold § 22-2-23 to be unconstitutional and it was improper to decide constitutional questions that were unnecessary to the disposition of a case; (2) the appellate court appeared to have confused § 22-2-23, which dealt with the termination of parental rights, and N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-2-33(A)(2) (Supp. 1971), which dealt with the rights created between an adopted parent and a child being adopted; (3) § 22-2-23 was not unconstitutional; and (4) the quantum of proof necessary in a § 22-2-23 action was clear and convincing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

220 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Norvell v. Credit Bureau of Albuquerque, Inc.


No. 9448


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


85 N.M. 521; 1973-NMSC-087; 514 P.2d 40; 1973 N.M. LEXIS 1283



September 7, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, FOWLIE, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff debtor filed an action against defendant credit bureau alleging she was sued and garnished by the credit bureau, which was unlawfully practicing law. After other debtors filed similar actions the state intervened and sought declaratory and injunctive relief. The District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) consolidated the cases and granted some relief and denied other relief. The state and credit bureau sought review.


OVERVIEW: The court held individual members of the state bar that intervened were not proper parties to the appeal as they failed to comply with N.M. Sup. Ct. R. 5(5), N.M. Stat. Ann. § 21-2-1(5)(5) (1953). The court held the attorney general was a proper party as the complaint in the intervention was captioned the State ex rel. David Norvell, Attorney General. The court found the credit bureau was licensed under the Collection Agency Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 67-15-22 to 67-1-89 (1953), letters were sent to debtors by employees who were not lawyers, the debtors were then sued by the credit bureau as the creditors rights were assigned to the credit bureau, and the credit bureau controlled the entire litigation in the magistrate court. The record also proved the credit bureau's collection manager appeared at trial to litigate the case but if an attorney appeared for a debtor an attorney litigated the case. The court affirmed the grant of injunctive relief prohibiting the credit bureau from the unauthorized practice of law under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 18-1-26 (1953). The court reversed the denial of injunctive relief enjoining the soliciting assignments of claims on a contingency fee basis claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of injunctive relief prohibiting the credit bureau from engaging in the unauthorized practice of law, reversed and remanded the denial of injunctive relief regarding the letters were sent to the debtors.

 

221 of 795 DOCUMENTS


City of Albuquerque v. Garcia


No. 9531


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


84 N.M. 776; 1973-NMSC-036; 508 P.2d 585; 1973 N.M. LEXIS 1236; 71 A.L.R.3d 1



April 6, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON CERTIORARI



DISPOSITION: Court of Appeals reversed; case remanded to district court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passenger appealed a judgment from the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which reversed the trial court's dismissal of the passenger's negligence action against defendant city for injuries she sustained in an accident while traveling on a city bus.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the passenger's suit against the city, finding that the suit was barred by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 64-25-9 (1953), which addressed and referenced governmental immunity from tort liability arising out of the operation of a State political subdivision's vehicles. The court of appeals reversed the judgment, finding that the statute was constitutionally inadequate because the statute's title failed to mention the subject matter of sovereign immunity. The court granted certiorari and held that the statute did not create absolute sovereign immunity but merely restated or expanded upon existing common law immunity. The court found that by the literal terms of N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16, sovereign immunity was not the subject of the statute but was only incidentally at issue. Therefore, the failure to mention the subject matter of sovereign immunity in the tittle of the statute did not violate the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

 

222 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Reynolds v. Lewis


No. 9201


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


84 N.M. 768; 1973-NMSC-035; 508 P.2d 577; 1973 N.M. LEXIS 1233



April 5, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CHAVES County, LaFEL E. OMAN, J., COURT OF APPEALS By Designation



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants landowners challenged an amended decision of the District Court of Chaves County (New Mexico), claiming that limiting the duty of water was a denial of due process and a taking without just compensation. Appellee state contended the trial court erred by assuming jurisdiction to grant a new appropriation of public water and by readjudicating the duty of water because its partial final judgment was a final order.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered a partial final judgment establishing the duty of water at three-acre feet per annum. It subsequently heard argument on a motion to modify that judgment and determined that there was evidence to support the duty of water and added a six-inch carriage loss as compensation for loss from the well. The court affirmed the judgment, finding that the trial court correctly determined that the partial final decree was somewhat ambiguous as to the duty of water and correctly proceeded to receive evidence in connection therewith as the parties were previously denied the opportunity to do so. The court also found there was substantial evidence to support the trial court's finding that the duty of water should properly be set at three-acre feet. Further, the order limiting the duty of water was not a denial of due process or the taking of property without just compensation as the trial court considered all of the matters in the record before it, including the conflicting evidence as to the annual duty of water and as to the amount of carriage losses, and the record indicated an exhaustive presentation of evidence directed to all the issues involved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order determining the water rights of the landowners and the state, and limiting the duty of water to three-acre feet per annum with a six-inch carriage loss as compensation for loss from the well.

 

223 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. One 1967 Peterbilt Tractor (In re One 1967 Peterbilt Tractor)


No. 9413


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


84 N.M. 652; 1973-NMSC-025; 506 P.2d 1199; 1973 N.M. LEXIS 1222



March 2, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LUNA COUNTY, HODGES, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Luna County (New Mexico), which, in a proceedings to declare the forfeiture of a tractor and trailer pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 54-7-26, 54-7-26.1 (Supp. 1971) that was initiated by appellee State, declared the forfeiture of both. The owner contended that the forfeiture of the equipment was based on the results of an illegal search and seizure.


OVERVIEW: The State police were contacted by an informant and told that the owner was regularly transporting amphetamines on trips west from Texas through the State. The police stopped and searched the tractor and trailer and seized 214 bottles of amphetamines. The court noted that the issue was whether there was probable cause to believe contraband was stored in or transported by the tractor and trailer at the time the search leading to the discovery of the amphetamines was conducted. The court held that that probable cause existed and that the trial court's refusal to suppress was correct. The information regarding the "sale," detailed information concerning the description of the owner and driver, the fact that he would be armed, the fact that a lady was traveling with him, and the recitation of the make and color of the tractor and the color of the trailer, considered together with the testimony concerning informant's reliability, furnished an adequate basis for the trial court's finding of probable cause.


OUTCOME: The judgment of forfeiture was affirmed.

 

224 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Comm'r of Motor Vehicles v. McCain (In re McCain)


No. 9540


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


84 N.M. 657; 1973-NMSC-023; 506 P.2d 1204; 1973 N.M. LEXIS 1217



February 23, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LEA COUNTY, NASH, Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Commissioner of Motor Vehicles of the State of New Mexico, sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Lea County (New Mexico), which rescinded the Commissioner's order revoking the driver's license of appellee driver pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 64-22-2.11 (1953).


OVERVIEW: Appellee was arrested for driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. Her driver's license was revoked because she refused to take a chemical test. The trial court rescinded the order revoking appellee's license. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 64-22-2.11 of the Implied Consent Law provided adequate safeguards and did not violate the due process requirements of the state and federal constitutions. It was a valid and reasonable exercise of the state's police power. Nor did the Law deny equal protection. It affected all persons licensed to operate motor vehicles. It was reasonable to make a separate classification for those who refused to submit to the test and it was not unreasonable that harsher treatment was given to those who refused to submit. Section 64-22-2.11 was not limited in application to public highways, streets, and thoroughfares. The arresting officer had reasonable grounds to believe that appellee was driving while under the influence. He properly advised her that failure to submit to the test would result in revocation of her license. Her acquittal of the crime did not affect the proceeding to revoke her license.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the district court and remanded the cause for further proceedings consistent with its opinion.

226 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Aguirre


No. 9490


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


84 N.M. 376; 1972-NMSC-081; 503 P.2d 1154; 1972 N.M. LEXIS 912



December 8, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CHAVES COUNTY, SNEAD, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Chaves County (New Mexico), which convicted him of kidnapping, rape, and assault with intent to commit a violent felony. Defendant claimed that the trial court abused its discretion or committed error in denying his motion for a change of venue, in allowing two other young women to testify concerning a similar crime, and in admitting the victim's in-court identification of him.


OVERVIEW: The evidence indicated that defendant stopped a young girl, forced himself into her pickup, and forced her to drive him into the country. He then raped her and attempted to strangle her. To support his motion that he could not get a fair trial in the county, he submitted five newspaper articles. The court held that the trial court's findings that he could received a fair trial in the county was supported by the evidence and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying his change of venue motion. Evidence from two female witnesses that an individual in a vehicle similar to defendant's had attempted to force them to stop in a manner used by the offender was admissible to prove the identity of defendant as the person who committed the crime. The court held that the trial court did not commit error in holding that the in-court identification of defendant by the victim was not tainted by the police showing photographs of defendant to the victim when she was in the hospital. Her identification of defendant was positive, and nothing suggested any dependence on the earlier identification of his photographs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

 

227 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jimenez


No. 9469


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


84 N.M. 335; 1972-NMSC-073; 503 P.2d 315; 1972 N.M. LEXIS 906



November 22, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF QUAY COUNTY, GALLEGOS, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed a judgment from the District Court of Quay County (New Mexico), which convicted him of first-degree murder. On the State's motion, defendant was certified as an adult under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 13-8-27 (1953) and was tried as such. At issue, inter alia, was the application of N.M. Const. art. II, § 18 and art. IV, § 16, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40(A)-2-1.


OVERVIEW: The victim died as the result of a blow on the head and face with a blunt instrument. Defendant was seen at the victim's home shortly before the crime was discovered. He had armed himself with a rock before entering her apartment, and he admitted to striking the victim with the rock and that he had taken a gun and cash from the apartment. On appeal, the court ruled, inter alia, that (1) prior court precedent established, contrary to defendant's contention, that the procedure in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 13-8-27 for certifying juveniles as adults did not violate N.M. Const. art. II, § 18 or U.S. Const. amend. XIV; (2) 1959 N.M. Laws 361 (Act), the enabling legislation for N.M. Stat. Ann. § 13-8-27, gave adequate notice that provisions for certification of a juvenile reasonably could have been found within the Act, for purposes of N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16; (3) the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying defendant's motion for change on venue; and (4) the facts and circumstances of the case unerringly established defendant's guilt of first-degree murder beyond any reasonable doubt, and thus substantial evidence supported his conviction under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-2-1(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

228 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. State Highway Comm'n v. Hesselden Inv. Co.


No. 9347


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


84 N.M. 424; 1972-NMSC-071; 504 P.2d 634; 1972 N.M. LEXIS 901



November 3, 1972 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 4, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TORRANCE COUNTY, BURKS, Judge



DISPOSITION: Cross-appeal dismissed and judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State Highway Commission of New Mexico sought review of the decision from the District Court of Torrance County (New Mexico), which awarded damages to appellee landowner in the State's eminent domain action condemning the landowner's property.


OVERVIEW: The State instituted condemnation proceedings against the landowner. The jury awarded the landowner damages for the partial taking. On appeal, the State claimed that the trial court erroneously adopted for the measure of damages, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-9-9.1 (1953), 1968 N.M. Laws 30.1, approved and effective as of February 19, 1968, because the law was not yet in effect on the "date of taking," purportedly February 9, 1968. The court found that clearly and logically the "date of taking" was the date on which the condemnor became vested with the legal right to possession, dominion, and control over the real estate being condemned. This date was March 5, 1968, the date of the order making the preliminary order of entry permanent. Thus the court held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-9-9.1 (1953) correctly stated the measure of damages applicable to the partial taking and was in effect on the date of taking. The court also found that the statute did not amend, alter, or modify other statutes during the pendency of a case in violation of N.M. Const. art. IV, § 34; rather, it merely codified the correct and existing rule or measure of damages in cases of a partial taking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

229 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Montoya v. Blackhurst


No. 9453


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


84 N.M. 91; 1972-NMSC-058; 500 P.2d 176; 1972 N.M. LEXIS 892



August 4, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, WALTERS, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent magistrates appealed the judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) which granted petitioner, an individual, his request for an alternative writ of mandamus and declared the replevin statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 36-13-1 through 36-13-6 unconstitutional and enjoined the magistrates from enforcing the replevin statutes.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner challenged the magistrates' authority to allow the opposing party to replevy goods in the petitioner's possession upon posting a bond and filing an affidavit. Only if the petitioner posted a similar bond, would he be entitled to keep the goods until a hearing was held on the other party's claim. Thus, the petitioner could be deprived of the goods without notice and an opportunity to be heard, even if he had a good defense to the replevin action, and if he did not or could not post the required bond. On appeal, the court rejected the magistrates' assertion that mandamus could not be used to question the constitutionality of the replevin statute. The court found that the petitioner did not have an adequate remedy at law or by appeal. The court affirmed the trial court's determination that the New Mexico replevin statute, in so far as it provided for a pre-judgment taking of property without notice and hearing, was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

230 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Peck v. Ives


No. 9384


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


84 N.M. 62; 1972-NMSC-053; 499 P.2d 684; 1972 N.M. LEXIS 887



July 21, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, CAMPOS, Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor sought review of a judgment by the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee homeowner on the contractor's action to foreclose on a mechanic's lien.


OVERVIEW: Summary judgment was granted to the homeowner on the ground that the contractor was not licensed to enter into a contract to build the home because the ultimate cost of the residence exceeded $ 50,000 and was thus barred from bringing the action. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that (1) the contract between the parties was never finalized; (2) although a price of $ 40,000 to $ 45,000 was discussed, no firm price was ever agreed upon; (3) no set of final plans was ever agreed upon; and (5) the contractor billed and was paid on a monthly basis. The court held that even if the contractor had violated the New Mexico Construction Industries Licensing Act (Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 67-35-1 67-35-63 (1953), he nevertheless substantially complied with the licensing requirements. The court reasoned that when the parties agreed to begin construction on a cost plus percentage basis with monthly billings, the contractor held a valid license. The court also noted that the contractor renewed his license seven months after the house was completed, so that he was financially responsible for up $ 100,000.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to the homeowner.

 

231 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Turner v. Barnhart


No. 9367


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


83 N.M. 759; 1972-NMSC-036; 497 P.2d 970; 1972 N.M. LEXIS 873



June 2, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY LARRAZOLO, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants citizens challenged a judgment from the Bernalillo County District Court (New Mexico), which granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment in the citizens' suit seeking a declaratory judgment and injunction and found that the results of a municipal election to place fluoride in the city's water supply were valid.


OVERVIEW: The citizens filed suit, alleging that the city was estopped from placing fluoride in the city's water supply because the election process contained irregularities. The trial court granted the city's motion for summary judgment. The citizens appealed, arguing that the full text of the proposed ordinance was not placed on the ballot as required by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 14-13-17(B) (1953) (1968). The court affirmed. The court held that provisions reserving to the people the power of initiative and referendum were to be given a liberal construction to effectuate the policy being adopted. New Mexico recognized that technical irregularities did not necessarily required that the results of an election be disturbed. In addition, the election laws were liberally construed to accomplish their purpose. The court concluded that the term "text" as used in § 14-13-17 protected the public and was not unconstitutional. The grant of summary judgment was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

232 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. 44 Gunny Sacks of Grain


No. 9303


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


83 N.M. 755; 1972-NMSC-033; 497 P.2d 966; 1972 N.M. LEXIS 867



May 26, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OTERO COUNTY, STANLEY, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed as to contaminated sacks and affirmed in other respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision from the District Court of Otero County (New Mexico), which held that the State was required to reimburse appellee grain owner for grain seized pursuant to the New Mexico Food Act, N. M. Stat. Ann. 54-1-6(c) (1953).


OVERVIEW: The grain owner possessed sacks of grain contaminated by mercury. The State detained and embargoed the sacks of grain not sold under the New Mexico Food Act, N. M. Stat. Ann. §§ 54-1-1 to 54-1-19 (1953). The trial court found that two of the sacks of grain were contaminated according to federal standards and adulterated within the meaning of N. M. Stat. Ann. § 54-1-10. The trial court awarded damages to the grain owner for the value of these two sacks. On appeal, the court held that the action contemplated by N. M. Stat. Ann. § 54-1-6(c) was in rem and not against the grain owner. The court held that the State acted properly within its police power. The seizure of grain was not an unconstitutional taking without just compensation but rather an action taken under the police power for the protection of public health. Injury resulting from the proper exercise of the State's police power was not compensable. The State was not required to make compensation when it seized and destroyed food found to be contaminated within the provisions of The New Mexico Food Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court as to the contaminated sacks of grain.

 

233 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Apodaca v. Fiorina


No. 9454


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


83 N.M. 663; 1972-NMSC-025; 495 P.2d 1379; 1972 N.M. LEXIS 862



April 18, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL MANDAMUS PROCEEDINGS



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ of mandamus made absolute.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator citizens petitioned the New Mexico Supreme Court for a writ of mandamus to require Respondents, the Secretary of State and the Attorney General, to certify only the names of persons who paid the filing fees prescribed by § N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-8-26 (1970) as candidates in the primary election, or, alternatively, to certify only those who tendered such fees under such conditions and restrictions as the court prescribed.


OVERVIEW: The court had previously issued a temporary writ in the case preventing the Secretary of State from certifying candidates for state offices without the payment of filing fees. In a separate action certain citizens received a judgment from a three-judge panel in the federal district court that enjoined the Secretary of State from requiring the citizens to pay a filing fee before being listed in the last election as candidates for U.S. Senator. Based on that case, the Attorney General directed the Secretary of State to allow candidates for salaried state offices to be listed as candidates in the coming primary without the payment of filing fees. Respondents claimed that § 3-8-26(A) was unconstitutional and void as a violation of the equal protection clause of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court disagreed and held that there was a rational relationship between the filing fee requirement and the legislative duty to protect the purity of elections and guard against abuses of the elective franchise in order to meet the requirements of the equal protection safeguards. The court noted that the filing fees required to be paid did not involve an element of arbitrary discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court made the temporary writ absolute and upheld the filing fee requirement.

People's Constitutional Party v. Evans


No. 9120


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


83 N.M. 303; 1971-NMSC-116; 491 P.2d 520; 1971 N.M. LEXIS 1621



December 6, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, ANGEL, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Secretary of State sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Santa Fe (New Mexico), which declared that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-8-2(B), (C) and N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-8-3(C) (1970) were unconstitutional and which enjoined the Secretary from enforcing the provisions. The judgment arose from a declaratory action brought by plaintiffs, a political party and a citizen.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that the signature requirements of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-8-2(B), (C) and N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-8-3(C) constituted burdens that prevented minority parties from placing their nominees on the ballot. They predicated their claim upon the "free and open" election provision of N.M. Const. art. II, § 8. The court reversed the judgment, finding that the legislature determined that the signature list requirements provided by the statutes were consistent with its authority and duty to secure the purity of elections and guard against abuse. The court concluded that it was its duty to uphold the legislative determination unless satisfied beyond all reasonable doubt that the legislature went outside its constitutional authority in enacting the requirements. Plaintiffs also contented that the signature requirements under violated their constitutional rights of freedom of association. The court determined the State had a legitimate interest in trying to determine good faith on the part of electors who sign nominating petitions and in assuring at least a modicum of support for a political party and its nominees whose names were placed on the election ballot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

235 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Rodriguez v. Dist. Court of First Judicial Dist.


No. 9332


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


83 N.M. 200; 1971-NMSC-101; 490 P.2d 458; 1971 N.M. LEXIS 1606



October 28, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROHIBITION PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed an original prohibition proceeding to prohibit respondents, the District Court of the First Judicial District for Santa Fe County (New Mexico) and the district judge, from executing or enforcing a certain order directing the State to discharge a prisoner.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner pleaded guilty to an offense in a certain district court. He was sentenced. He filed a document with that court which was treated as a motion for a new trial and denied. He filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, and the presiding judge conditionally granted it, based on an assumed denial of the prisoner's right of appeal. The proviso was that the sentencing court might enter an order allowing an appeal before the date set for release, and thus avoid the writ. The sentencing judge was not informed of the order. On the date set for release the State got an order allowing an appeal, but this was not timely. Fifteen days later the time for the State to appeal the habeas order expired. The prisoner filed a second habeas petition, which was reluctantly granted by respondents. The State then filed the writ of prohibition. The court denied the writ of prohibition. The court held that even if the first habeas order were erroneous, the State had not appealed it and was bound by it. The court noted that the second habeas order aptly reflected this reasoning and could not lawfully be prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of prohibition sought by the State.

 

236 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Holiday Mgmt. Co. v. City of Santa Fe


No. 9095


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


83 N.M. 95; 1971-NMSC-088; 488 P.2d 730; 1971 N.M. LEXIS 1591



August 30, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, REESE, Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant City of Santa Fe sought review of a judgment entered in the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), in favor of plaintiff partnership in the partnership's action to enjoin the city from enforcing its zoning ordinance with respect to a non-conforming advertising sign.


OVERVIEW: The partnership purchased a motel in 1968 and also leased the advertising sign on the premises from a franchisor. The face area of the sign exceeded that permitted by a city ordinance adopted in 1964. The partnership's predecessor had constructed the motel, erected the sign in compliance with then-existing ordinances, and entered into a sign lease with the franchisor in 1961. On appeal of the judgment enjoining the city from enforcing the ordinance, the court held that the partnership had no standing to procure the injunction. Rejecting the partnership's claim that its sign lease was a reissue of the original lease and it was thus entitled to the same rights its predecessor had, the court held that the partnership's rights did not vest prior to the passage of the ordinance. The court also determined that the partnership could not claim that the ordinance as applied to it was unconstitutional by reason of the toleration period being arbitrarily short when its rights in the sign were not in existence at the time the ordinance was adopted and when it was aware of the sign ordinance at the time it acquired the motel and had knowingly acquired rights in a non-conforming use.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the partnership with instructions to dissolve the injunction and enter judgment for the city.

 

237 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Apodaca v. N.M. State Bd. of Educ.


No. 9193


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


82 N.M. 558; 1971-NMSC-058; 484 P.2d 1268; 1971 N.M. LEXIS 1566



May 10, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, SCARBOROUGH, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, residents of a school district, appealed a judgment from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which discharged an alternative writ of mandamus relating to the residents' contention that the consolidation of their school district with another by the New Mexico State Board of Education was illegal.


OVERVIEW: The residents complained that the effect of the consolidation was that their children would not be attending schools in the district in which the residents were entitled to vote for the school board. In affirming the judgment, the court held that this did not abridge the residents' right to vote. The court held that the right to vote was a franchise granted by the state, not a natural right. The court found nothing in N.M. Const. art. VII, §§ 1 or 3, that guaranteed the right to vote for any school board other than the one in which the elector resided, as provided by N.M. Const. art. XII, § 6. The court next held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 77-3-3(b) (Interim Supp.1970), which authorized the consolidation, was not a special law in violation of N.M. Const. art. IV, § 24. The court next held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 77-3-3(b) (Interim Supp.1970) did not violate the residents' rights of equal protection and due process secured by N.M. Const. art. II, § 18, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Lastly, the court held that because the consolidation was authorized by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 77-3-3(b) (Interim Supp.1970), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 77-3-9 through 12 (Repl. Vol. 11, pt. 1, 1968) were inapplicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that discharged the alternative writ of mandamus.

 

238 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Safeway Stores, Inc. v. City of Las Cruces


No. 9117


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


82 N.M. 499; 1971-NMSC-052; 484 P.2d 341; 1971 N.M. LEXIS 1555



April 26, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF DONA ANA COUNTY, SANDERS, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and its commissioners, appealed the judgment from the District Court of Dona Ana County (New Mexico), which, in plaintiff licensee's and corporation's suit seeking review of the denial of their application to transfer ownership of the licensee's liquor license to the corporation, held in favor of the licensee and the corporation.


OVERVIEW: The city and the commissioners denied the licensee's application to transfer ownership of the licensee's liquor license to the corporation. The licensee and the corporation sought the trial court's review. The trial court reversed the denial. The city and the commissioners appealed asserting that although the licensee and the corporation met all of the statutory prerequisites necessary to the granting of a liquor license application or transfer of such a license under the Alcoholic Beverages Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 46-1-1 to 46-12-13 (1953), the trial court erred in failing to find that the state legislature had conferred upon state municipalities the discretionary power to approve or disapprove an application for a liquor license. The court held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 46-4-8 (C), in circumstances where the local governing body failed to act for a certain period of time or approved a liquor license transfer, authorized the chief of the division to approve the transfer in his discretion, and it could not be held that the legislature intended local governing bodies to have a broader range of permitted action than the chief of the division. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the licensee and the corporation was affirmed.

 

239 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of Trs. v. Montano


No. 9020


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


82 N.M. 340; 1971-NMSC-025; 481 P.2d 702; 1971 N.M. LEXIS 1534



February 15, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SAN MIGUEL COUNTY, ANGEL, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowners appealed a judgment from the District Court of San Miguel County (New Mexico) that declared and established plaintiff landowner's right of to use and enjoy for ingress to and egress from his land an existing road that traversed the lands of defendants. At issue was the validity of N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 8-6-1 to 8-6-13 (1953). The Board of Trustees of the Town of Las Vegas was also a plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: All the roads at issue were located within the Mexican Land Grant, also known as the Las Vegas Grant. Plaintiff acquired title to his land from the Board, which was administrator of the Las Vegas Grant. An argument presented was that the legislation that made the Board administrator was special legislation that violated the Springer Act, 48 U.S.C.S. § 1471 and the N.M. Const. art. IV, § 24. The court held that the prohibitions against special legislation in the Springer Act and in the N.M. Const. art. IV, § 24, were not applicable to enactments that related to the governing or managing bodies of specific community land grants or to the manner in which these bodies used their powers of control, management, and disposition over grant lands. The court's rationale was based, inter alia, on a lengthy legislative history of enactments that related to the control or management of the land of specific grants. The court rejected the argument that there was no substantial evidence for the trial court's findings. Defendants waived any error in the trial court's denial of their motion to dismiss made at the close of the plaintiff's case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

240 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Sanchez v. City of Santa Fe


No. 9014


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


82 N.M. 322; 1971-NMSC-012; 481 P.2d 401; 1971 N.M. LEXIS 1519



January 25, 1971 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 3, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, McINTOSH, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the City of Santa Fe, appealed a declaratory judgment entered in the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which held that certain subdivision regulations complained of by plaintiffs were unlawful and in violation of the New Mexico and United States Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The City's ordinances provided that subdividers had to pay to the municipality, prior to the approval of subdivided land, the sum of $ 50 for each lot being subdivided. Sums collected were to be placed in a separate special "public facilities purchase fund" and used for the purchase or improvement of public facility sites, which sites were intended to serve the area being subdivided. Plaintiffs refused to pay the fee, contending that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The trial court agreed and granted plaintiffs' request for declaratory relief. On appeal, the court affirmed, reasoning that nn actual controversy existed under the New Mexico Declaratory Judgment Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-6-1 (1953 Comp.). Having questioned the constitutional validity of the applicable statutes, ordinances, and regulations, plaintiffs were not required to exhaust their administrative or statutory remedies. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 14-18-6 (1953 Comp.) did not specifically confer any right upon the City to exact the fee per lot and the ordinance was not drafted such that its provisions came under the general police power of the City. Thus, the fee was in the nature of an unconstitutional tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

241 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Hair v. Motto


No. 8965


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


82 N.M. 226; 1971-NMSC-001; 478 P.2d 554; 1970 N.M. LEXIS 1347



December 31, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: January 4, 1971


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SAN JUAN COUNTY, MUSGROVE, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an elector challenging certain ballots as having been illegally cast in a recent municipal election, challenged the order of the District Court of San Juan County (New Mexico) that dismissed his suit against appellees, the city mayor and the city clerk.


OVERVIEW: Following an election held for the purpose of voting on general obligation bonds for three municipal improvements, the elector filed an application for a recount, alleging that unqualified voters were permitted to cast ballots in the election. The district court concluded that the disputed votes were legal and dismissed the elector's suit. The elector appealed the dismissal of his claim. In affirming, the court concluded that a vendee in a real estate contract was a person owning property within the statutory and constitutional requirements. Further, a veteran and his wife, by virtue of claiming the soldiers' exemption to the payment of real estate tax granted by a constitutional amendment, became taxpayers and were thus qualified to vote. The soldiers' exemption amendment to the state constitution was the payment of that portion of a veteran's property tax by the state; by claiming the exemption, the veteran consented to payment of his taxes by the state. Neither the state constitution nor the statutory law required that payment of property taxes be made personally in order to qualify one eligible to vote.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

242 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Witt v. Hartman


No. 8991


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


82 N.M. 170; 1970-NMSC-147; 477 P.2d 608; 1970 N.M. LEXIS 1463



December 7, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, MACPHERSON, JR., Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a Special Assistant Attorney General, challenged an order of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which quashed an alternative writ of mandamus directing appellee, the Director of the Department of Finance, to approve a reimbursement voucher to pay for appellant's out-of-state travel. Appellant contended that appellee had a clear ministerial duty to approve the voucher under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 11-1-9(E).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was granted an alternative writ of mandamus which ordered appellee to approve a reimbursement voucher to pay for appellant's out-of-state travel. Subsequently, the trial court quashed the writ, and appellant challenged the ruling. Appellant contended that appellee had a clear ministerial duty, involving no discretion, to approve the voucher under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 11-1-9(E). Appellant argued that, because the statute stated that "public funds shall not be expended to reimburse public officers without written authorization from the governor or his designee," the legislature meant that where funds were budgeted and appropriated for a legitimate purpose, the governor's designee had a clear and undisputed statutory duty to approve the voucher. On review, the court held that, pursuant to the statute, appellee was authorized to adopt rules and regulations for exception from gubernatorial authorization. The court found no legislative intent that appellee was required to approve all state vouchers merely because appropriated funds were available.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.
