Bd. of Educ. v. Maloney


No. 9160


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


82 N.M. 167; 1970-NMSC-146; 477 P.2d 605; 1970 N.M. LEXIS 1464



December 7, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL MANDAMUS PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: Order accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted a preliminary writ of mandamus, upon the petition of relator school board, directing respondent attorney general to approve a bond transcript submitted by the board or to respond to the writ. The attorney general responded to the writ.


OVERVIEW: The attorney general refused to issue a bond transcript submitted by the school board after an election because the board did not maintain separate ballot boxes for voters, separating real estate owners from non-owners as mandated by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 11-6-38 (1953 Comp., 1970 Supp.). The purpose for maintaining the separate boxes was that under N.M. Const. art. IX, § 11, a majority vote of real estate owners was required for a general obligation bond. The court made the writ permanent, holding that both N.M. Const. art. IX, § 11, and N.M. Stat. Ann. § 11-6-38 (1953 Comp., 1970 Supp.) were unconstitutional as violative of the Equal Protection Clause of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court based its decision on several rulings from the United States Supreme Court construing similar provisions in other states as well as New Mexico. The court also adopted the reasoning of the Supreme Court and only made its decision retroactive to elections pending subsequent to June 23, 1970.


OUTCOME: The preliminary writ was made permanent.

 

244 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Maloney v. Sierra


No. 8964


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


82 N.M. 125; 1970-NMSC-144; 477 P.2d 301; 1970 N.M. LEXIS 1460



November 23, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, MONTOYA, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state, through the attorney general, sought review of a judgment in favor of defendant director of the department of alcoholic and beverage control on a counterclaim asserted against a declaratory action to enjoin the enforcement of 1969 N.M. Laws ch. 216, § 1, in the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico).


OVERVIEW: The state, by the attorney general, appealed a judgment in favor of the director of the state department of alcoholic and beverage control on a counterclaim asserted in response to the attorney general's declaratory action. The attorney general urged that the liquor law statute at issue permitted the sale and consumption of alcohol by the drink on the premises of licensed dispensers on Sundays. The director contended that the lower court correctly found that the uncodified law, 1969 N.M. Laws ch. 216, § 1 precluded the sale by drink during Sundays, permitting only the service and consumption in accordance with a proposed regulation. The court dispensed with the argument that an actual controversy was lacking, finding that the situation concerned an administrative stalemate between two public officers when the attorney general was charged with administering the laws while the director was charged with enforcing liquor laws. The court found that under the plain and proper construction of the legislature's purposeful omission of the word sell in the applicable clause, the sale and consumption of liquor by the drink on licensed premises was not permitted on Sundays.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which declared that the liquor law challenged by the state was properly enforced by the director of the department of alcoholic and beverage control as a ban on the sale of alcoholic beverages on Sundays on licensed premises.

Hobbs v. State


No. 8953


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


82 N.M. 102; 1970-NMSC-133; 476 P.2d 500; 1970 N.M. LEXIS 1454; 2 ERC (BNA) 1046



November 2, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, SCARBOROUGH, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment proceeding filed by plaintiff protesters, defendants, a state engineer and a city, appealed a judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which declared that the state engineer lacked jurisdiction to adjudicate applications to appropriate underground water.


OVERVIEW: The city and a water company entered into a contract wherein the water company agreed to obtain permits to appropriate underground water for the city. 1967 N.M. Laws ch. 308, § 2, amended N.M. Stat. Ann. § 75-11-3 (1953) and permitted the removal of a proceeding for application for use of underground water from the state engineer's jurisdiction and placed it within the original jurisdiction of the courts. The trial court held that the state engineer had no jurisdiction to adjudicate the applications. The court reversed, holding that 1967 N.M. Laws ch. 308, § 2 was unconstitutional as violative of the separation of powers doctrine of N.M. Const. art. III, § 1. The court declined to rule on defendants' contentions that the trial court erred in finding that the city's contract with the water company violated the Bateman Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 11-6-6 (1953), and that it erred by finding that the city was not the real party in interest in the applications before the state engineer because the parties' rights had not been fixed by proper administrative proceedings and thus, any determination as to any impairment of the protesters' rights was speculative.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and dismissed the protesters' case.

State Racing Comm'n v. McManus


No. 9091


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


82 N.M. 108; 1970-NMSC-134; 476 P.2d 767; 1970 N.M. LEXIS 1456



November 2, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROHIBITION PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ of prohibition made permanent and district judge's temporary restraining order declared void.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, state racing commission and board of racing stewards, appealed a decision from respondents, the district judge and the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which issued an ex parte temporary restraining order enjoining petitioners from enforcing a suspension of respondent jockey. The court issued an alternative writ of prohibition, and before the court was the question of whether to make the same permanent.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners issued an order suspending the jockey for seven days for careless riding, and the jockey then filed a petition seeking a temporary restraining order to enjoin the suspension. The district court granted the jockey's petition and petitioners sought an alternative writ of prohibition to stay the district court from enforcing its restraining order. Petitioners asserted lack of jurisdiction and that district court erred in enjoining its action. The court made permanent the alternative writ of prohibition and declared the district court's restraining order null and void, holding that the district court erred in staying the suspension because there was no showing of bad faith or abuse of discretion on the part of the racing board of stewards or the commission, and that due process did not required that a hearing be held prior to the suspension of state licensed individuals. The court also concluded that the district court lacked jurisdiction to determine the matter because the jockey failed to exhaust his administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court determined that its alternative writ of prohibition should be made permanent in petitioners' action to have respondents' ex parte temporary restraining order invalid.

Bureau of Revenue v. Dale J. Bellamah Corp.


No. 9028


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


82 N.M. 13; 1970-NMSC-107; 474 P.2d 499; 1970 N.M. LEXIS 1440; 36 Oil & Gas Rep. 710



August 3, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 29, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, MONTOYA, District Judge



DISPOSITION: Cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Bureau of Revenue of the State of New Mexico sought review of a summary judgment from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), rendered in favor of appellee corporation in the Bureau's suit to recover tax assessments due under the Emergency School Tax Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 72-16-1 - 72-16-47 (1953), on gross receipts from management and engineering services and from equipment rental.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the corporation's motion for summary judgment on the ground that the action was barred by the applicable statute of limitations, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-21-25. The Bureau contended that § 72-21-25 was in conflict with N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16 because the subject of matter N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-21-25 was insufficiently expressed in the title to the House Bill in which it was incorporated to meet constitutional requirements. The court reversed the judgment, finding that § 72-21-25 was void. The court did not find that the natural reaction to a reading of the entire title to House Bill would be that a limitation on the collection of the privilege tax on businesses other than oil and gas producers would be included in the body of the House Bill. The court found that the title did not alert readers to the limitation since neither the title nor the body of the House Bill provided for any such limitation on the collection of the enumerated privilege taxes. Because § 72-21-25's limitation provision was not germane to either the general subject of House Bill or the express wording of its title, the court concluded that the attempt to include the provision was improper.


OUTCOME: The court held that the statute of limitations relied upon for granting summary judgment was void and remanded the action to the trial court to reinstate the cause.

 

248 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Southern Union Gas Co. v. City of Artesia


No. 8906


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


81 N.M. 654; 1970-NMSC-086; 472 P.2d 368; 1970 N.M. LEXIS 1422



June 8, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 30, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF EDDY COUNTY, NEAL, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff utility appealed a decision of the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico), which held that it was not entitled to reimbursement of expenses resulting from the forced removal and relocation of its utility lines, in an action it brought against defendants, agency and city, seeking to recover those expenses.


OVERVIEW: The utility was a private corporation that operated a gas distribution system in the city pursuant to a franchise agreement. An urban renewal project that was mostly funded by the United States Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD) forced the utility to remove and partially relocate certain of its utility lines from streets and alleys in the area covered by the project. HUD regulations prohibited compensation to private utilities for removal and relocation expenses, so the city was compensated for its removal costs but the utility was not. It brought an action against the agency and the city seeking to recover its costs. The trial court entered judgment against the utility and it appealed, arguing, inter alia, that it was entitled to compensation because the requirement to remove its lines constituted a complete ouster and was therefore a taking of property without due process of law. The court affirmed, holding that the removal and partial relocation of the utility's lines at its own expense was a condition of its franchise, was required by the valid exercise of defendants' police power, and did not constitute an ouster which would entitle the utility to compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision that the utility was not entitled to compensation for expenses in the removal and partial relocation of some its utility lines in an area covered by an urban renewal project after it was required to do so by the city but was refused reimbursement for the expenses by the agency.

 

249 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Fellows v. Shultz


No. 8804


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


81 N.M. 496; 1970-NMSC-071; 469 P.2d 141; 1970 N.M. LEXIS 1412



May 4, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF EDDY COUNTY, NEAL, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment void and case dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, protesters and a state engineer, sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico), which entered judgment in favor of appellee applicants on their petition to change the location of a water well pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 75-11-7 (1953).


OVERVIEW: When some applicants sought to change the location of a water well by applying to the state engineer pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 75-11-7 (1953), the protesters contested the application. The trial court approved the application. The court dismissed the case, holding that the trial court's judgment was void because the amendments to § 75-11-7 that allowed de novo review of such an application by the district court violated N.M. Const. art. III, § 1, the separation of powers clause. The statute assigned an administrative function to the district court; it did not just review the state engineer's decision, it made the decision de novo. Neither did the adoption of N.M. Const. art. XVI, § 5 make N.M. Stat. Ann. § 75-11-7 (1953) constitutional. Although that constitutional provision allowed the type of de novo district court action done in the case at bar, it had not been passed until the amendments to § 75-11-7 had been enacted. Since N.M. Const. art. XVI, § 5 was not made explicitly retroactive, nor did it explicitly ratify N.M. Stat. Ann. § 75-11-7 (1953), it could not make the statute constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the case and held that the trial court's judgment in favor of the applicants was void.

Kaiser Steel Corp. v. W. S. Ranch Co.


No. 8842


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


81 N.M. 414; 1970-NMSC-043; 467 P.2d 986; 1970 N.M. LEXIS 1384; 1 ERC (BNA) 1188



March 16, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 29, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COLFAX COUNTY, McINTOSH, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ranch owner challenged of an order of the District Court of Colfax County (New Mexico), which held that plaintiff coal mine owner was entitled to enter upon the land of the ranch to bring water to the coal mine without seeking permission of the ranch by the undertaking a condemnation under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 75-1-3. The trial court also held that the ranch could only recover against the coal mine owner in an adverse condemnation action.


OVERVIEW: A coal mine owner operated a coal mine, and sought to make water available to the mine. In order to do so, the coal mine owner had to intrude upon the land of a ranch, and either drill for water or transverse upon the land with a pipeline. The coal mine sought to do so without seeking permission of the ranch pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 75-1-3 (1953) and commenced suit for a declaration of rights. The trial court granted summary judgment to the coal mine owner, and held that the coal mine owner had the power under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 75-1-3 (1953) to use the ranch's lands, and that the exclusive remedy of the ranch was that of "inverse condemnation," as provided by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-9-22 (1953). On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held: (1) the use of water by the coal mine owners was a public use; (2) it was permissible to take the land of the ranch to convey water; (3) the act permitting condemnation for rights of way of water was not vulnerable to attack, because it was in the public interest to distribute water; and (4) the coal mine owner was only liable for damages to the ranch in an inverse condemnation action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that held that the coal mine owner was entitled to enter upon the land and lay a pipeline from the river across the lands of the ranch without seeking permission of the ranch by the undertaking of a condemnation action, and the ranch was permitted to recover against the coal mine owner only in an inverse condemnation action.

 

251 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Turnbow


No. 8850


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


81 N.M. 254; 1970-NMSC-033; 466 P.2d 100; 1970 N.M. LEXIS 1378



March 9, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SAN JUAN COUNTY, ZINN, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of San Juan County (New Mexico), which denied his petition under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 21-1-1(93) (Supp. 1969). Defendant had pleaded guilty to second-degree murder and was sentenced to imprisonment of not less than three years nor more than life.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he should have been sentenced to a fixed, determined number of years. The court disagreed, holding that the trial court's sentence was the proper imposition of both a minimum and maximum penalty as prescribed by law. At the time of the offense, the applicable statutory penalty for second-degree murder was imprisonment for any period of time not less than three years. In prescribing a minimum penalty, but not a maximum penalty, the legislature by implication authorized a penalty in excess of the minimum. Because a maximum penalty was authorized by implication, there was no unconstitutional delegation of legislative power.


OUTCOME: The court denied the order denying relief.

Speer v. Sierra County Comm'rs


No. 8827


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


80 N.M. 741; 1969-NMSC-154; 461 P.2d 156; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1701



November 10, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SIERRA COUNTY, BURKS, Judge



DISPOSITION: Cause reversed and remanded with direction to set aside and vacate judgment and to dismiss intervention.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator bondholder appealed the judgment from the District Court of Sierra County (New Mexico), which, in the bondholder's mandamus action against respondents commissioners, withdrew, upon intervenor property owner's motion, a mandamus and ordered the commissioners to remove a levy from the tax rolls.


OVERVIEW: The bondholder petitioned for mandamus to compel the commissioners to levy a tax of mills alleged to be necessary to pay the principal and interest on the district's bonds. The trial court ordered a peremptory writ of mandamus. The commissioners levied the tax without the actual issuance and service of the writ. Thereafter, the property owner moved to intervene. The trial court allowed the property owner to intervene and he then moved for an order to set aside the previous judgment and to dismiss the bondholder's petition asserting that the bond issue was invalid because no valid bond election had ever been held. The trial court withdrew the writ of mandamus and ordered the county officials to remove the levy from the tax rolls. The bondholder appealed asserting that the order permitting the intervention was improper and untimely. The court agreed as, when the intervention order was entered, there was no controversy existing between the bondholder and the commissioners. The controversy was ended after the order of the court was followed by the action of the commissioners in making the levy.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the property owner was reversed and the judgment was remanded with direction to set aside and vacate judgment and to dismiss the intervention.

 

253 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Overton v. N.M. State Tax Comm'n


No. 8793


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


81 N.M. 28; 1969-NMSC-140; 462 P.2d 613; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1689



October 20, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 9, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, SWOPE, Judge



DISPOSITION: Remanded for dismissal of action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, tax assessor and tax association, sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which held in favor of respondents, tax commission and veterans, that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-1-11 was constitutional. Respondents also sought review of a judgment stating that although § 72-1-13 was unconstitutional, it was a severable provision from an otherwise constitutional statute.


OVERVIEW: The state brought an action for the assessor against the commission, questioning the constitutionality of § 72-1-13. The trial court entered a two-part judgment, and both parties sought review of the decision. On appeal, the court remanded the case to the trial court for dismissal. The court held that appellants had no standing to bring the cause of action. The court found that there was no allegation or finding that the assessor would be injured or jeopardized by the questioned laws. In addition, the court stated that although the tax association was an association comprised of veteran taxpayers, none of the members alleged any injuries or jeopardized rights. The court found that the members were not similarly situated within the meaning of § 21-1-1(23), as adequate representation on behalf of those entitled to the exemption would have conflicted with the interests of those who were not. The court therefore found that appellants could not allege by amendments to their complaints the "personal stake" required, and there was no actual controversy within the meaning of § 22-6-1. Thus, the court stated that it was not necessary to determine the matters raised by the cross-appeal.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for a dismissal of the action.

 

254 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Cutter Flying Serv. v. Straughan Chevrolet, Inc.


No. 8704


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


80 N.M. 646; 1969-NMSC-132; 459 P.2d 350; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1683



October 10, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REHEARING



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant airplane owner sought review of a decision of the District Court (New Mexico), which awarded appellee airplane repair service damages and attorney fees in a suit seeking to compel payment for work performed on an airplane.


OVERVIEW: The airplane owner left his airplane with the airplane repair service to have a nose strut repaired. The airplane owner testified that he requested that an annual inspection be performed, but not any actual repairs performed until he was advised of the repairs needed. The airplane service went ahead and performed the inspection and completed the repairs it determined were required. After payment was not forthcoming, the airplane service filed suit seeking to compel payment. The trial court awarded the airplane service damages for the inspection work and related repairs, but not the nose repair because it was not properly done, along with attorney fees. The airplane owner sought review contending that it did not authorize the inspection repairs and challenged the attorney fee award. The court affirmed holding that there was substantial evidence to support to support the trial judge's decision as to liability to pay for the repairs. Pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 18-1-37 the prevailing party in an action to recover on an open account could be allowed a reasonable attorney fee set by the court. It was constitutional to apply the attorney fee statute retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of damages and attorney fees to the airplane service in the suit seeking to compel payment for work performed on an airplane.

 

255 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Barber's Super Mkts., Inc. v. City of Grants


No. 8762


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


80 N.M. 533; 1969-NMSC-115; 458 P.2d 785; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1671



September 15, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF VALENCIA COUNTY, LARRAZOLO, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, and cause remanded with instructions to dismiss complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision of the District Court of Valencia County (New Mexico), which entered a judgment requiring the city to issue appellee supermarket a permit for the installation and use of an incinerator in a declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The city passed an ordinance that granted a contractor an exclusive franchise to collect, remove, and dispose of garbage from locations within the city's corporate limits. The supermarket generated large quantities of combustible waste material, such as empty packing cartons and cases, paper, packing material, trash, and other refuse. The supermarket applied to the city for a building permit to allow the installation of an incinerator upon its premises. The city denied the permit based on the ordinance. The supermarket filed a declaratory action against the city. The trial court entered a judgment requiring the city to issue a permit finding that a competitor of the supermarket was allowed to build an incinerator and that the ordinance was unreasonable, arbitrary, and capricious. The court reversed and remanded holding that a city was the sole judge as to what was best for the public health and safety of its inhabitants, unless the decision was so arbitrary and unreasonable as to be equivalent to fraud. If part of the ordinance was unconstitutional if could be declared void, however, the entire ordinance was not to be declared invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment requiring the city to issue the supermarket a permit for the installation and use of an incinerator in the declaratory action.

 

256 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Michael J. Maloof & Co. v. Bureau of Revenue


No. 8750


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


80 N.M. 485; 1969-NMSC-100; 458 P.2d 89; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1657



August 11, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, MONTOYA, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed a judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which denied their claim for a refund from defendant Bureau of Revenue for taxes they paid on the gross receipts of their sales of alcoholic beverages pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16-4.4 (1953) (repealed).


OVERVIEW: N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16-4.4 (1953) (repealed) was amended by 1963 N.M. Laws ch. 325, § 13 to require a tax of one-half of one percent upon the gross receipts of alcoholic liquors and beverages. The taxpayers were licensed wholesalers of liquor. They paid, under protest, the tax required by 1963 N.M. Laws ch. 325, § 13. They contended that the amendment to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16-4.4 (1953) (repealed) violated their rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and N.M. Const. art. II, § 18 because it made a discriminatory, arbitrary, and unreasonable distinction between wholesalers in the liquor business and wholesalers of other commodities. The court held that unless the classification in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16-4.4 (1953) (repealed) was arbitrary, capricious, or void for uncertainty, it could not substitute its views in selecting and classifying taxpayers for those of the legislature. It further held that the taxpayers were in a different class from wholesalers of other commodities and that the legislature's motives for amendment of § 72-16-4.4 were founded upon pertinent and real differences between liquor wholesalers and other wholesalers in order to achieve permissible ends.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Garcia


No. 8742


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


80 N.M. 466; 1969-NMSC-097; 457 P.2d 985; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1651



August 4, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF QUAY COUNTY, GALLEGOS, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded for sentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the District Court of Quay County (New Mexico), which convicted him for murder in the first degree and sentenced him to be executed. Defendant argued error in unconstitutionally dismissing prospective jurors and contended improper questioning by the district attorney. Defendant also argued that N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 40A-29-2 and 40A-29-2 were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the prospective jurors were unconstitutionally dismissed because they expressed general objections to the death penalty on conscientious and religious grounds, improper questioning by the district attorney upon cross examination of defendant brought about by statements which created prejudice in the minds of the jury against defendant, and the statute imposing the death penalty and death sentence were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court stated that a statute had become effective a few months before had abolished death penalty for murder. With respect to the district attorney's questioning, the court stated that it was not improper because defendant made voluntary statements, even after being repeatedly stopped by the court and also after he had been dismissed as a witness. The court, noting that defendant had been admonished not to volunteer statements, but he continued to do so, stated that voluntary statements could not be a basis for reversal. The court, finding no error, stated that defendant was competent to intelligently assist counsel in his own defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision but remanded for resentence of defendant.

State v. Sanchez

259 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Springer Corp. v. Welch (In re Estate of Welch)


No. 8809


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


80 N.M. 448; 1969-NMSC-093; 457 P.2d 380; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1649



July 28, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF ROOSEVELT COUNTY, BLYTHE, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation filed a proof of claim against decedent's estate. The motions of appellee administratrix and heirs to dismiss the claim was granted by the District Court of Roosevelt County (New Mexico) for failure to comply with N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 31-8-2, 31-8-3 (1953) in that a notice of hearing was not timely served on the administratrix. The corporation's appeal challenged the constitutionality of the statutory notice provisions.


OVERVIEW: The corporation apparently concedes there was support for the trial court's ruling on the motions to dismiss the claim. It was contended, however, that N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 31-8-2 and 31-8-3 (1953), were unconstitutional because the notice of hearing requirement was not clearly expressed in the title to the statutes. It was not necessary that the title to a legislative enactment be an index of everything in the act itself; the title only had to give notice of the subject matter of the legislation. The title was sufficient if, by application of every reasonable intendment in favor of its validity, it may be said that the subject of the legislative enactment was expressed in its title. In the court's view, the challenged legislation did not offend N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16. The two statutes were in pari materia and had to be read together. There were two mandatory steps the corporation had to take for the claim to be allowed: (a) filing a claim; and (b) notice of hearing thereon. Both requirements had to be met; otherwise, the claim was barred. The corporation failed the requirement of notice of hearing. The trial court's judgment was not disturbed.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.

 

260 of 795 DOCUMENTS


McKinley v. Alamogordo Mun. Sch. Dist. Auth.


No. 8723


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


81 N.M. 196; 1969-NMSC-086; 465 P.2d 79; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1641



July 14, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 25, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OTERO COUNTY, TRIVIZ, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a municipal school district authority, a municipal school district, and the New Mexico State Board of Education, sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Otero County (New Mexico), which permanently restrained the authority from proceeding with a plan to finance construction of a facility for school purposes pursuant to the provisions of the School Leasing Law, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 77-17-1 to 77-17-14 (1953).


OVERVIEW: The authority was a nonprofit corporation. The district court determined that the plan authorized by the School Leasing Law and followed by the authority permitted the creation of a debt in excess of the limits permitted by N.M. Const. art. IX, § 11. The district court further ruled that the plan provided for lease payments which constituted a debt and that no provision for a special fund or for revenue to pay the same was made, except out of state appropriation. In addition, the district court held that the plan as contemplated and authorized the School Leasing Law by would have permitted the levying of ad valorem taxes to make lease payments and would have constituted a debt prohibited by art. IX, § 11. Appellants sought review. On appeal, the court upheld the judgment. The court concluded that the authority was clearly nothing more nor less than the school district acting through a public entity other than its regularly designated Board. The court further found that the procedure authorized by the School Leasing Law was simply an effort by indirection to avoid the provisions of art. IX, § 11, when it could not have been done directly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

261 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clark


No. 8792


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


80 N.M. 340; 1969-NMSC-078; 455 P.2d 844; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1635



June 16, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF CERTIORARI



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from an order of the Court of Appeals (New Mexico), which affirmed his conviction of kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the crime of kidnapping in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-4-1 (1953) and the appellate court affirmed his conviction. On appeal, the court found that § 40A-4-1 required an intent to confine against the victim's will when he was taken, restrained, or confined with intent that he be held for ransom, or as a hostage, but it was not necessary the he be confined against his will when the purpose of the taking, restraining, or confining was that the victim be held to service against his will. The court determined that the record in the case failed to demonstrate that defendant intended to hold his victim for ransom or as a hostage, or to service against her will. There was no way under the proof elicited to conclude what was intended except through assumption or speculation and the court reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order from the trial court.

Amador v. N.M. State Bd. of Educ.


No. 8754


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


80 N.M. 336; 1969-NMSC-076; 455 P.2d 840; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1632



June 16, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, SCARBOROUGH, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the New Mexico State Board of Education, challenged a judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which granted to appellee, a teacher and elected member of the Board (Board member), an injunction restraining and enjoining the Board from enforcing its resolution, which required the suspension of the teaching certificate of a teacher elected to the Board, and from suspending the Board member's teaching certificate.


OVERVIEW: The Board member was a certified teacher and was elected a member of the Board, which previously had adopted a resolution requiring the suspension of the teaching certificate of a teacher elected to the Board. Upon being served with an order to show cause why his teaching certificate should not be suspended, the Board member sought and was granted an injunction restraining and enjoining the Board from enforcing its resolution or suspending his teaching certificate. The Board appealed, but the court affirmed the district court's judgment. Although the Board relied upon N.M. Stat. Ann. § 77-8-19(A) (1953) for its authority to suspend the Board member's teaching certificate, an examination of the Act requiring the licensing of school teachers convinced the court that its purpose is to protect the public against incompetent teachers and to insure proper educational qualifications, personal fitness, and a high standard of teaching performance. The suspension of a teacher for incompatibility with membership on the Board did not fall within the purpose of insuring a high quality of public instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State ex rel. State Highway Comm'n v. Chavez


No. 8684


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


80 N.M. 394; 1969-NMSC-072; 456 P.2d 868; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1628



June 9, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TORRANCE COUNTY, BURKS, Judge On Rehearing



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant New Mexico State Highway Commission sought review of a judgment from District Court of Torrance County (New Mexico), which in a condemnation action awarded appellee lessee damages. The basic issue on appeal were whether the jury verdict was supported by substantial evidence or was so excessive as to require a reversal or remittitur. The Commission contended that the award was shockingly excessive.


OVERVIEW: The lessee was in possession of the land in question pursuant to a so-called "business lease," which had been originally issued in 1938 and thereafter renewed each five years. The lessee had purchased the lease in 1948 and had renewed the lease at least once. He had added a considerable amount of improvements and operated the property as a store, service station, curio shop, bar, and two rental rooms. The court stated that, while the award was higher than it would have found if it were the trier of the facts, it could not hold as a matter of law that the award should have been reversed. The Commission asserted error in the trial court's refusal to submit interrogatories to the jury to make it possible to determine what amount of damages was ascribed to each element considered. The court stated that it was not necessary to consider each requested interrogatory in order to arrive at a conclusion concerning the correctness of the ruling. The trial court had reasonable discretion in the matter of what questions should have been submitted to the jury for special findings and, unless that discretion was abused, it would not be disturbed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Sanchez v. Bd. of Educ.

SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teacher sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Valencia County (New Mexico), which awarded him damages in the amount of three years' salary for wrongful termination in his action against appellee town board of education.


OVERVIEW: The tenured teacher was discharged by the board. The discharge reverted back four years. The teacher appealed to the State board, which reversed the discharge. The teacher brought an action against the board to recover damages of his unpaid salary for seven years, starting with the year of discharge. The trial court awarded the teacher damages for three school years because it held that the teacher's cause of action arose on the date of the State board of education's decision. The teacher appealed. The court held that the teacher's acceptance of the State board's decision created a new contract with the board. The court rejected the board's argument that an award of damages was barred by N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 5-4-5 (1966) or 40A-23-2 (1964). The court held that damages were an exception. The teacher was entitled to salary for seven years, plus interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the action for further proceedings.

Langdon v. Jaramillo


No. 8768


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


80 N.M. 255; 1969-NMSC-060; 454 P.2d 269; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1621



May 12, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, REIDY, Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county clerk sought review of an order of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico) requiring the county clerk to accept the affidavits of voter registration of appellee voters, in the voters' action against the county clerk to compel the acceptance of the affidavits. The county clerk refused to register the voters pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-1-1 (1953).


OVERVIEW: The voters resided on an United States military base located in New Mexico. In refusing to register the voters, the county clerk found that the voters resided within an area under the exclusive jurisdiction of the United States and that § 3-1-1 would not have permitted voter registration under the circumstances. The trial court ordered registration based upon its finding that both the United States and New Mexico had jurisdiction over the land where the voters resided. The court ruled that reversal of the trial court's order was necessary because it erred in concluding that New Mexico had concurrent jurisdiction over the federal military base. The court noted that the United States acquired the property for the base from New Mexico pursuant to U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 17, which afforded the United States exclusive jurisdiction over the land. Moreover, the court found no legislative action by the United States Congress that would have conferred concurrent state jurisdiction over this federal enclave.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order compelling the county clerk to register the voters, and remanded the matter to the trial court.

267 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Barela v. N.M. State Bd. of Educ.


No. 8764


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


80 N.M. 220; 1969-NMSC-038; 453 P.2d 583; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1618



March 31, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 28, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON REHEARING



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of New Mexico, acting on behalf of appellants, property owners in a school district, challenged a judgment of the trial court (New Mexico) that denied their petition for an order of mandamus to dissolve a school district consolidation and that dismissed their action seeking the order against appellees, the New Mexico State Board of Education, the New Mexico State Superintendent of Public Instruction, and two school districts.


OVERVIEW: The State Board ordered the disputed consolidation after the board of the district in which the owners resided and the board of a district in another county passed consolidation resolutions. The owners contended that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 73-20-3 (Repealed 1967) did not authorize inter-county consolidations. The court reversed the trial court judgment, holding that the attempted consolidation was a nullity. Language in the first paragraph of § 73-20-3 limited consolidation to "two or more rural school districts within the county," and the court disagreed with appellees' argument that language in the second paragraph, added in 1955, removed the limitation. Had the legislature intended to amend the statute to allow consolidation between districts in different counties, the court held that it would have done so unambiguously. Appellees did not proceed under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 73-20-5 (Repealed 1967), which did allow inter-county consolidations. Because the districts were operating as if consolidated at the time of its decision, the court directed that the order was not to be made effective until July 1, 1969, provided that in the interim a consolidation had not been properly effected.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the action to the trial court for further proceedings. It directed that the trial court order to be entered pursuant to its mandate was to be made effective July 1, 1969, provided that in the interim a consolidation in conformity with law had not been effectuated.

Midwest Video v. Campbell


No. 8671


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


80 N.M. 116; 1969-NMSC-034; 452 P.2d 185; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1594



March 24, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, MONTOYA, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Governor, Attorney General, and an Assistant Attorney General of New Mexico, appealed from a judgment from the District Court of Santa Fe (New Mexico), which held that plaintiffs, the operators of a community antenna television system (CATV) in New Mexico, were not engaged in "price advertising" within the meaning of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 67-7-13(m).


OVERVIEW: The operators' CATV system received television signals from Texas stations and circulated them by cable to their New Mexico subscribers. Those stations broadcast price advertisements of Texas optical firms. Such advertising was prohibited in New Mexico by § 67-7-13(m) but was not prohibited under Texas law. The district court enjoined enforcement of § 67-7-13(m) against the operators, finding that they were not "advertising" and that § 67-7-13(m), as applied to the operators, violated N.M. Const. art. II, § 18. On appeal, the court affirmed without reaching the constitutional issue. The court noted that the operators did not sell advertising space or receive compensation from either the broadcasters or their advertisers but simply carried the signals to additional viewers. The exposure of the price advertising to the subscribers was only incidental to an otherwise lawful activity and did not amount to "advertising" by the operators.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

 

269 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thomson


No. 8564


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


79 N.M. 748; 1969-NMSC-006; 449 P.2d 656; 1969 N.M. LEXIS 1570



January 20, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, WOOD, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant claimants appealed the decision of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which quieted title in land that they claimed to own in plaintiff State.


OVERVIEW: The tract at issue was sold to the State for taxes unpaid by the original owner. Later, the original owner conveyed the property by quitclaim deed to the claimants. The claimants made application to repurchase the tract from the tax commission and received a deed upon the showing that they had paid certain taxes. The trial court held that the original owner's title was extinguished by de facto condemnation, that the original owner's quitclaim deed conveyed no title, and that the tax sale and the deed to the claimants had no effect on the State's title to the property. The trial court held that the State had absolute fee simple title, which was transferred to the penitentiary. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that because the penitentiary statute was a special act, it prevailed over the general tax statute. The court held that the State did not take property without due process of law because the original owner failed to timely redeem, and the right to repurchase did not come into existence. The court held that, thus, the claimants acquired no valid interest upon which any redemption could operate to justify the issuance of a proper deed from the tax commission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's holding that the State had absolute fee simple title in the tract at issue.

 

270 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Thompson v. Legislative Audit Comm'n


No. 8717


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


79 N.M. 693; 1968-NMSC-184; 448 P.2d 799; 1968 N.M. LEXIS 2029



November 25, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 7, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL MANDAMUS PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ of mandamus made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state auditor filed an original mandamus proceeding that challenged the validity of 1965 N.M. Laws ch. 287 (N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 4-24-1 to 4-24-25 (1953). The state auditor claimed that the statute was unconstitutional because it removed substantially all powers and duties of a constitutionally established office.


OVERVIEW: In an original mandamus proceeding, the state auditor challenged a statute that provided for a transfer from the state auditor to the legislative audit commission of all equipment, supplies, records, and any other property or thing held by him in his official capacity; and after a certain date to reduce the salary of the state auditor to $ 1.00 per year. The auditor would have retained only some minor duties. The New Mexico Constitution designated the executive officers of the State, and specifically included the state auditor; however, it was silent with respect to any duties of that office. The court held that the legislature could not by statute abolish a constitutional office nor deprive the office of a single prescribed constitutional duty. Nor could the legislature abolish the office indirectly, by removing all statutory duties, thereby leaving the office in name only, an empty shell. The court noted that a earlier effort to amend the constitution to abolish the office of state auditor had failed. The court found that the duties removed were implicit in the office of state auditor and declared the statute to be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court declared the entire statute unconstitutional and the alternative writ of mandamus was made permanent.

 

271 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sisneros


No. 8619


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


79 N.M. 600; 1968-NMSC-175; 446 P.2d 875; 1968 N.M. LEXIS 2022



November 8, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, McMANUS, JR., Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 21-1-1(93) (Supp. 1967).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a juvenile, confessed to the murder of a schoolmate. Prior to his confession, defendant was warned of his right to obtain counsel and to refrain from making any statements. Defendant's parents were in an adjoining room. Thereafter, defendant was convicted of murder in the second degree. In a subsequent proceeding, the court quashed defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Defendant filed a motion for post-conviction relief under § 21-1-1(93). The district court denied defendant's motion. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that defendant's confession was voluntary because the evidence demonstrated that defendant had sufficient mental capacity at the time of his confession to be conscious of what he was doing, to retain memory of his actions, and to relate with reasonable accuracy the details of his actions. Further, any error that the district court might have made over proper objection did not invoke the doctrine of fundamental error because it could not seriously be suggested defendant's innocence appeared indisputable. Finally, the voluntariness of defendant's confession was not dependent on a verbatim transcript of warnings given to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying defendant's motion for post-conviction relief.

 

272 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Chavez v. Evans


No. 8746


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


79 N.M. 578; 1968-NMSC-167; 446 P.2d 445; 1968 N.M. LEXIS 2012; 39 A.L.R.3d 290



October 25, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL MANDAMUS PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: No motion for reharing will be entertained.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidates filed a writ of mandamus seeking to require respondent secretary of state to certify their names to the various county clerks for the offices to which they were nominated by the People's Constitutional Party.


OVERVIEW: The eight candidates sought a writ of mandamus to require the secretary of state to certify their names to the various county clerks for the offices to which they were nominated by their political party. The court determined that five of the eight candidates were qualified for the offices that they were seeking and that the writ should issued. The court further determined that three of the candidates were not qualified for the positions they were seeking and that the writ should be quashed with respect to them. The court directed the secretary of state to forthwith certify for the political party, to the various county clerks, the president and vice-president candidates, two congressional candidates, and the board of education candidate. The candidate for governor was not certified because he had been convicted of a felony and therefore the candidate for lieutenant-governor was not certified as the positions were elected jointly by casting a single vote. The candidate for the district attorney was denied certification because he was not learned in the law as required by the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The court made the writ of mandamus permanent as to five of the eight candidates. The court quashed the writ with respect to three of the candidates.

 

273 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Cortez v. Martinez


No. 8572


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


79 N.M. 506; 1968-NMSC-153; 445 P.2d 383; 1968 N.M. LEXIS 1999



September 23, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TAOS COUNTY, McINTOSH, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administratrix appealed a judgment from the District Court of Taos County (New Mexico), which granted the motion for summary judgment of defendants, a driver and a father, in the administratrix's wrongful death action. The district court found that the father was protected by the guest statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 64-24-1.


OVERVIEW: In a wrongful death action, an administratrix sought damages for the negligent operation of a car by a driver, which resulted in the death of her decedent. She also claimed that the driver's father was the owner of the car, which was being used for family purposes at the time of the accident. The trial court granted the motion for summary judgment of the driver and the father, finding that the car was owned by the driver and he was protected by the guest statute under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 64-24-1. The court affirmed the judgment of dismissal against the father. The court reversed the judgment against the driver. The court held that it was error for the trial court to disregard the certificate of title. The court ruled that summary judgment should not have been granted because there was an issue of fact on the question of ownership. The case was remanded with instructions to grant a trial against the driver. The court concluded that there was no claim of gross negligence or wilful misconduct as to the driver. Therefore, his liability being predicated solely on the family purpose doctrine, the administratrix was not entitled to recovery from him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the judgment against the father. The court reversed and remanded with instructions for the trial court to reinstate the administratrix's complaint and grant her a trial against the driver.

Sunset Package Store, Inc. v. Carlsbad


No. 8556


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


79 N.M. 260; 1968-NMSC-105; 442 P.2d 572; 1968 N.M. LEXIS 1959



June 17, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF EDDY COUNTY, NEAL, Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee businesses in a complaint filed by the businesses which alleged that the city had failed to pass an ordinance imposing a lawful license tax in accordance with the provisions of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 46-4-2.


OVERVIEW: The businesses filed a complaint against the city that alleged the city had failed to pass an ordinance imposing a lawful license tax in accordance with the provisions of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 46-4-2. The city answered and, upon consideration of the businesses' motion, the pleadings and depositions of the city's mayor, the trial court granted summary judgment. The city appealed the judgment. The narrow point on appeal was whether the ordinance imposed a valid license tax for a tax period beginning on a specified date. The city argued that the ordinance remained in effect until it was amended or repealed. The businesses argued that the statute required the enactment of a license tax ordinance annually in order to have a valid imposition of the tax. The trial court sustained the businesses' contention and granted their motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court determined that the amount, the date, and manner of payment fixed by the ordinance remained from year to year until such time the ordinance was modified or repealed by an ordinance of the legislative body enacting the same. Accordingly, the trial court's grant of summary judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

 

275 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lopez


No. 8406


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


79 N.M. 235; 1968-NMSC-098; 441 P.2d 764; 1968 N.M. LEXIS 1950



June 10, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF McKINLEY COUNTY, ZINN, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed an order of the District Court of McKinley County (New Mexico), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief filed pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 21-1-1(93) (1953).


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief filed pursuant to N.M. R. Crim. P. 93, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 21-1-1(93) (1953). On appeal, the inmate, who was serving a sentence for escape, contended that his incarceration on the charge of escape was unlawful because his underlying detention for a violation of ordinances against drunkenness was in violation of his constitutional rights under U.S. Const. amends. VIII and XIV. The inmate admitted that he was a chronic alcoholic and argued that confining him as a violator of the criminal ordinances amounted to punishing him for an illness. The court held that as long as the commitment to custody was valid on its face, it was no defense to a charge of escape that the incarceration was based on a violation of a law which was allegedly unconstitutionally applied. The inmate also argued that the court failed to adequately inform him of his rights at his arraignment when he waived counsel and pled guilty to the escape charge. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that the trial court's finding that defendant's waiver was knowingly and voluntarily made was supported by the a preponderance of evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the petition for post-conviction relief.

 

276 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Burns v. State


Nos. 8453, 8454


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


79 N.M. 53; 1968-NMSC-060; 439 P.2d 702; 1968 N.M. LEXIS 1916



April 8, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY: CONSOLIDATED FOR PURPOSES OF APPEAL APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, MONTOYA, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two residents of Texas, brought separate actions against defendants, the State of Mexico, Bureau of Revenue, Income Tax Division, challenging the jurisdiction of the State to levy an income tax on wages paid to civilian personnel employed by the federal government in New Mexico. The District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) rendered judgment in favor of the State. Plaintiffs' appeals were consolidated for decision.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, residents of Texas, were civilians employed by the federal government at a missile range in New Mexico. The state had ceded jurisdiction of the property to the United States, reserving only the right to serve process. Prior to the cession of jurisdiction, the United States had passed the Buck Act, 4 U.S.C.S. §§ 104-110, which provided in part that no person was relieved from liability for a state income tax by reason of receiving income from services performed in a federal area. Plaintiffs challenged the jurisdiction of the State to levy an income tax on their wages. On appeal of a judgment in favor of the State, the court affirmed. The court held that the Buck Act had to be accorded prospective operation. It refused to presume an intention on the part of the legislature to cede its taxing power in the absence of a clear showing to the contrary. The court also rejected plaintiffs' argument that the income tax levied a tax upon personal property within the meaning of N.M. Const. art. VIII, § 2 and was in excess of the rates allowed in that section. The court held that the income tax was not levied upon real or personal property as those words were used in art. VIII, § 2.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments.

Holladay v. Upton


No. 8056


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


79 N.M. 1; 1968-NMSC-044; 438 P.2d 885; 1968 N.M. LEXIS 1903



March 25, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LEA COUNTY, REESE, JR., Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank applicants sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Lea County (New Mexico), which dismissed their appeal from a decision of appellee Commissioner of Banking. The Commissioner denied the applicants permission to file corporate papers.


OVERVIEW: The applicants filed a notice of intention to organize a bank. They received no notice of defects therein and made application for permission to file corporate papers. The Commissioner rejected their application. The applicants appealed the decision to the trial court. The Commissioner filed a motion to dismiss on the ground that the applicants failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The trial court granted the motion, holding that such an appeal was without basis in law. The applicants appealed to the court. The Commissioner argued that under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 48-22-34 (1953), appeal lay only from "orders" of the Commission; the denial of the application was not an "order." The court rejected the Commissioner's argument. The court held that the applicants were persons aggrieved by an order of the Commissioner, as required by § 48-22-34. The court held that the applicants were entitled to appeal the Commissioner's decision to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for further proceedings.

 

278 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Peyton v. Nord


No. 8456


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


78 N.M. 717; 1968-NMSC-027; 437 P.2d 716; 1968 N.M. LEXIS 1891



February 26, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: February 26, 1968


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL HABEAS CORPUS PROCEEDING (On MOTION FOR REHEARING)



DISPOSITION: Writ of habeas corpus made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner juvenile violated N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 40A-16-1 and 40A-16-3 (1953) and sought a writ of habeas corpus to effect his release from the custody of respondent county sheriff. The juvenile was made a ward of the court until the age of 21, or until further order of the court, and was ordered committed to a state boys' school during that period. He was in the physical custody of the sheriff pending delivery to the school.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile presented three serious questions for review: was the juvenile code adopted in 1955 and the juvenile court therein created constitutional; was the denial of a trial by jury a denial of constitutional rights guaranteed by the United States Constitution and the New Mexico Constitution; and was the fact that the juvenile received a penalty different from that provided when adults violated the same provisions of law deny the juvenile due process of law and equal protection of the law? The court granted a permanent writ of habeas corpus. In so ruling, the court concluded that the denial of a jury trial by the juvenile court was error. The court ruled that a juvenile charged with violation of a state law is entitled to a trial by jury in juvenile court if there is no certification to district court under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 13-8-27 and if the offense was one which would be triable by jury if committed by an adult. A judge was also named as a respondent but the court dismissed him because he did not have physical custody of the juvenile and he was unable to produce juvenile in court, therefore he was not a proper party.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that a permanent writ of habeas corpus be issued. Upon consideration of a motion for rehearing the opinion previously filed was withdrawn and the court's opinion was substituted therefor.

In re Nelson


No. 8533


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


78 N.M. 739; 1968-NMSC-028; 437 P.2d 1008; 1968 N.M. LEXIS 1892



February 26, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: Motion sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent attorney filed exceptions to a report by hearing commissioners in disciplinary proceedings and filed a motion that challenged the constitutionality of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 21-2-1.12, which required him to deposit the estimated cost of the transcript of the proceedings.


OVERVIEW: After being advised of the estimated cost of a transcript of his disciplinary hearing, § 21-2-1.12 required the attorney to deposit that amount in order to include the transcript in the record on appeal. The attorney filed a motion alleging that § 21-2-1.12 was a denial of procedural due process. On review, the court sustained the motion and found that § 21-2-1.12 violated U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV. The court noted that the commissioners' recommendation was not binding and that the attorney was entitled to a determination by the court. Because the facts developed at the hearing had to be incorporated in a transcript, full consideration could only be accomplished by submitting the transcript and giving the attorney an opportunity to indicate in what portion of the transcript the charges of misconduct as found by the commissioners were not supported or the discipline recommended was not justified. The court held that to require payment in advance prior to a determination on the merits could result in a denial of proper presentation and trial, thereby depriving the attorney of due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the attorney's motion.

 

280 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Witt v. State Canvassing Bd.


No. 8554


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


78 N.M. 682; 1968-NMSC-017; 437 P.2d 143; 1968 N.M. LEXIS 1885



February 5, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL MANDAMUS PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An original proceeding was brought by petitioner New Mexico Attorney General on behalf of the State and requested that respondent canvassing board be ordered to certify Proposition 7, amending N.M. Const. art. VII, § 1, as passed. The Attorney General asserted that N.M. Const. art. VII, § 3, insofar as it required a favorable vote of not less than two-thirds of those voting in each county to amend N.M. Const. art. VII, § 1, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: New Mexico was the only state in which there were no provisions for absentee voting. Several attempts to amend the state constitution to provide for absentee voting were unsuccessful because of the requirement that any amendment to N.M. Const. art. VII, § 1, be approved by a two-thirds favorable vote in every county and by at least three-fourths of the electors voting in the entire state. The court concluded that the requirement of a two-thirds favorable vote in every county resulted in greatly disproportionate values to votes in the different counties. Proposition 7 was passed by 81.8 percent of the voters who voted on the proposal but not by two-thirds favorable vote in every county. The court noted that under the Baker v. Carr rationale, it could see no rational basis to distinguish between voting for representatives in the legislature and voting on constitutional amendments. The requirement of "at least three-fourths of the electors voting in the whole state" was met when that percentage voting on the particular proposition favored it. The court held that requirement of a two-thirds vote in each county was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The canvassing board was ordered to certify that Proposition 7 had been ratified.

State v. Baros


No. 8419 (which includes No. 8084)


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


78 N.M. 623; 1968-NMSC-001; 435 P.2d 1005; 1968 N.M. LEXIS 1872



January 8, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, LARRAZOLO, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which denied his motion to vacate a third sentence entered against him for forging a check.


OVERVIEW: The inmate pled guilty to forging a check. Judgment was entered committing him to the penitentiary for 29 days. He was also placed on probation for two years; no conditions of probation were stated. The inmate served the 29 days. The State filed a motion to invoke the suspended sentence for violating the terms of suspension. The trial court committed the inmate to the penitentiary for not less than 2 nor more than 10 years. The inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus in the county in which he was imprisoned. The writ was granted and the inmate was returned to the trial court. The trial court sentenced the inmate again to 2 to 10 years, with credit for the 29 days previously served. The inmate filed a motion to vacate the third sentence. The trial court denied the motion and the inmate appealed. The court held that the original 29 day sentence was a valid sentence. The court held that the trial court could not revoke the inmate's probation because no conditions were stated. The court held that after the inmate served his sentence, the trial court lost jurisdiction over the sentence. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the action with directions to set aside and vacate the third sentence against the inmate.

State v. Hines


No. 8286


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


78 N.M. 471; 1967-NMSC-237; 432 P.2d 827; 1967 N.M. LEXIS 2833



October 23, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COLFAX COUNTY, McINTOSH, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant ought review of a judgment from the District Court of Colfax County (New Mexico), which denied his motion for post-conviction relief without a hearing. Defendant asserted that he was entitled to a hearing, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, and that the felony murder statute in existence at the time of his conviction was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that he was not advised of his right to a preliminary hearing, had none, and did not waive his right to one. Defendant also asserted that at trial, his counsel was ineffective for failing to file a plea of abatement, failing to request that jurors be released during their deliberations, and for "permitting" accomplice testimony. The trial court denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief without a hearing. The court held that defendant was not entitled to a hearing based on the substance of his claims. The court further held that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel where there was no indication that the trial was a travesty or a sham. Finally, the court held that defendant's claim that the former felony murder statute violated equal protection and due process had to be denied because defendant failed to allege what classification he belonged to that was treated unfairly or how the vagueness claim applied to him. The court explained that constitutional claims could only be considered when defendant alleged how the propositions applied to him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied defendant's motion for post conviction relief.

PEYTON v. NORD

SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


1967 N.M. LEXIS 2830



October 16, 1967

PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL HABEAS CORPUS PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: No jury trial having been accorded to petitioner, although requested, the writ of habeas corpus heretofore issued should be made permanent.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner juvenile filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, claiming that his imprisonment was illegal because he was improperly tried by a juvenile court without a jury.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was tried and convicted of a criminal offense. He did not appeal his conviction, but filed a writ of habeas corpus, claiming that he was improperly being held. The court held that it had jurisdiction to hear the habeas corpus petition because it would have been pointless for the juvenile to proceed before the trial court. The court also determined that the juvenile court was authorized by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 13-7-26 (1953) to hold the juvenile for trial after determining that it was actually a district court and not an inferior court. Finally, the court concluded that because the juvenile requested and was denied a trial by jury, the juvenile court violated his rights to due process. The court granted the writ, concluding that the juvenile should have been granted a trial by jury.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

Raburn v. Nash


No. 8446


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


78 N.M. 385; 1967-NMSC-194; 431 P.2d 874; 1967 N.M. LEXIS 2794



September 1, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 28, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL MANDAMUS PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: Writ discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate brought an original mandamus action seeking to compel respondent judge to dismiss the criminal information because of a denial of his rights to a speedy trial.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was first charged with forgery on March 4, 1965, He disqualified the resident judge and the case was set for trial at the April 1967 term. The inmate had also been charged with escape on February 5, 1965, to which he pleaded insanity. A psychiatric report was received September 20, 1965. In October 1965 the inmate was tried and convicted on the escape charge, for which he was serving a sentence in the penitentiary when he filed his mandamus against the trial judge. The court held that the inmate's speedy trial rights were not waived when he was in custody on other charges. The court held that inmate took no affirmative steps to make known his demand for a speedy trial, and that motions filed in the escape action did not equate to requests for speedy trial in the forgery action. In discharging the mandamus the court held that the inmate's prosecution for escape, incarceration for that offense, and his plea of not guilty by reason of insanity all constitute reasons making the delay in his prosecution reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court discharged the alternative writ of mandamus.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Valencia County (New Mexico) that denied his release based on alleged improprieties in entering his plea of guilty to the offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that he pled guilty to an escape charge based upon an inducement by the district attorney for the sentence to run concurrently with time spent in jail. The sentence was vacated on the DA's motion, and defendant was subsequently sentenced to a period of not less that two years. In affirming the judgment the court held that defendant's entry of a guilty plea after counsel with his attorney constituted waiver of his right to a preliminary hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
