City of Raton v. Sproule


No. 8214


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


78 N.M. 138; 1967-NMSC-141; 429 P.2d 336; 1967 N.M. LEXIS 2747



June 19, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COLFAX COUNTY, McINTOSH, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city clerk and intervenor taxpayers appealed the decision of the District Court of Colfax County (New Mexico), which found in favor of plaintiff city in an action seeking a judgment declaring the constitutional validity of N.M. Const. art. 9, § 12; 1965 N.M. Laws ch. 300; and an election resolution.


OVERVIEW: The city filed an action seeking a judgment declaring the constitutional validity of N.M. Const. art. 9, § 12; 1965 N.M. Laws ch. 300; and an election resolution. The action was brought against the city clerk, who refused to publish the resolution and to proceed with the election. The trial court upheld the validity of the amendment, implementing statutes, and the election resolution in all respects; the city clerk and the taxpayers appealed. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, holding that the application of the legislation was not confined to any precinct and was not confined to any particular affair or affairs of a precinct. It applied equally to all municipalities and to all counties in New Mexico. It was the court's opinion that the statutes did not fall within the constitutional prohibition against special or local laws regulating precinct affairs. In view of the court's disposition of the questions concerning the validity of the amendment and the implementing legislation, it followed that the city clerk's contention that she may not spend public monies for the publication of notice of holding an illegal election, must fail.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court in favor of the city in its action against the city clerk and the taxpayers seeking the constitutional validity of statutes.

 

288 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of Dirs. of Mem. Gen. Hosp. of Las Cruces v. Cnty. Indigent Hosp. Claims Bd.


No. 8192


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


77 N.M. 475; 1967-NMSC-042; 423 P.2d 994; 1967 N.M. LEXIS 2656



February 20, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF DONA ANA COUNTY, ZIMMERMAN, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital challenged a decision from the District Court of Dona Ana County (New Mexico) which held in favor of appellee board and held that the Indigent Hospital Claims Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 13-2-12 to 13-2-29 (1953) was unconstitutional as violative of the New Mexico Constitution.


OVERVIEW: In an action brought by a hospital to recover funds paid for care of indigents, the trial court found that the hospital had done everything required of it by the Act, and that funds were due on account of claims duly filed. The trial court also found there was no money in the county indigent hospital claims fund with which to pay the hospital's claims. The trial court found the Act unconstitutional and the board was not required to pay the funds to the hospital. In the instant case the county had budgeted and levied the full 20 mills to pay indigent hospital claims, and the voters had voted against a levy exceeding that budgeted amount to pay further indigent hospital claims. The court held that since the county had budged the full 20 mills, and the voters had refused to authorize an additional levy in excess of that amount to pay hospital bills of indigents, the statute which attempted to authorize the creation of a public debt could only be characterized as a device for circumventing the limitation of N.M. Const. Art. VIII, § 2. The court affirmed the decision that the Act was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision in favor of the board, holding that the Act was unconstitutional.

290 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Bell Tel. Lab., Inc. v. Bureau of Revenue


No. 7955


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


78 N.M. 78; 1966-NMSC-253; 428 P.2d 617; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2804



November 28, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal Dismissed June 12, 1967. See 87 S.Ct. 2111.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, SCARBOROUGH, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed the decision of the District Court of Santa Fe County, Scarborough (New Mexico), which held that the taxpayers were not entitled to recover a refund of taxes paid to appellees, Bureau of Revenue of the State of New Mexico (bureau) and director of school tax division (director). The trial court did find that the taxpayers were entitled to a refund of a penalty, but otherwise dismissed the complaint with prejudice.


OVERVIEW: The tax was assessed against the taxpayers pursuant to the Emergency School Tax Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 72-16-1 to 72-16-47 (1953). The tax was imposed upon entities or persons "engaged in business" under the terms of the statute. The taxpayers asserted that they were not "engaged in business" in the state as they did not hold themselves out as engaging in business in New Mexico, did not advertise in the state, nor sell or distributed goods in state. The taxpayers conducted intermittent development tests of missiles, launching equipment, guidance systems, radar, and data collection in New Mexico. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court finding that the taxpayers were engaged in a local business activity. The court found that the evidence of continuous testing in New Mexico supported that finding and the imposition of the tax. The court also found that the tax being imposed on receipts due to the testing conducted by the taxpayers was fair as the activities involved in the testing were sufficiently disjoined from the interstate operation so that those activities were a local incident or business activity and that the receipts of such activity were taxable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court in favor of the bureau and the director was affirmed in the taxpayers' suit for a refund.

 

291 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Sitta v. Zinn


No. 8221


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


77 N.M. 146; 1966-NMSC-239; 420 P.2d 131; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2790



November 14, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROHIBITION PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: The alternative writ heretofore issued will be made permanent.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought a writ of prohibition to a district court judgment which denied their motion, made pursuant to N.M. R. Ann. 1-41(e) (1965), to dismiss a complaint filed against them. The trial court overruled the motion because it considered N.M. Stat. Ann. § 132 (1965) to be applicable to proceedings that were pending at the time it had been filed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were defendants in a proceeding filed in the district court less than two years before the effective date of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 132 (1965). After the passage of two, but less than three years from the date of filing, the case had not been finally determined, and petitioners filed a motion to dismiss under N.M. R. Ann. 1-41(e). N.M. Stat. Ann. § 132 (1965), purported to amend N.M. R. Ann. 1-41(e) so as to increase the time for taking action to bring proceedings to a final determination from two years after filing to three years and, in addition, to exempt entirely from the rule's operation proceedings wherein jury action had been demanded. The trial court overruled the motion finding N.M. Stat. Ann. § 132 (1965) to be applicable to proceedings pending when it went into effect. A writ of prohibition and mandamus was sought and the court issued an alternative writ. On hearing of the matter the court made the writ permanent. The court held that § 132 could not be constitutionally applied to pending matters.


OUTCOME: The alternative writ was made permanent.

 

292 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Drink, Inc. v. Babcock


No. 7942


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


77 N.M. 277; 1966-NMSC-236; 421 P.2d 798; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2782



November 7, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion to Intervene and for Rehearing Denied January 3, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, MONTOYA, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retail liquor dealer, appealed an order of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which denied the dealer's petition for injunctive relief an the dealer's action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 46-9-1, 46-9-3, and 46-9-11 (1953), or, in the alternative, an injunction to prohibit enforcement of those provisions of the law by defendant director of the liquor division.


OVERVIEW: The dealer challenged the constitutionality of three statutes, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 46-9-1, 46-9-3, and 46-9-11 (1953), which required the distiller, by contract, to establish the wholesale and retail prices of his product and prohibit the sale of trademarked liquor not bearing an established and published price. Under the statutes, sales of trademarked liquor at less than the contract price constituted unfair competition. Such a sale gave rise to a right of action by anyone damaged thereby, and subjected the dealer to criminal penalties, whether or not the dealer was a party to the contract. The trial court held that there was a failure to prove the challenged provisions to be unconstitutional and denied injunctive relief. The dealer appealed, and the court reversed and held that the statutes at issue were unconstitutional and void. The court held that the fair-trade contract and markup provisions of the Liquor Control Act were manifestly unreasonable legislation, were not an appropriate exercise of the state's police power, and were in violation of N.M. Const. art. II, §§ 4 and 18.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and found the statutes unconstitutional and unenforceable.

 

293 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. Cox


No. 8237


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


77 N.M. 55; 1966-NMSC-210; 419 P.2d 253; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2765



October 17, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL HABEAS CORPUS PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: Writ theretofore issued discharged and petitioner remanded to custody.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a writ of habeas corpus and contended that his imprisonment was unlawful because he was not furnished appointed counsel at his parole revocation hearing and evidence of escape from a Tennessee court was not sufficient evidence of violation of parole.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was sentenced after conviction, then was paroled to a detainer to serve another sentence in Tennessee. By letter from the Tennessee penal farm, the warden was advised that the inmate had escaped. The inmate was apprehended and following a hearing on the violation of the terms of his parole, his parole was revoked. The court held that there was no constitutional right to an attorney in a parole revocation proceeding. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-17-27 (1953) indicated that the parole board was not required to hear statements or arguments by attorneys. The requirements for a hearing on the parole violation, set forth in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-17-28(C) (1953), did not by implication give the inmate the right to effective appearance or representation by counsel. Because the parole was an act of clemency or grace extended by the parole board, ordinary procedural rules did not apply as in criminal proceedings. In discharging the petition, the court held that the evidence from the Tennessee penal farm, in the form of a letter advising of the inmate's escape, was sufficient because strict observance of technical rules was not required in a hearing before an administrative body.


OUTCOME: The court discharged the petition and remanded the inmate to custody.

 

294 of 795 DOCUMENTS


City of Albuquerque v. Chapman


No. 7920


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


77 N.M. 86; 1966-NMSC-212; 419 P.2d 460; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2767



October 17, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, SWOPE, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which awarded compensation to appellee landowners in a condemnation proceeding.


OVERVIEW: In a condemnation proceeding, the city obtained an order authorizing immediate entry of a 35-foot strip of land that belonged to the landowners for the purpose of widening a road. After the order authorizing entry, the landowners sold the entire property to the buyers. The buyers then filed a plat of a subdivision with the county that showed the entire acreage and the 35-foot strip for the road. The trial court held that the city was obligated to pay the landowners for the strip. The court held that the city's taking of the property was complete before sale to the buyers because the city had installed curbs, gutters, and pavement. The court held that the dedication in the plat did not waive the liability to pay compensation because there was no dedication of the 35-foot strip. In affirming the judgment, the court held that the city used its power of eminent domain to take the strip before the land was dedicated by plat, and it remained liable to pay the landowners.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

295 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Coe v. City of Albuquerque


No. 7878


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


76 N.M. 771; 1966-NMSC-196; 418 P.2d 545; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2751



September 19, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 14, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, McMANUS, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, City of Albuquerque and the City Commission of Albuquerque and its members, sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which rezoned petitioner property owners' tract to C-1 and enjoined respondents from requiring a replat of the tract as a condition for either changing the zone maps or issuing building permits to the property owners.


OVERVIEW: In reversing the judgment, the court found that to the extent that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 14-28-16, (1953) purported to allow the district court to zone land, it was void as an unconstitutional delegation of power to the judiciary, contravening N.M. Const. art. III, § 1. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 14-28-16 (1953) provided for a record that showed on what grounds the decision was made. However, the return to the writ showed recommendations made by the planning department, the decision of the planning commission, and the decision of the city commission. There was nothing in the return to the writ to show the grounds of the decision appealed from. Further, when the trial court issued its writ, the tract was zoned R-2, conditioned on a replat. Respondents did not appeal that portion of the trial court's judgment enjoining enforcement of the condition. Accordingly, that portion of the injunction was in effect. However, the portion of the injunction pertaining to building permits was not within any issue raised by the proceedings, nor was it litigated. Not being within the issues, that part of the injunction pertaining to building permits was erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause with instructions to the trial court to set aside the judgment and enter a new judgment enjoining respondents from enforcing the condition to R-2 zoning, to give respondents an opportunity to amend their return to the writ, and to decide whether denial of C-1 zoning was arbitrary as a matter of law.

 

296 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Raton Pub. Serv. Co. v. Hobbes


No. 7795


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


76 N.M. 535; 1966-NMSC-150; 417 P.2d 32; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2706



July 25, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COLFAX COUNTY, GALLEGOS, Judge



DISPOSITION: Cause remanded to district court with instructions to strike order not to violate statute from its judgment, and as so modified judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public utility company sought review of the decision from the District Court, Colfax County (New Mexico), which ordered that all final decisions of the public utility company be made at meetings open to the public as required by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 5-6-17 (1953).


OVERVIEW: The public utility company brought a declaratory judgment action to determine whether it was subject to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 5-6-17 (1953), relating to public meetings of all governing bodies of the state that are supported by public funds. The public utility company claimed that the statute did not apply to it where its sole function was of a business nature without any control over financial matters or the fixing of rates and that, if the statute applied, it was unconstitutionally vague. The trial court held that all final decisions made by the public utility company should be made at open meetings. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that: (1) the public utility company, which had an obligation to pay over to the city all income not consumed in the operation of the electric utility system, was supported by public funds within the meaning of § 5-6-17; (2) the title to the statute was not so misleading as to be unconstitutional under N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16; and (3) where the purpose of the statute was to provide that governing bodies make decisions in the open, its language was broad enough to include the public utility company.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the trial court's decision insofar as it required that all final decisions made by the public utility company be made a meetings open to the public. The cause was remanded to the trial court with instructions to strike from its judgment the order not to violate the statute where an injunction not to violate a statute was without foundation in law or equity.

 

297 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Bowdich v. Albuquerque


No. 7729


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


76 N.M. 511; 1966-NMSC-133; 416 P.2d 523; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2689



July 5, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, McMANUS, Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which ruled that the assessment roll adopted by the city was void and invalid.


OVERVIEW: The city voters approved the issuance of bonds. The construction of a sewer project required that substantial portions of a certain street be torn up in order to install a storm sewer. The city decided that overall savings could be effected by uniformly widening and rebuilding the street at the same time that the sewer work was being done. A protest hearing was held and overruled. The city adopted a total assessment of over several thousand dollars. An action by appellee property owners in the area was filed in opposition to the assessment roll. The lower court ruled that the provisional order method of assessment did not vest the city with the power to assess the property owners in the area for the cost of removal and replacement of pavement, curbs, gutters, and sidewalks and that such assessment was arbitrary and capricious. The assessment roll adopted was held void and invalid. On review, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter. The court held that the provisional order method for street improvement vested the city with the power to remove existing paving, gutters, curbs, and sidewalks, to replace them, and to assess the property owners of the area the cost.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter to the district court, with direction that the judgment against the city be set aside and that it should proceed in a manner consistent with the court's opinion.

 

298 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Cmty. PSC v. N.M. PSC


No. 7739


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


76 N.M. 314; 1966-NMSC-053; 414 P.2d 675; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2611



March 21, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 1, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LINCOLN COUNTY, ZIMMERMAN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner public utility appealed an order of the District Court of Lincoln County (New Mexico), which affirmed an order of respondent New Mexico Public Service Commission in a proceeding under N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 68-9-1 to 68-9-5 (1953), wherein the Commission granted a certificate of public convenience and necessity to respondent electric cooperative to serve a particular subdivision.


OVERVIEW: The public utility challenged the grant of the certificate to the electric cooperative and raised the issue of the constitutionality of an act that amended N.M. Stat. Ann. § 68-3-2(F)(1) (1953) to place rural electric cooperatives under the Public Utility Act for certain purposes by including them within the definition of "public utility." The trial court upheld the act and the utility appealed. The court reversed and held that the amendments to the public utility law were discriminatory and denied to the utility the equal protection of the laws and were violative of the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution and of N.M. Const. art. II, § 18. The court held that there was no supportable or rational basis for permitting the electric cooperative to serve selected individuals who were not members of the cooperative with entire freedom from control of its rates, while at the same time the utility, when serving the same individuals, was required to charge for such service only such rates as the Commission approved.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the declaration of constitutionality and remanded.

State v. Miller


No. 7893


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


76 N.M. 62; 1966-NMSC-041; 412 P.2d 240; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2599



March 14, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BERNALILLO COUNTY, ZINN, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: Remanded with direction to grant a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which convicted him of murder.


OVERVIEW: After a store clerk was killed during a robbery attempt an arrest warrant for defendant was issued. The complaint upon which the warrant was issued charged that defendant fled the state of New Mexico and traveled interstate commerce to avoid prosecution in New Mexico for armed robbery. Defendant was arrested in San Diego, California, by a Federal Bureau of Investigation (F.B.I.) agent acting under the authority of the warrant. Defendant was taken to the San Diego F.B.I. office where a set of his fingerprints were obtained. The fingerprints were later introduced in evidence at a preliminary hearing and at his trial. Defendant was found guilty of the murder. On review, defendant's major assertion was that the lower court erred when it failed to suppress the evidence concerning the fingerprints. Defendant asserted that the arrest was illegal because the warrant had been issued on a complaint, which was insufficient, because it did not show the necessary probable cause for his arrest. The court remanded. The court held that the complaint was deficient and the resulting arrest was therefore illegal and the fingerprints should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the lower court with direction to grant defendant a new trial, consistent with the views expressed in the case.

State ex rel. State Park & Rec. Comm'n v. N.M. State Auth.


No. 7650


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


76 N.M. 1; 1966-NMSC-033; 411 P.2d 984; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2588



February 28, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 28, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, McCULLOH, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with direction to set aside the judgment and proceed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state park and recreation commission (commission) challenged the judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which held that the State Revenue Bond Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 11-10-1 et seq., was unconstitutional because it allowed state agencies to issue bonds in violation of state laws prohibiting indebtedness without providing for sufficient tax.


OVERVIEW: The commission sought to issue bonds to finance the construction of a boat dock facility under the State Revenue Bond Act (act), N.M. Stat. Ann. § 11-10-1 et seq. Defendant state authority (authority) refused to allow the commission to issue the bonds and the commission filed suit. The trial court held that the act was unconstitutional under N.M. Const. art. IV, § 29 and the commission appealed the ruling. The court held that the laws passed by the legislature were entitled to a presumption of legality, and would not be declared illegal unless it exceeded the bounds of the constitution. The court stated that the act was not unconstitutional because it did not violate art. IV, § 29, and because the bonds did not violate the prohibition against indebtedness without providing for sufficient tax. The court determined that the legislature was authorized to allow state agencies to issue bonds for the construction of public works, and that the authority erred in not granting the commission permission. The court reversed and remanded for additional proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, which held that state law allowing state agencies to issue bonds was unconstitutional under the state constitution.

 

301 of 795 DOCUMENTS


George A. Rutherford, Inc. v. Gonzales


No. 7755


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


75 N.M. 774; 1966-NMSC-031; 411 P.2d 751; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2590



February 28, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, REIDY, JUDGE



DISPOSITION: Reversed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Commissioner of the Bureau of Revenue of the State of New Mexico, challenged the judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) that determined that appellee, a general contractor, was entitled to a refund of taxes that were unlawfully paid but paid without protest.


OVERVIEW: The general contractor constructed buildings for the federal government and paid taxes to the state on proceeds received in performing the contract. Three years later, the contractor petitioned for a refund under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16-23 (1953), claiming that the taxes were erroneously paid. Following a hearing, the Commissioner of the Bureau of Revenue of the State of New Mexico denied the refund application after concluding that a refund was not permitted based upon a mistake of law. The contractor appealed, and the district court concluded that the contractor was entitled to a refund of the amount unlawfully paid. The commissioner appealed the adverse ruling. In reversing, the court concluded that, under N.M. Stat. § 72-16-28 (1953), where the legality of an assessment was challenged, taxes were to be paid under protest. Because the contractor paid the taxes without protest, there was no remedy or right of action available to it.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was reversed, and the matter was remanded with direction to set aside the judgment and entered a judgment sustaining the order of the Commissioner of the Bureau of Revenue.

Daniels v. Watson


No. 7987


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


75 N.M. 661; 1966-NMSC-011; 410 P.2d 193; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2568



January 17, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LEA COUNTY, NASH, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Lea County (New Mexico), which held the Junior College Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 73-33-1 to 73-33-20 (1953), to be constitutional and ruled against plaintiffs in their action against defendant New Mexico Junior College Board members.


OVERVIEW: The Act provided for the formation of the junior college districts, for the elections concerning the formation of the districts and the selection of the members of the supervisory board, for the means for the operation of the junior colleges, and provided for the issuance of bonds. The New Mexico Junior College was created and funded under the Act. Plaintiffs claimed that the Act was unconstitutional in their action. The district court ruled against them and they sought review. On appeal, the court upheld the judgment. The court rejected plaintiffs' argument that the Act required board members to reside in the junior college district, in violation of N.M. Const. art. V, § 13, on the theory that the board members were state officers, not district officers, and therefore their residence could not be restricted. The court held that board members were not elective public officers in the sense as used in N.M. Const. art. VII, § 2 and that the legislature could have justifiably set their qualifications. The court found that the officers of a public corporation for a municipal purpose were not "public officers" within the contemplation of art. VII, § 2.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

303 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Rask v. Bd. of Bar Examiners


No. 7883


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


75 N.M. 617; 1966-NMSC-001; 409 P.2d 256; 1966 N.M. LEXIS 2558



January 3, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: Decision reversed; motion for admission granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney sought the reversal of the decision of respondent board of bar examiners, which denied his application for admission to practice law in New Mexico on motion.


OVERVIEW: The attorney applied for admission to practice law in New Mexico on motion, and the board denied the application under rule II. A. 10. of the rules governing bar examiners, bar examinations and admissions to the Bar of the State of New Mexico because the attorney did not show exceptional circumstances to justify waiving the bar exam. The court reversed and set aside the board's denial of the attorney's application and granted the motion for admission. The board had changed its policy with respect to admissions on motion, which was not justified in view of the long history of ruling otherwise. The board did not give any information as to what it considered to be "exceptional circumstances" or what matters the board considered. Discretion was not exercised by the board, or, if such discretion was exercised, the board failed to follow the almost uniform practice of its predecessors. The term "exceptional circumstances" could not be used to arbitrarily refuse to recommend the admission on motion, without the giving of underlying reasons.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and set aside the board's denial of the attorney's application for admission to practice law in New Mexico on motion. The court granted the motion for admission.

State v. Dalrymple


No. 7857


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


75 N.M. 514; 1965-NMSC-124; 407 P.2d 356; 1965 N.M. LEXIS 1602



November 1, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CHAVES COUNTY, REESE, JR., Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Chaves County (New Mexico), which sentenced him as an habitual offender after he had pleaded guilty to one count of robbery in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-16-2 (1953).


OVERVIEW: Defendant had pleaded guilty to one count of robbery in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-16-2 (1953). An information was filed charging defendant with being a habitual offender in that he had been convicted in 1958, 1960, and 1963 in another state of crimes which if committed in New Mexico would have been felonies. Defendant was tried before a jury on the issue of prior convictions. Defendant contended that he only had pro forma representation in the prior convictions. The State's motion to strike that evidence was granted. The trial court, by jury verdict, found that defendant was the same person convicted in each of the out-of-state cases and sentenced him to imprisonment for the rest of his natural life, pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40A-29-5(C). The court held that the evidence on due process and defendant's right to counsel in the prior convictions was admissible. The court further held that the trial court erred in sustaining the motion to strike. The court concluded that if the prior convictions were void, they would be nullities and not convictions that could be used to sentence defendant as a habitual offender. The court ordered a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment which sentenced defendant as an habitual offender after he pled guilty to one count of robbery. The court remanded the cause to the trial court with instructions to grant defendant a new trial.

 

305 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Orosco v. Cox


No. 7951


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


75 N.M. 431; 1965-NMSC-098; 405 P.2d 668; 1965 N.M. LEXIS 1585



September 7, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL HABEAS CORPUS PROCEEDING



DISPOSITION: Writ discharged and petitioner remanded to custody.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought a writ of habeas corpus alleging that he was being illegally restrained of his liberty by respondent warden by virtue of a purported judgment of the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico) where petitioner was adjudged guilty of murder in the second degree and sentenced to serve a term of not less than three nor more than 99 years.


OVERVIEW: The inmate brought a writ of habeas corpus. The court held that he failed to establish his right to release on a writ of habeas corpus. However, the court considered his right to introduce evidence to contradict or to establish matters not shown in the record of proceedings below. N.M. Const. art. II, § 7 provided that the privilege of the writ of habeas corpus should not be suspended. The writ of habeas corpus was a collateral attack on a judgment upon which commitment had issued, and would lie only when the judgment under attack was absolutely void because the court which rendered the judgment was without jurisdiction. There was nothing wrong in the appellate court receiving evidence outside the record to establish the absence or loss of jurisdiction through denial of any of the rights guaranteed to a prisoner at the bar by either the United States or New Mexico Constitutions. Here, the evidence offered was properly received and entitled to consideration by the appellate court. Having weighed the evidence with the court record, the court find no denial of any constitutional rights. The writ was discharged and the inmate was remanded to the custody of the warden.


OUTCOME: The court discharged the writ of habeas corpus. The inmate was remanded to the custody of the warden.

 

306 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Silver City Consol. Sch. Dist. No. 1 v. Bd. of Regents of N.M. W. College


No. 7673


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


75 N.M. 106; 1965-NMSC-035; 401 P.2d 95; 1965 N.M. LEXIS 1519



April 5, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GRANT COUNTY, HODGES, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a college board of regents, challenged the writ of mandamus issued by the District Court of Grant County (New Mexico) that required it to transfer and convey to appellee school district a high school building, its furnishings, and sufficient land surrounding the building for school purposes.


OVERVIEW: The school district paid funds to the college, which used the money to construct and furnish a high school building on its campus. The college thereafter maintained and operated the high school until 1960, at which time it relinquished operation to the school district. When the college refused to transfer and convey the building, land, and furnishings to the school district as required by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 73-8-46 (1953), the school district filed suit. The district court issued a writ of mandamus requiring the college's board of regents to convey the property. The board appealed. In affirming, the court concluded that, while public property held and used in a proprietary, rather than governmental, capacity could not be taken for another public use without payment of just compensation, the operation of a school by a state institution was a governmental rather than a proprietary function. The transfer of such property to another governmental entity devoted to a similar public use was one for which no compensation was required.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

307 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Gomez v. Campbell


No. 7678


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


75 N.M. 86; 1965-NMSC-025; 400 P.2d 956; 1965 N.M. LEXIS 1509



March 8, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 28, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING IN MANDAMUS



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ of mandamus discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original proceeding in mandamus, relator county taxpayers sought an alternative writ of mandamus seeking to require respondents, the governor and 11 state boards or commissions, to return and thereafter maintain the main offices of the executive agencies at the State capital and not elsewhere.


OVERVIEW: The fundamental question involved in the mandamus action related to the meaning of N.M. Const. art. V, § 1, and whether it mandatorily required that all officers of the executive department to maintain their offices at the capital. The State capital was located in the county in which the taxpayers lived and voted. After consideration of the law, the court concluded that the alternative writ of mandamus was improvidently issued and discharged it. The court held that the taxpayers lacked standing to raise the constitutional question in their mandamus action. It was not the duty of the court or any other court to sit in judgment upon the action of the executive branch of the government except when the question was presented by a litigant claiming to be adversely affected by the executive act on the particular ground complained of. The court concluded that a citizen was without standing to question the constitutionality of a statute. The court found that, rather than to apply to the courts for relief, the taxpayers had other remedies such as through the elective process or appealing to the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court discharged the taxpayers' writ of mandamus.

 

308 of 795 DOCUMENTS


STATE ex rel. STATE PARK & REC. COMMN. v. NEW MEXICO STATE AUTH.


No. 7650


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


1965 N.M. LEXIS 1508



March 1, 1965 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Opinion Withdrawn February 28, 1966


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF SANTA FE COUNTY, McCULLOH, Judge



DISPOSITION: The cause is reversed and remanded to the district court with direction that the judgment heretofore entered be set aside and to proceed in a manner not inconsistent with the views herein expressed.

IT IS SO ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, State Park And Recreation Commission, its superintendent, and members, sought review of the decision of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which entered judgment for appellees, New Mexico State Authority and its members, holding that the State Revenue Bond Act (bond act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 11-10-1 et seq. was unconstitutional in the commission's declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The commission had sought the issuance of bonds under the bond act to construct a boat dock facility at a state park. The court reversed, holding that the bond act did not constitute an unlawful delegation of legislative power. The legislature declared the policy and established primary standards to which the agencies had to conform. The court found that the legislature had not delegated its authority to make a law, but had delegated power to determine facts upon which the law makes its own action depend. The court held that the title of the bond act gave reasonable notice of the subject matter of the statute and that it had not violated N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16. The court found that the bond act did not constitute the incurrence of indebtedness in violation of N.M. Const. art. IV, § 29 and N.M. Const. art. IX, §§ 7 and 8. The bond act did not contravene N.M. Const. art. IV, § 18 because it did not amend 1963 N.M. Emergency Laws ch. 98 or other laws pertaining to state agencies, counties, towns, and other entities granted power by the bond act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed declaratory judgment in favor of the authority and the members in the commission's superintendent, and member's declaratory judgment action.

 

309 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Gruschus v. Bureau of Revenue


No. 7519


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


74 N.M. 775; 1965-NMSC-013; 399 P.2d 105; 1965 N.M. LEXIS 1497



February 8, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY: Action to recover privilege tax paid. The District Court, Santa Fe County, James M. Scarborough, D. J., denied relief, and plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, Noble, J., held that privilege tax provision exempting state contractors (who had previously been exempt in any case) from liability with respect to existing lump-sum or unit price contracts for particular projects if contracts would not allow increase to cover privilege tax was not unconstitutional as in violation of requirements of equal protection or equality and uniformity of taxation.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Santa Fe County (New Mexico), in favor of appellees, the Bureau of Revenue and revenue officials, in the contractor's action seeking a refund of a gross receipts tax paid. The tax was imposed on five unit price contracts after they had been made. An issue presented by the appeal concerned the constitutionality of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16-5(D) (1953).


OVERVIEW: N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16-5(D) (1953) provided an exemption from an emergency school tax imposed on gross receipts from any lump sum or unit price contract for a particular project entered into before the effective date of the tax where the contract did not by its terms allow the contractor to increase his price to cover the tax. In the refund action, the trial court ruled that the exemption contravened the equality and uniformity clause of N.M. Const. art. VIII, § 1 and the equal protection clauses of N.M. Const. art. II, § 18 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. On appeal, the court rejected the contention that the exemption created a special, unreasonable class and that the denial of the exemption to others amounted to discrimination. The court found that only those having a cost-plus or cost-plus-a-fixed-fee contract were claimed to have been denied the benefit of the exemption, but such contracts automatically included the tax where there was no express agreement to the contrary and, ergo, were different from lump sum or unit price contracts. The court held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16-5(D) (1953) was a proper use of legislative power. Thus, remand was required.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case with instructions to the trial court to vacate its judgment and to proceed further in a manner not inconsistent with what the court had said.

Llano, Inc. v. Southern Union Gas Co.


No. 7508


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


75 N.M. 7; 1964-NMSC-257; 399 P.2d 646; 1964 N.M. LEXIS 2336; 23 Oil & Gas Rep. 566



December 21, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 26, 1965.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a gas company and the state public service commission, sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Lea County (New Mexico), annulling and vacating an administrative order that had declared appellee corporation to be a public utility and had ordered it to cease and desist from the sale and delivery of natural gas.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the corporation, which provided natural gas to only one customer, was not a public utility and was not required to comply with the New Mexico Public Utility Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 68-3-1 to 68-6-8, 68-7-1 to 68-11-1, 68-11-3 to 68-11-5 (1953 Comp.). The court affirmed, holding that although the trial court erred in its admission of additional testimony, the error was harmless because no significant new evidence was produced. The court determined that the decisive findings and conclusions of the trial court were properly based upon the record of proceedings before the public service commission. The court found that the corporation, on the facts in the record, was not a public utility as defined in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 68-3-2(F) because it did not hold itself out as engaged in the business of supplying natural gas to the public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment annulling and vacating the order of the public service commission.

Bd. of Educ. v. Hartley


No. 7479


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


74 N.M. 469; 1964-NMSC-204; 394 P.2d 985; 1964 N.M. LEXIS 2277



August 24, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: August 24, 1964


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus proceeding by Board of Education to compel Attorney General to issue certificate of approval of school bond issue. The District Court, Santa Fe County, Samuel Z. Montoya, D. J., quashed the alternative writ and dismissed the cause, and the board appealed. The Supreme Court, Carmody, J., held that resolution calling for school bond election, notice of election, ballot, and resolution publication calling for election and in one way or another stating that purpose of the election was to issue bonds for school purposes rendered election proceedings invalid under constitutional prohibition against borrowing of money by school district except for erecting and furnishing school buildings and purchasing school grounds, notwithstanding claimed presumption that money raised would be used for constitutional purposes.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school board sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which quashed its alternative writ in mandamus and dismissed the board's suit to compel the New Mexico Attorney General to issue a certificate of approval of the board's proposed bond issue.


OVERVIEW: The school board adopted a resolution to issue bonds to raise funds "for school purposes." After electoral approval, the board requested the Attorney General's certificate of approval, which was denied. The board filed suit in mandamus for such approval. On appeal from the adverse judgment, the board appealed, arguing that any error in the bond issue's documentary language was cured under N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 73-8-31 and 73-8-32 (1953) and that the words "for school purposes" were sufficient description of the purpose of the borrowing. In affirming, the court ruled that §§ 73-8-31 and 73-8-32 provided a limitation period for district court suits to contest the bond issue's validity and not to the exercise of the Attorney General's statutory duty. The court also ruled that the description of "for school purposes" was too general and encompassed uses of funds other than that permitted by N.M. Const. art. IX, § 11. The court held that the election proceedings for bond approval were rendered invalid because the electorate were not informed of the actual purpose of the attempted borrowing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

312 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Palmer v. Miller


No. 7608


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


74 N.M. 129; 1964-NMSC-072; 391 P.2d 416; 1964 N.M. LEXIS 2150



April 13, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: April 13, 1964


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceeding on petition for writ of mandamus to require petitioner's name to be placed on primary election ballot. The Supreme Court held that statute providing that petition for nomination to be valid must be signed by at least 3% of votes cast at last general election for office for which petition is being circulated means 3% of total votes for all candidates for office, and not merely 3% of votes cast for candidate of particular political party.



DISPOSITION: Writ previously issued discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizen sought a writ of mandamus to require respondent Secretary of State, State of New Mexico to place the citizen's name on the primary ballot of the Democratic party as a candidate for the office of United States Senator. Pursuant to the original jurisdiction vested in the court under N.M. Const. art. VI, § 3, it issued an alternative writ ordering the citizen's name placed on the ballot as requested.


OVERVIEW: The citizen proceeded under the provisions of N.M. Stat. Ann § 3-11-7 (1953), which provided that he could have his name included as a candidate by the timely filing of a declaration of candidacy together with a nominating petition signed by qualified electors who were members of the Democratic party, resident in one-half of the counties in the state, equal to at least three percent of the votes cast for the office. The citizen was advised that his name would not be placed on the primary ballot because the number of signatures required by law was not contained in the petition. It was agreed that sufficient names were signed to the nominating petition if § 3-11-7 meant three percent of the votes cast for the Democratic candidate, and not for all candidates. The court ordered that the alternative writ be discharged. The court noted that the legislative language was clear, and there was little room for construction, and concluded that the legislature could not have intended that the number of names signed on a petition should equal three percent of the vote cast for a particular party candidate for an office, and not three percent of the vote cast for all candidates for the office.


OUTCOME: The writ previously issued by the court was discharged.

Sandia S&L Ass'n v. Kleinheim


No. 7356


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


74 N.M. 95; 1964-NMSC-067; 391 P.2d 324; 1964 N.M. LEXIS 2144



April 6, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: April 6, 1964


PRIOR HISTORY: Tax refund suit. The District Court, Bernalillo County, D. A. Macpherson, Jr., D. J., dismissed complaint, and plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, Moise, J., held that if tax was unconstitutional, as asserted, there was no right or power in state tax commission to assess it and no jurisdiction in commission to consider complaint and statute providing for protesting valuation was inapplicable and, therefore, exhaustion of administrative remedies provided by statute was not prerequisite to refund suit.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which dismissed the corporation's action against appellee county treasurer seeking a refund of the taxes paid for lack of standing pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-5-4 (1953).


OVERVIEW: The state tax commission determined the actual value of the shares of capital stock of the corporation and certified the same to the local county assessor as required by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-6-4 (1953). The value was determined in accordance with N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-6-6 (1953). The corporation timely paid the first half of the taxes under protest and then instituted an action alleging that the tax was null and void. The county treasurer filed a motion to dismiss the action for failure to state a cause of action because the assessment was made by the state tax commission. The trial court held that the corporation should have exhausted the administrative remedies of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-6-8.2 (1953) and having failed to do so had no standing to file the action under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-5-4 (1953) and dismissed the action. The court held that if the tax was unconstitutional, as asserted by the corporation, there was no right or power in the state tax commission to assess it. The court determined that the exhaustion of administrative remedies provided by the statute was not a prerequisite to a refund action.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the cause to the district court with instructions to consider the constitutionality of allegations that the law upon which the tax assessment was based was unconstitutional.

Dikewood Corp. v. Bureau of Revenue


No. 7349


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


74 N.M. 75; 1964-NMSC-057; 390 P.2d 661; 1964 N.M. LEXIS 2135



March 23, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: March 23, 1964


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceeding on claim for refund of taxes paid under protest. The District Court, Santa Fe County, James M. Scarborough, D. J., entered judgment adverse to plaintiff, and plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, Chavez, J., held that Emergency School Tax Act exempting sellers of personal tangible property to federal government but not vendors of services to government did not violate constitutional right of a vendor of services to equal protection.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporate taxpayer sought review of the adverse judgment of the District Court, Santa Fe County (New Mexico), in its claim for refund of taxes paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: The corporation engaged in the business of supplying scientific consulting services to the federal government and paid sales tax to the State of New Mexico under protest. The district court concluded that the gross receipts which were the basis for the taxes paid under protest after were not exempt under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16-5 of the Emergency School Tax Act, that the exemption was constitutional; and that the corporation's claim was to be denied and dismissed. The corporation contended that since § 72-16-5 exempted those who sold personal tangible property to the government but did not exempt him as the vendor of services it was a violation of his constitutional rights under the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment of the U.S. Constitution, and N.M. Const. at. II, § 18. The court held that legislature intended to tax the privilege of conducting certain businesses as provided in §§ 72-16-4.1 to 72-16-4.13, and intended, as expressed in § 72-16-5, to exempt certain transactions. Inequalities which resulted from a singling out of one particular class for taxation or exemption, infringed no constitutional limitation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

State ex rel. Callaway v. Axtell


No. 7313


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


74 N.M. 339; 1964-NMSC-046; 393 P.2d 451; 1964 N.M. LEXIS 2227



March 9, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 15, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action to recover a gratuity paid by the state and subsequently determined to have been granted unconstitutionally. The District Court of Santa Fe County, Samuel Z. Montoya, D. J., sustained a motion to dismiss the complaint, and plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, Carmody, J., held that where state money was used together with matching federal funds to pay seller of feed furnished to farmers and ranchers in emergency, and statute appropriating state funds for such purpose was subsequently held unconstitutional as donation of public funds, state could recover amounts so paid, notwithstanding good faith of payment and receipt.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State of New Mexico (state) challenged a decision of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which, in the state's action to recover money used to pay for feed that was furnished to defendant farmers, sustained the farmers' motion to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The farmers were the recipients of hay and roughage that was paid for by the state and federal governments under the Cooperative Roughage Emergency Program. The use of state money for the benefit of private individuals who were not destitute was found to be unconstitutional. Subsequently, the attorney general made demand upon the farmers for restitution of the monies that they had received under the program. When restitution was not made, the state filed an action to recover the money. The farmers filed a motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim. The trial court granted the motion. On appeal, the court reversed and held: (1) the farmers received a gratuity, not of the funds but only the benefit therefrom, under the cooperative agreement between the state and the federal government; (2) public monies were trust funds belonging to the people, and were required to be reimbursed by the recipients if they were paid out illegally by a public official, even though in good faith; and (3) whether the benefit was "in cash or in kind" made no difference, as the fact that it was an outright donation made it unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's order that dismissed the state's action to recover money used to pay for feed that was furnished to the farmers.

City of Santa Fe v. Gamble-Skogmo, Inc.


No. 7327


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


73 N.M. 410; 1964-NMSC-016; 389 P.2d 13; 1964 N.M. LEXIS 2090



January 27, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: January 27, 1964


PRIOR HISTORY: Defendants were convicted in the District Court, Santa Fe County, Edwin L. Swope, D. J., of violation of building code and they appealed. The Supreme Court, Noble, J., held that regulation in zoning ordinance pertaining to size of windows in construction or alteration of buildings within historic area of Sante Fe as part of preservation of "Old Sante Fe Style" of architecture, was valid exercise of police power granted to city.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant owners appealed from a decision of the District Court, Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which convicted them of violating the building code in their remodeling of a building within the historic area of Santa Fe.


OVERVIEW: The owners obtained a permit pursuant to the city building code to remodel a building within the historical zone in Santa Fe. After completion of the remodeled building, but before plaintiff city's approval, the owners removed the dividers leaving large show windows contrary to the city ordinance and the building permit. The district court convicted them of the building code violation. The owners claimed that there was a lack of enabling legislation authorizing such an exercise of the police power by the city. The court affirmed the judgment and sentence. The court held that the purpose of the Santa Fe historical zoning ordinance was within the term "general welfare," as used in the municipal zoning enabling legislation. The court found that the general welfare of the community and the state was enhanced by the historic features and culture. The court held that regulation of the size of window panes in the construction or alteration of buildings within the historic area of Santa Fe, as a part of the preservation of the "Old Santa Fe Style" of architecture, was a valid exercise of the police power granted to the city.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of the owners for violating the building code in their remodeling of a building within the historic area.

State v. Tipton


No. 7265


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


73 N.M. 24; 1963-NMSC-175; 385 P.2d 355; 1963 N.M. LEXIS 2026



September 23, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: September 23, 1963


PRIOR HISTORY: Convicted, in the District Court, Curry County, E. T. Hensley, Jr., D. J., as a second felony offender, after he had pleaded guilty to rape charge, defendant appealed. The Supreme Court, Noble, J., held, inter alia, that the indeterminate sentence law did not repeal by implication the habitual criminal act.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the District Court of Curry County (New Mexico), which enhanced his sentence for conviction of a second felony as provided by the habitual criminal act under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-16-1 (1953). Defendant pled guilty to rape of a female, having previously been convicted of statutory rape. Defendant contended that § 41-16-1 was repealed by implication.


OVERVIEW: The validity of the habitual criminal act was challenged on the ground that 1955 N.M. Laws ch. 150, the indeterminate sentence law, repealed N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-16-1 (1953) by implication. In addition, defendant asserted that the increased penalty for a second felony conviction could not be applied under the language of the indeterminate sentence statute; and, that N.M. Stat. § 41-17-1 repealed N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-16-1 (1953) by implication. The court affirmed. The court held that there was no obstacle imposed by the indeterminate sentence law to complying with the provisions of § 41-16-1. Further, the court was unable to agree with defendant's argument that the indeterminate sentence law, the later legislative enactment, related to the same subject matter, or was one fully covering the subject matter of, the habitual criminal statute. The court held that the indeterminate sentence law merely provided that the sentencing judge should impose the minimum and maximum sentence that was provided by law. The court noted that the increased penalty that was provided by the habitual criminal statute was the penalty that was provided by law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, City of Albuquerque, City Commission of the City of Albuquerque, and members of the city commission, sought review of a judgment entered in the District Court, Bernalillo County (New Mexico) in favor of appellee landowners in the landowners' action for review by petition for writ of certiorari of the city commission's affirmance of the planning commission's denial of the landowners' petition to re-zone their property.


OVERVIEW: The landowners petitioned the planning commission for a zone change from "historical" to "commercial." The planning commission denied the request and the landowners appealed the denial to the city commission. When the city commission affirmed the planning commission's decision, the landowners filed a petition for writ of certiorari with the district court under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 14-18-16 for review of the city commission's refusal to re-zone. On appeal of the district court's judgment deleting the landowners' property from the historic zone, appellants argued that the district court was without jurisdiction to review the denial of the landowners' request for re-zoning. The court affirmed the judgment and ruled that the district court's action was to review the action of the city commission sitting for the purpose of hearing and deciding appeals and was permitted under § 14-18-16. The court also ruled that the writ of certiorari as provided in § 14-18-16 was an express grant of a means to allow the landowners to contest the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment in favor of the landowners in the landowners' action for review by petition for writ of certiorari of the city commission's affirmance of the planning commission's denial of the landowners' petition to re-zone their property.

State Highway Comm'n v. Ruidoso Tel. Co.


No. 6957


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


73 N.M. 487; 1963-NMSC-150; 389 P.2d 606; 1963 N.M. LEXIS 2093



August 19, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 9, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: Declaratory judgment action to determine the liability, as between highway commission and telephone utility company, for the cost of relocating telephone lines in connection with the widening of highway right-of-way. The District Court, Santa Fe County, Samuel Z. Montoya, D. J., held that the telephone utility had a valid prescriptive easement as to certain of the poles but no valid easement as to others and appeals and cross-appeals were taken. The Supreme Court, George L. Reese, Jr., D. J., held that the telephone utility's placement of its poles on private land had served to create valid easements in its favor even though the utility had not compensated the landowners prior to the placement of the poles and that the Highway Commission was therefore liable for the cost of moving the poles.



DISPOSITION: Judgment accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a state highway commission, sought a declaratory judgment as to the liability for the cost of relocating the telephone lines of defendant, a telephone utility company, in connection with the widening of highway right-of-way. The District Court, Santa Fe County (New Mexico) held that the company had a valid prescriptive easement as to a certain section of the lines, but no valid easement as to another. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The commission refused to reimburse the company for the relocation of a portion of its lines and facilities within the old right of way unless the company proved a valid title or property interest superseding the commission's right of way. The company asserted that by reason of its power of eminent domain, it had valid easements covering the entire disputed portion of its lines and facilities located on private lands outside the old right of way. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part, holding that the company had valid easements for the entire disputed portion of the lines. The court found that the commission had notice of the occupancy and rights of the company and took its right of way easements subject to the burden of the right of the company to maintain its lines on the lands in question. The commission was in no position to claim any damages which the previous landowners could have suffered because knowledge of the previous owners of the construction of the company's lines on their line could be properly inferred, and only the previous owners had the right to damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment as to the portion of the lines that were held to be a valid easement and reversed as to the portion of the lines that were held to not be a valid easement. The court remanded to the trial court with directions to enter judgment in favor of the company.

State ex rel. Interstate Stream Comm'n v. Reynolds


No. 7204


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


71 N.M. 389; 1963-NMSC-023; 378 P.2d 622; 1963 N.M. LEXIS 1893



February 5, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: February 5, 1963


PRIOR HISTORY: Action brought on relation of the Interstate Stream Commission to test the validity of statutes appropriating reservoir trust funds. The District Court, Santa Fe County, James M. Scarborough, D. J., rendered a judgment upholding the statute and the plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, Compton, C. J., held, inter alia, that the Ferguson Act, granting lands to New Mexico territory for establishment of permanent water reservoirs for irrigating purposes, provided funds for establishment of permanent sources of water for irrigation purposes so as to include permanent regulation of use of water stored naturally or coming directly from natural sources as well as establishment of other permanent reservoirs, and the act permitted expenditure of trust funds to construct, improve or repair existing facilities established to utilize water by diverting it from its natural sources.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Interstate Stream Commission (Commission) appealed from a decision of the District Court, Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which upheld the validity of statutes, 1961 N.M. Laws Chapters 181, 182 and 183, appropriating reservoir trust funds.


OVERVIEW: The Commission brought an action to enjoin the State Engineer from expending the funds appropriated to him on the ground that the appropriations violated the provisions of the Ferguson Act of June 21, 1898, 30 Stat. 484, and the New Mexico Constitution. The Commission contended the appropriations were void as a breach of the trust imposed by the Ferguson Act as they were for purposes, such as maintenance, other than those for which the grant was made and for which the fund was created, which was establishment of reservoirs. The court held that the term "establishment" as used in the Ferguson Act included the permanent regulation of use of water stored naturally or coming directly from natural sources as well as the establishment of other permanent reservoirs. Th court concluded that the appropriations were not in violation of neither N.M. Const. art. IV, §§ 24, 26, 31, nor N.M. Const. art. IX, § 14. The appropriation legislation did not constitute inappropriate special laws, did not impermissibly benefit any corporation, did not impermissibly benefit charitable organizations not under the control of the state, and did not constitute a donation to any corporation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

City of Albuquerque v. Reynolds


No. 7013


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


71 N.M. 428; 1962-NMSC-173; 379 P.2d 73; 1962 N.M. LEXIS 1524



December 14, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 15, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: The city of Albuquerque applied to the state engineer for permits to appropriate underground waters from the Rio Grande underground water basin. The city appealed from the decision of the state engineer. The District Court, Bernalillo County, D. A. Macpherson, Jr., District Judge, rendered judgment, and the state engineer appealed. The Supreme Court, Geo. L. Reese, Jr., District Judge, held that district court had no jurisdiction to adjudicate pueblo water right claim of city and that state engineer could impose suitable conditions so as to permit such taking as would not result in impairment of rights of river appropriators.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of District Court reversed and matter remanded to that court with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State Engineer of New Mexico (engineer), sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which reversed the engineer's decision denying plaintiff city's applications to appropriate water from an underground basin.


OVERVIEW: The city filed applications with the engineer for permits to appropriate water from an underground basin. The water the city sought to appropriate was part of the base flow of the Rio Grande River. The engineer denied the applications, finding that the granting of such permits would impair the existing rights of prior appropriators of the river water. The district court reversed, finding that the city held ancient pueblo water rights that granted it an absolute and unconditional right to divert as much of the surface and underground water of the Rio Grande as was necessary for its use and the use of its inhabitants. The engineer appealed. The court reversed, holding (1) the district court did not have jurisdiction to adjudicate the city's pueblo water rights because the issue was not before the engineer, (2) the engineer had the authority to consider the effects on surface rights holders of the appropriation of water from an underground basin, (3) the engineer had the authority to require the city to retire certain surface water rights as a precondition to granting the permits, and (4) the water rights of a municipality were subject to the state's regulatory authority.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court and remanded the matter to the district court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

323 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Gray v. Armijo


No. 6874


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


70 N.M. 245; 1962-NMSC-082; 372 P.2d 821; 1962 N.M. LEXIS 1578



June 18, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: June 18, 1962


PRIOR HISTORY: Original prohibition proceeding after the District Court overruled petitioners' motion to quash service of process. The Supreme Court, Chavez, J., held that statute which would subject motorist who moved from state prior to commencement of an action arising from automobile accident to jurisdiction of state's courts and which was passed almost two years after the accident but prior to commencement of the action, was procedural in nature and could therefore be applied retroactively.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and writ of prohibition set aside and ordered discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner nonresident vehicle owners filed a petition for writ of prohibition against respondent judge of the Fourth Judicial District Court of the State of New Mexico, which overruled their motion to quash service of process in an action for damages arising out of an automobile accident that occurred on New Mexico highways at a time when the nonresident vehicle owners were New Mexico residents. The court issued an alternative writ.


OVERVIEW: The nonresident vehicle owners were involved in an automobile accident on New Mexico highways at a time when they were New Mexico residents. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 21-3-16 (1953 Comp.), which subjected the nonresident vehicle owners to the jurisdiction of the New Mexico courts, was enacted after the accident. Thereafter, an action arising from the accident was commenced against the nonresident vehicle owners after they had moved out of New Mexico. The district court judge overruled the nonresident vehicle owners' motion to quash service of process. In a proceeding for a writ of prohibition, the court held that § 21-3-16 was procedural in nature and could therefore be applied retroactively. Section 21-3-16, with one immaterial exception, was adopted verbatim from Illinois. The court presumed that the New Mexico Legislature, in adopting the statute, also adopted the prior construction of the statute by the highest courts of Illinois, which held that the Illinois act merely established a new mode of obtaining jurisdiction of the person of a defendant in order to secure existing rights, and that the Illinois act was applicable to rights of action which arose before the act was adopted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court judge's decision overruling the nonresident vehicle owners' motion to quash service of process. The court set aside the writ of prohibition and ordered that it be discharged.

Bradbury & Stamm Constr. Co. v. Bureau of Revenue


No. 7105


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


70 N.M. 226; 1962-NMSC-078; 372 P.2d 808; 1962 N.M. LEXIS 1576



June 11, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: June 11, 1962


PRIOR HISTORY: Action involving constitutionality of statute providing exemption of certain sales to the United States, the State and non-profit organizations from payment of the emergency school taxes. From a judgment of the District Court, Sante Fe County, James M. Scarborough, D. J., the plaintiffs appealed and defendants cross-appealed. The Supreme Court, Noble, J., held, inter alia, that allegedly invalid section of statute relating to gross receipts from contract for particular project entered into prior to effective date of statute is severable from remainder, and remainder is constitutional, and that the imposition of the tax upon one rendering services to the United States does not constitute a prohibited tax to the United States.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and in part remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractors challenged the judgment of the District Court of Sante Fe County (New Mexico), which held that one portion of a statute imposing a sales tax was unconstitutional, but that said portion was severable and remainder of the statute lawfully imposed a tax on the contractors. The contractors had paid the tax under protest to appellee state and sought a refund.


OVERVIEW: The contractors challenged the constitutionality of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16-5 (1953), and the lower court determined that one section of the statute was invalid but severable. Because the remainder of the statute still required the contractors to pay the tax, they appealed the severability of the section. The court affirmed and held that the section was severable, leaving the remainder of the statute intact. The court held that the deletion of the offending subsection in no way affected the enforceability of the other portions of the statute. The other section were clear, certain, and unambiguous, and they were not so connected either in subject or purpose with the invalid portions that the legislature would not have enacted the remainder if it had known that the one subsection was invalid. The court found no merit to the contractors' contention that the statute had the effect of levying an unconstitutional tax upon the United States, its agencies, or departments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that held that the constitutional portions of the statute were severable and enforceable. The court remanded in part to allow one appellant proper interest on its judgment.

Cont'l Oil Co. v. Oil Conservation Comm'n


No. 6830


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


70 N.M. 310; 1962-NMSC-062; 373 P.2d 809; 1962 N.M. LEXIS 1592; 18 Oil & Gas Rep. 69



May 16, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 20, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceedings on application for change of gas proration formula. The District Court, Lea County, John R. Brand, D. J., affirmed the commission's order, and an appeal was taken. The Supreme Court, Carmody, J., held that the commission's order lacked basic findings necessary to, and upon which, its jurisdiction depended; that commission should have been permitted to participate in appeal to district court; and that district court should not have admitted additional evidence.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, various natural gas companies, sought review of the order of the District Court, Lea County (New Mexico), which affirmed the order by appellee, the Oil Conservation Commission, in the action by appellees, various pipeline companies, seeking a change of the gas proration formula.


OVERVIEW: Following the application of a gas company, the commission made a change to the gas proration formula. The natural gas companies argued that the commission's order was unlawful and unreasonable in depriving them of their property without due process of law. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the commission's order was invalid and void because it lacked the basic findings necessary to, and upon which, its jurisdiction depended. Although formal and elaborate findings were not absolutely necessary, basic jurisdictional findings, supported by evidence, were required to show that the commission followed the law. The court found that the commission should have been permitted to participate in the appeal to the trial court. Because the commission was a necessary adverse party, it was error for the trial court to refuse to allow the commission to participate. The trial court erred in allowing additional evidence in an effort to determine whether the commission had exceeded its delegated authority. Admission of such testimony, outside of the record of that received by the commission, was improper in that the trial court was substituting its judgment for that of the commission.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court affirming the commission's order.
