N.M. Bd. of Examiners in Optometry v. Roberts


No. 7001


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


70 N.M. 90; 1962-NMSC-053; 370 P.2d 811; 1962 N.M. LEXIS 1548



April 11, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: April 11, 1962


PRIOR HISTORY: Action to enjoin resident newspaper and radio stations from disseminating advertising submitted by optometrist residing in adjoining state. The District Court, Lea County, John R. Brand, D. J., granted injunction, and the newspaper and radio stations appealed. The Supreme Court, Compton, C. J., held that state statute prohibiting price advertising in field of optometry was not superseded by and did not conflict with federal legislation relating to advertising in interstate commerce.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court, Lea County granted plaintiff optometry board's application to perpetually enjoin and restrain defendants, a newspaper and radio stations, from accepting, disseminating and publishing advertising of any nature from an out of state optometrist that quoted prices or discounts. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: N.M. Stat. Ann. § 67-7-13 prohibited any person from advertising the prices or terms on eyeglasses or optometric devices. Defendants accepted advertising from an optometrist whose office was located in another state. Defendants argued that § 67-7-13 was an unconstitutional obstruction on interstate commerce. The trial court found that the statute was not unconstitutional, and the court affirmed. State action affecting interstate commerce was precluded if it directly burdened interstate commerce, conflicted with federal regulations, or if Congress had evidenced an intent to completely pre-empt the area of regulation involved. The court found that there was no pre-emption by Congress of the entire field of advertising in interstate commerce and that there was no conflict between the state statute and federal legislation relating to false advertising. Further, § 37-7-13 did not obstruct interstate commerce because it did not stop the newspaper or radio stations from publishing their advertising in interstate commerce or even prohibit advertising of optometric goods either within the state or in interstate commerce. The statute merely restricted the manner of advertising.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Melfi v. Goodman

SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


69 N.M. 488; 1962-NMSC-020; 368 P.2d 582; 1962 N.M. LEXIS 1468

DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded with directions.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a decision of the District Court of Lincoln County (New Mexico), which entered an order quashing personal service made outside the state on defendant, a non-resident, pursuant to N.M. Comp. Stat. § 21-3-16(A)(1) (1953).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was a large shareholder in a corporation, against which defendant held a judgment. Plaintiff, desiring to protect the corporation from execution, entered into an agreement with defendant in the state to purchase the judgment. The initial payment was made in the state. Subsequently, the corporation defaulted in interest payments to plaintiff, and as a result of which defendant threatened to execute on the judgment, though plaintiff was not in default on the deferred payments. Plaintiff instituted an action to enjoin the threatened acts of defendant but the trial court quashed service of process. In reversing the trial court's decision, the court held that § 21-3-16(A)(1) was constitutional. State ex rel. Lee v. Hartman


No. 7034


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


69 N.M. 419; 1961-NMSC-171; 367 P.2d 918; 1961 N.M. LEXIS 1668



December 19, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: December 19, 1961


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding in mandamus to determine whether Director of Department of Finance and Administration had authority to reduce lawful appropriations made to the Oil and Gas Accounting Commission. The Supreme Court, Moise, J., held that the Director did not have authority to make such reductions.



DISPOSITION: Peremptory writ of mandamus issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator Executive Director of the Oil and Gas Accounting Commission brought an original proceeding in mandamus to determine whether respondent Director of Department of Finance and Administration had the authority to reduce lawful appropriations made to the Oil and Gas Accounting Commission.


OVERVIEW: The relator sought a determination of whether respondent was legally empowered to reduce the budget of the Commission, so as to provide for the expenditure of a lesser amount than was appropriated to the Commission for a specific fiscal year in the General Appropriation Act passed by the 1961 legislature and duly approved by the Governor. After consideration of the facts and the law, the court granted the relator's writ. The court held that respondent's actions were illegal and unconstitutional in that neither in the state constitution nor in any statute had respondent been granted the power to reduce a lawfully made appropriation. The court ruled that respondent could not refuse approval without some basis, and if the budget as submitted was within the amounts appropriated and the items were proper, he was given no discretion except to approve them. The court rejected respondent's argument that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 11-4-1.6 (1953) gave him authority to prevent any agency from expending the full amount of money appropriated to it inasmuch as the budget division could have approved a budget in a sum less than the total appropriated.


OUTCOME: The court issued the peremptory writ of mandamus.

State ex rel. Holmes v. State Bd. of Fin.

DISPOSITION: Writ made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, the Chief Tax Commissioner, State Tax Commission of New Mexico, filed a petition for a writ of prohibition commanding respondent, the State Board of Finance of the State of New Mexico, to refrain from cutting or reducing budget of State Tax Commission.


OVERVIEW: The Board relied on the provisions of § 24, Chap. 254, N.M.S.L. 1961, which authorized the board to reduce all annual operating budgets not to exceed 10 percent subject to certain exceptions, in proposing to reduce the Commissioner's annual operating budget. The Commissioner filed a petition for a writ of prohibition commanding the Board to refrain from cutting or reducing the budget. The court granted the Commissioner's petition, and issued the writ, holding that the statute relied upon by the Board was unconstitutional. The court found that the unrestricted and unguided power contained in the statute was an unconstitutional grant to the Board of a legislative power. The statute purported to delegate legislative powers to reduce appropriations to the executive and such powers were non-delegable under N.M. Const. art. IV, § 22 and N.M. Const. art. III, § 1.

Hockett v. Chapman


No. 6968


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


69 N.M. 324; 1961-NMSC-163; 366 P.2d 850; 1961 N.M. LEXIS 1659



November 27, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: November 27, 1961


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by injured workman against his coemployees. The District Court, San Juan County, C. C. McCulloh, D. J., dismissed the complaint, and the plaintiff and intervenor appealed. The Supreme Court, Compton, C. J., held that injured employee's coemployees were "persons other than the employer", within statute permitting injured workman to recover from such persons.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee and intervenor, the employer's insurer, sought review of a judgment from the District Court, San Juan County (New Mexico), which dismissed the employee's personal injury action against defendant co-employees as barred on the ground that the employee had received workmen's compensation benefits for his injuries, which were received in an accident that arose out of and in the course of his employment.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured as the result of a collision between a truck driven by his fellow employee in which he was a passenger and a truck driven by another fellow employee. The accident arose out of and in the course of their employment. The employee received workmen's compensation benefits and thereafter brought a negligence action against his co-employees. The employer's insurer intervened. On appeal of a judgment dismissing the employee's complaint, the court reversed. The co-employees were persons other than the employer against whom a negligence action could be maintained pursuant to the Workmen's Compensation Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 59-10-4(F) and 59-10-25. The action was not barred by the provisions of N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 59-10-5 and 59-10-6, as those provisions dealt only with the exclusiveness of the remedy between the employer and the employee. Therefore, the trial court erred in dismissing the negligence action against the co-employees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment with directions to the trial court to proceed in a manner not inconsistent with the views expressed in its opinion.

Clovis Nat'l Bank v. Callaway


No. 6825


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


69 N.M. 119; 1961-NMSC-129; 364 P.2d 748; 1961 N.M. LEXIS 1618



August 30, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: August 30, 1961


PRIOR HISTORY: Several national banks brought suit against the State Treasurer to prevent enforcement of the Uniform Disposition of Unclaimed Property Act. The District Court, Santa Fe County, James M. Scarborough, D. J., rendered a judgment that the act was constitutional in part and unconstitutional in part, and the banks appealed, and the State Treasurer cross-appealed. The Supreme Court, Moise, J., held that the act, insofar as it relates to the transfer of custody of abandoned property from banks to State Treasurer, is not unconstitutional, on ground that notice provided for in the act is insufficient to meet the requirements of due process.



DISPOSITION: Cause remanded with instructions to vacate judgment and enter new one in conformance with opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant national banks challenged the decision from the District Court, Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which held the Uniform Disposition of Unclaimed Property Act (Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 22-22-1 to 22-22-29 (1953), was constitutional in part and unconstitutional in part. Appellee treasurer cross-appealed the trial court's determination that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-22-24 (1953) was unconstitutional as applied to the national banks.


OVERVIEW: The national banks doing business in New Mexico, sought an injunction for themselves and all others similarly situated to prevent enforcement of the Act, alleging that it was unconstitutional, and also that it attempted to authorize visitorial powers by a state official over a national bank in violation of 12 U.S.C.S. § 484 of the National Banking Act. On appeal, the national banks asserted, among other things, that the Act was unconstitutional because the notice provided for in the Act was insufficient to meet the requirements of due process. The court remanded, holding that (1) the provision for escheat after the passage of 40 years added in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-22-20 (1953) was nothing more than a means of depriving the owners of property because of the passage of time without a claim thereto being asserted; (2) the last sentence of § 22-22-20 must be ruled invalid where there was a total absence of any provisions for notice of the escheat, and no opportunity whatsoever to appear and oppose the same; and (3) the trial court erred in finding that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-22-24 (1953) was unconstitutional as applied to national banks because of the provision 12 U.S.C.S. § 484.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to vacate the judgment appealed from and enter a new one conforming with the court's findings.

State ex rel. Albuquerque v. Lavender

SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


69 N.M. 220; 1961-NMSC-096; 365 P.2d 652; 1961 N.M. LEXIS 1638



July 13, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 3, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding in mandamus to require the highway commission to reimburse a city for water and sewer line, relocations necessitated by construction of federal-aid highways. The Supreme Court, Carmody, J., held that the statute requiring the state to pay in certain cases the nonbetterment costs of utility relocations necessitated by highway improvements is not a release of an obligation to the state and does not violate the constitutional prohibition against state aid to private enterprise.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ made absolute.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the state of New Mexico and the city of Albuquerque, brought a writ of mandamus to require respondents, the New Mexico state highway commission, commission members, and the commission's chief highway engineer, to reimburse petitioner city for the relocation of water and sewer lines, made necessary by reason of the construction of federal-aid highways on the interstate and primary system.


OVERVIEW: The New Mexico legislature enacted 1957 N.M. Laws 237, which provided for reimbursement to public utilities for the relocation of their facilities. The court later declared portions of Chapter 237 unconstitutional, but failed to rule on whether petitioner city was entitled to repayment of relocation costs, which it had by reason of moving municipally owned facilities from its municipally owned right of way. Petitioners brought a writ of mandamus to recoup funds spent these relocation costs. The legislature had passed 1959 N.M. Laws 310 that authorized the commission itself to expend public funds for the relocation of utility facilities. Chapter 310 also stated that the utility, as to relocations, was under the absolute control of the commission and was merely acting as a contractor for the state. The court granted the writ and made it absolute, holding that under Chapter 310 there was a legitimate and equitable apportionment of costs of relocations rather than a donation to utility companies. The court found Chapter 310 constitutional, but overruled State Highway Commission v. Southern Union Gas Co., 1958, 65 N.M. 84, 332 P.2d 1007.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus and made it absolute.

State ex rel. Reynolds v. Mendenhall


No. 6768


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


68 N.M. 467; 1961-NMSC-083; 362 P.2d 998; 1961 N.M. LEXIS 1574



June 26, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: June 26, 1961


PRIOR HISTORY: Statutory suit for adjudication of rights to water in the Roswell Artesian Basin. The District Court, Chaves County, E. T. Hensley, Jr., D. J., made an order from which an appeal was taken. The Supreme Court, Moise, J., held that a landowner who lawfully initiated development of an underground water right and carried it to completion with reasonable diligence acquired a water right with a priority date as of the beginning of his work, notwithstanding the fact that the lands involved were put into a declared artesian basin before work was completed and water put to beneficial use on the ground.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners disputed an order by the District Court, Chaves County (New Mexico), which denied them any rights to water from an artesian basin. The court considered the effect of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 75-11-4 (1953) and whether the doctrine of relation applied so as to protect the landowners in any rights which they had initiated but which had not fully vested due to an order by a state engineer extending the basin to include their lands.


OVERVIEW: The water at issue was used for crop irrigation for several years before appellee State of New Mexico began the action. On appeal from a ruling that the landowners had no rights to the water, the court reviewed the history of the statutory underground water laws. In particular, the court noted that N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 75-11-1 to 75-11-10 (1953) included a declaration that public waters were subject to appropriation for beneficial use. The court held that the statutory law as it existed at the time in no way controlled or interfered with the landowners' right to undertake development and to complete the appropriation of the basin water. The court held that the substance and intent of § 75-11-4 (1953) was the same as that of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 75-8-1 (1953), originally enacted in 1907, which was held to recognize the doctrine of relation. Based on the doctrine, the court held that, because the landowners began drilling the well before the state engineer's order and proceeded diligently to develop the water, they acquired a valid water right before the order extending the basin, and that right was not affected by the order. The court reversed and remanded with instructions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the district court and remanded with instructions that the order denying the landowners rights to water from an artesian basin be set aside and a new order entered.

Airco Supply Co. v. Albuquerque Nat'l Bank


No. 6747


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


68 N.M. 195; 1961-NMSC-031; 360 P.2d 386; 1961 N.M. LEXIS 1514



March 15, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: March 15, 1961


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by depositor against bank to recover money paid on forged checks. The District Court, Bernalillo County, Robert W. Reidy, D. J., rendered judgment for bank, and plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, Compton, C. J., held that the evidence supported a finding that the depositor had been negligent, and that the depositor was barred by negligence and failure to give timely notice of the forgeries.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff depositor appealed the judgment of the District Court, Bernalillo County (New Mexico) entered for defendant bank in plaintiff's action against defendant bank to recover money paid on forged checks.


OVERVIEW: One of plaintiff's employees had checks made out to fictitious entities, which she then endorsed for deposit into her own account. The forgery scheme was not discovered until a year end audit even though plaintiff received cancelled checks and bank statements on a regular basis. The trial court ruled that defendant bank was entitled to charge the forged checks to plaintiff's account and plaintiff appealed. The court affirmed, saying that there was substantial evidence that plaintiff's negligence was the proximate cause of the loss. The general rule is that a bank paid checks at its peril, but defendant bank in this instance established its own due care and also established that plaintiff was negligent because plaintiff failed to review the cancelled checks it received or compare them to invoices. Although the burden was on the bank to establish the depositor's negligence in order to relieve the bank of liability, the burden was met by evidence that showed that no one at plaintiff's organization examined the checks.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for defendant bank because there was substantial evidence to support the trial court's findings that plaintiff depositor was negligent in its examination of cancelled checks and had failed to give timely notice of the forgeries.

Rocky Mt. Wholesale Co. v. Ponca Wholesale Mercantile Co.


No. 6781


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


68 N.M. 228; 1961-NMSC-015; 360 P.2d 643; 1961 N.M. LEXIS 1521



February 8, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 12, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action under the Cigarette Fair Trade Act to enjoin a wholesaler from selling cigarettes below cost. From an adverse judgment of the District Court, Bernalillo County, John B. McManus, Jr., D. J., the defendant appealed. The Supreme Court, Noble, J., held that the Act was a reasonable attempt by the state, for the general welfare, to protect free competition, bore a reasonable relationship to the legislative purpose, and was not arbitrary or discriminatory.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant wholesaler appealed a judgment issued by a district court (New Mexico) that permanently enjoined it from selling cigarettes below cost, arguing that the New Mexico Cigarette Fair Trade Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 49-3-1 to 49-3-14 (1953), unreasonably interfered with private property rights, had no reasonable relation to the public welfare, and violated N.M Const. art. II, §§ 4, 18, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff wholesaler filed suit under the New Mexico Cigarette Fair Trade Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 49-3-1 to 49-3-14 (1953), to enjoin defendant wholesaler from selling cigarettes to consumers below cost. The district court permanently enjoined defendant from selling cigarettes at a price less than its cost, finding that plaintiff had been harmed by defendant's practices. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the Act. In affirming, the court concluded that the Act was intended to prevent the formation of monopolies and anti-competitive trade. The State was free to adopt laws that furthered this purpose without violating due process. The prevention of monopolies, the fostering of fair competition, and the prohibition of unfair trade practices promoted the public welfare. The Act was not price-fixing legislation but merely prohibited the sale of cigarettes at below cost. The Act was not arbitrary or discriminatory, even though it permitted one wholesaler to sell to another wholesaler below cost but denied wholesalers the right to sell below cost to retailers privileged to buy direct from the manufacturer. N.M. Stat. Ann. §49-3-3(b) (1953) was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

Patton v. Fortuna Corp.


No. 6664


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


68 N.M. 40; 1960-NMSC-136; 357 P.2d 1090; 1960 N.M. LEXIS 1249



December 29, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: December 29, 1960


PRIOR HISTORY: Action seeking a declaration that the state racing statutes were unconstitutional, and for certain injunctive relief. The District Court, Dona Ana County, Samuel Z. Montoya, D. J., made a determination adverse to plaintiffs and they appealed. The Supreme Court, Carmody, J., held that where plaintiffs' case was based upon claimed unconstitutionality of statute legalizing pari-mutuel betting under fixed conditions, and their complaint did not allege in what manner, if any, plaintiffs were adversely affected thereby, they were without standing to question the constitutionality of the statute.



DISPOSITION: Action of lower court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of the adverse judgment from the District Court, Dona Ana County (New Mexico), which rejected their challenge to the constitutionality of state racing statutes and sought injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed suit, seeking a declaration that the state racing statutes were unconstitutional and an injunction barring defendant from using certain premises for pari-mutuel betting on horse racing. The trial court ruled against plaintiffs, who appealed. Upon review, the court noted that the case was based upon the claimed unconstitutionality of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 60-6-6 (1953), the statute legalizing pari-mutuel betting under fixed conditions. Because the foundation of plaintiffs' case was based upon the unconstitutionality of the statute and their complaint failed to allege in what manner, if any, they were adversely affected, the court held that plaintiffs lacked standing to question the constitutionality of the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

337 of 795 DOCUMENTS


City of Albuquerque v. Campbell


No. 6684


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


68 N.M. 75; 1960-NMSC-138; 358 P.2d 698; 1960 N.M. LEXIS 1252



December 29, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 6, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action against city for personal injuries arising out of an accident involving a dump truck owned by city and driven by city employee. The District Court, Bernalillo County, John B. McManus, Jr., D. J., dismissed the action and plaintiffs appealed. The Supreme Court, Moise, J., held that city was a "political subdivision" within statute which provided for liability insurance on all vehicles owned by state and operated by employees, agents or officials of state, or any of its institutions, agencies or political subdivisions but which further provided that actions for damages resulting from operation of such vehicles should be brought against the driver and not against the state or its "political subdivisions", and that city was protected from suit.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of judgments from the District Court, Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which dismissed three separate personal injury actions against defendant city arising out of an accident involving a dump truck owned by the city and driven by a city employee. The trial court held that the provisions of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 64-25-9 (1953) protected the city from suit. The cases were consolidated for appeal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of the dismissal of their personal injury actions against the city, plaintiffs argued that § 64-25-9 did not apply to municipal corporations and that if it did apply, it was unconstitutional because the title did not meet the requirements of N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16. The court affirmed the judgment. The court found that the headings in both N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 64-25-8 and 64-25-9, which referred to "state vehicles," were not part of the law but were merely descriptive. The court held that municipal corporations were political subdivisions of the state and therefore, the personal injury action could not be maintained against the city under the statutes. The court also held that the use of the term "state" in the title of the act creating the statutes did not render it unconstitutional under N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16. The act was neither a hodgepodge nor "log-rolling" legislation. The inclusion of political subdivisions of the state within the broader term "state" did not work surprise or fraud upon the legislature. Nor could the public fail to take notice that the components that made up the state were included in the term "state."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments dismissing the actions.

City of Clovis v. Crain


No. 6679


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


68 N.M. 10; 1960-NMSC-129; 357 P.2d 667; 1960 N.M. LEXIS 1245; 88 A.L.R.2d 1243



December 12, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: December 12, 1960


PRIOR HISTORY: Suit on debt by city to recover for garbage and sewer assessments or service fees. The District Court, Curry County, George T. Harris, D. J., entered judgment for city and defendants appealed. The Supreme Court, Chavez, J., held that municipality acted beyond scope of its authority in attempting to collect garbage assessments by bringing suit for debt upon a personal obligation against parties who refused to pay sums assessed, but that property owner, whose sewers had long since been paid for, could be compelled to help finance extensions of sewer system into new areas of municipality, and to help finance new sewage disposal facilities made necessary by such extensions.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with respect to garbage collection fees and affirmed with respect to sewage assessment and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owner sought review of a decision from the District Court, Curry County (New Mexico), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff city in its suit on a debt to recover for garbage and sewer assessments or service fees.


OVERVIEW: The city collected the garbage under garbage assessment rates set up by a city ordinance. The property owner was indebted to the city for unpaid garbage assessments and sewer assessments. The city filed suit on the debt. On appeal from a judgment in favor of the city, the court reversed with respect to the garbage assessments and affirmed with respect to the sewer assessments. The court held that N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 14-32-6 to 14-32-11 (1953) provided the exclusive procedure for the city to make and enforce assessments and therefore, the city's action at law had to be dismissed. The court rejected the property owner's argument that as a property owner whose sewers had long since been paid, she could not be compelled to help finance extensions of the sewer system into new areas of the city and to help finance new sewage disposal facilities made necessary by the extensions. The court held that § 14-40-38, which authorized such use of sewer assessment revenues by the city, was constitutional. The property owner did not meet her burden of proving that the sewer service charges were unreasonable and arbitrary. The sewer service charges were not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment with respect to the garbage collection fees and affirmed with respect to sewage assessment and remanded for proper action in conformity with its opinion.

Johnson v. Sanchez


No. 6517


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


67 N.M. 41; 1960-NMSC-029; 351 P.2d 449; 1960 N.M. LEXIS 1146



March 15, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 13, 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action against commissioner of motor vehicles to set aside six-month suspension of driver's license. The District Court, Eddy County, John R. Brand, D. J., sustained the suspension and extended the term from six months to one year but driver, who appealed and superseded the judgment pending the appeal, obtained a renewal license during the period of suspension. The Supreme Court, Carmody, J., held that evidence of a record of traffic violations was sufficient to sustain six-month suspension of license but court had no jurisdiction to enlarge the term of suspension and held, also, that commissioner was empowered to refuse to renew a driver's license in a proper case where to grant a renewal, would be to permit the avoidance of the consequences of suspension.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Eddy County (New Mexico) that sustained the six-month suspension of the driver's license, which was imposed by defendant motor vehicle commissioner, and that further extended the term of the suspension to one year.


OVERVIEW: The driver filed an action against the commissioner to set aside the six-month suspension of his driver's license. The commissioner imposed the suspension due to habitual reckless or negligent driving. On appeal, the district court sustained the suspension and extended the term from six months to one year. The driver appealed, and the district court's judgment was superseded after the driver furnished an appeal bond. While the case was pending, the driver filed a motion to dismiss the appeal on the ground that it was moot because his license had expired by its own terms. The driver also sought to have the district court's judgment be declared inadmissible in any future proceeding. The court remanded the case to the district court, with direction to set aside its judgment and to enter one sustaining the commissioner's order. The court held that the district court erred in enlarging the term of the suspension because such action was beyond its jurisdiction. The court stated that the driver's motion to dismiss his appeal was without merit because the commissioner had a definite and tangible standard to determine whether or not a driver was a habitual reckless or negligent driver.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the district court and directed it to set aside its judgment that extended the term of the suspension imposed by the commissioner with respect to the driver's license. The district court was further directed to enter an order sustaining the commissioner's original order of suspension.

State v. Roybal


No. 6638


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


66 N.M. 416; 1960-NMSC-012; 349 P.2d 332; 1960 N.M. LEXIS 1130

The Supreme Court, Compton, J., held that statute proscribing theft of equipment from motor vehicles was not unconstitutional on theory that it contravened section of the Constitution providing that no bill embracing more than one subject shall be passed, merely because act contained other than anti-theft provisions, in view of fact subject of the act was motor vehicles.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.

Ann. § 64-9-4(b). He was then charged with having been previously convicted of a felony; he admitted this fact and was sentenced to serve not less than two and a half years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was seen going empty-handed in the direction of the victim's car and returning from it with a tire and jack. He was found the next day, intoxicated, in another car with the tire and jack from the victim's car. His knife was found in the victim's car. The court affirmed, holding: (1) the jack was "equipment" within the meaning of the statute; (2) the State established the corpus delicti; (3) intoxication was not a defense to larceny; (4) N.M. Stat. Ann. § 64-9-4(b) did not violate N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16; and (5) § 41-16-4 was not void for indefiniteness and uncertainty, denying defendant due process in violation of N.M. Const. art. II, § 18.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Nelson v. Cox


No. 6691


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


66 N.M. 397; 1960-NMSC-005; 349 P.2d 118; 1960 N.M. LEXIS 1125



January 7, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: January 7, 1960


PRIOR HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding. The Supreme Court, Per Curiam, held that defendant was not deprived of a fair and impartial trial because the trial court in response to a question by the jury during the course of their deliberations read to the jury the constitutional provision and the laws concerning pardon and parole and that the fact that the defendant unsuccessfully attempted to disqualify the trial judge who participated on both trials and was unsuccessful in the attempt did not establish prejudice.



DISPOSITION: Writ discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner made a motion for a writ of habeas corpus after a decision of the District Court (New Mexico), which discharged an earlier motion for a writ of habeas corpus after the prisoner was convicted of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner appealed his first degree murder conviction to the U.S. Supreme Court. The U.S. Supreme court denied certiorari. The prisoner, who was awaiting execution on death row, then filed a motion for a writ of habeas corpus in the district court. The district court discharged the writ. The prisoner then filed another motion for a writ of habeas corpus with the court. The court discharged the writ holding that it was not error for a court to give a jury an instruction concerning pardon and parole, at the behest of the jury. To convict for felony murder, it was immaterial whether the homicide occurred before or after the felony. A judge was authorized to retry a case that was overturned on appeal absent any bias or prejudice. The court determined that the prisoner was not deprived of any constitutional right.


OUTCOME: The court discharged the prisoner's motion for a writ of habeas corpus after the prisoner was convicted of first degree murder.

In re Sedillo


No. 6564


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


66 N.M. 267; 1959-NMSC-095; 347 P.2d 162; 1959 N.M. LEXIS 980



November 24, 1959 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: November 24, 1959


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding asking that applicant on motion be granted a license to practice law. The Supreme Court, Carmody, J., held, inter alia, that the statute establishing educational requirements for admission to the bar which were less than those provided for by the Supreme Court Rule is an unconstitutional invasion of the judicial powers.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original proceeding before the court, applicant on motion brought a petition asking that he be granted a license to practice law.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court had adopted a rule that gave to the board of bar commissioners the power to determine and prescribe by rules the qualifications and requirements for admission to practice law. Pursuant to the authority granted, the commission promulgated certain rules, one of which provided that no person, other than those admitted on certificate from other states, would be granted a license to practice law in New Mexico or would be entitled to take examination for admission to the bar unless such person had graduated from a law school approved by the American Bar Association. The applicant was unable to meet the educational qualification imposed by the rule, but based his motion on N.M. Stat. Ann. § 18-1-26 (1953), which established educational requirements that were less stringent than those provided by the rule. The court held that the statute was an unconstitutional invasion of the judicial powers and ordered that the applicant's petition for admission be denied. Even if the statute were to be construed as permissive, the result would be the same because it would still be an act of the legislature seeking to have the court lower its standards under those provided by rule.


OUTCOME: The applicant's petition for admission was denied.

Thomson v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


No. 6570


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


66 N.M. 159; 1959-NMSC-072; 344 P.2d 171; 1959 N.M. LEXIS 953



September 14, 1959

The Supreme Court, Carmody, J., held that where all of county public schools had been consolidated with municipal school district, private or denominational schools or Girls' Welfare Home were not rural school rooms under jurisdiction of county school superintendent, and under statute he was entitled to no more compensation than $ 1 per year.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county school superintendent sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo, New Mexico that dismissed his claim to recover compensation against appellee Bernalillo County Board of County Commissioners, Bernalillo County Board of Education and the Albuquerque Board of Education (collectively "the Board").

The Board filed a motion to dismiss, which motion was granted. On appeal, the court ruled that the superintendent had no rural school room under his jurisdiction and was entitled to $ 1 per year for his salary. The court held that while the statute was incomplete, it was certainly not sufficiently vague and indefinite as to be unenforceable as to the $ 1 per year proviso.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that limited the superintendent's compensation to $ 1 per year.

Munroe v. Wall


No. 6496


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


66 N.M. 15; 1959-NMSC-054; 340 P.2d 1069; 1959 N.M. LEXIS 934



June 26, 1959 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: June 26, 1959


PRIOR HISTORY: Action under the Declaratory Judgment Act seeking a judicial determination of the legality of regulation promulgated by the Board of Trustees of a hospital. From an adverse judgment in the District Court, Roosevelt County, John R. Brand, D. J., the plaintiffs appealed. The Supreme Court, Carmody, J., held that the statutes respecting osteopathic physicians do not require a governing board of a public hospital to afford to osteopathic surgeons and physicians the same treatment as is given to doctors of medicine who are graduates of American Medical Association approved colleges.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, osteopathic doctors, filed an action under the Declaratory Judgment Act, N.M. Comp. Stat. § 22-6-1 et seq. (1953), seeking a judicial determination of the legality of a regulation promulgated by defendants, hospital trustees. The District Court of Roosevelt County (New Mexico) sustained the trustees' motion to dismiss on the ground that the complaint failed to state a cause of action. The doctors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The doctors argued that N.M. Comp. Stat. § 67-8-12 (1957) required the governing board of a public hospital to afford to osteopathic surgeons and physicians the same treatment as was given to doctors of medicine who were graduates of American Medical Association approved colleges or, in other words, that the legislature intended to place osteopathic physicians on the same footing as medical doctors in every respect. The court examined the history of the act, including amendments and repealed sections to reach a contrary position. A fair analysis of the statute in question would be that the first two paragraphs placed osteopaths on equal footing with medical doctors, but that the third paragraph reserved to the governing boards of public hospitals full control over the making of regulations to determine who should be on the staff, irrespective of the so-called equal rights given to osteopaths. If it were otherwise, there would have been no reason for the elimination of the "anti-discrimination" and "permissive removal from the staff" provisions of the 1947 law. The court held that the regulation was not unreasonable nor arbitrary nor contrary to the statutes New Mexico.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

State ex rel. Oil Conservation Comm'n v. Brand


No. 6483


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


65 N.M. 384; 1959-NMSC-038; 338 P.2d 113; 1959 N.M. LEXIS 917; 10 Oil & Gas Rep. 958



April 15, 1959 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: April 15, 1959


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceeding invoking original jurisdiction of the Supreme Court, wherein relators sought a writ prohibiting a district judge from receiving any evidence in a case involving an appeal from the oil conservation commission, other than the record as heard before the commission. The Supreme Court, Carmody, J., held that record did not establish that relators' remedy by appeal was so inadequate or that error, if it occurred, would work such irreparable mischief, or cause such extraordinary hardship, costly delays or highly unusual burdens of expense, that Supreme Court, in the exercise of its superintending control over district court, should issue a writ prohibiting district judge from taking such a course of action.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ of prohibition discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the State of New Mexico and others, applied for a writ of prohibition seeking to preclude respondent, a district court judge, from receiving any evidence in a case involving an appeal from a decision of petitioner Oil Conservation Commission.


OVERVIEW: The Oil Conservation Commission held hearings concerning the proration of gas production. After the commission entered its final order ,various operators who objected to the order petitioned for judicial review. During a pretrial conference, the district court ruled that the operators would be permitted to offer proof that was not available to the commission in order that it might determine whether the commission's order was proper. Following this announcement, the State of New Mexico, the commission, and others petitioned for a writ of prohibition to preclude the district court judge from receiving additional evidence. A temporary writ issued, and the matter proceeded for hearing. In discharging the temporary writ, the court concluded that it would not exercise superintending control over the district court to prevent it from error. The fact that the district court might be on the verge of wrongly deciding a matter before it was of no concern to the court, nor was it material that it might, on review, be compelled to reverse the case.


OUTCOME: The temporary writ of prohibition was discharged as improvidently issued.

 

346 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Mt. States Tel. & Tel. Co. v. State Corp. Comm'n


No. 6473


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


65 N.M. 365; 1959-NMSC-035; 337 P.2d 943; 1959 N.M. LEXIS 914



April 9, 1959 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: April 9, 1959


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceeding on telephone company's application for removal of Corporation Commission's order suspending effective date of new tariffs sought by telephone company relative to some eight communities, for 90 days or until determination of reasonableness and lawfulness of rate. The Supreme Court, Carmody, J., held that where telephone company applied for increase in telephone rates for some eight communities and after statement of telephone company's position and without any witnesses testifying or exhibits introduced Commission ordered suspension of new tariffs pending state wide rate investigation, action of Commission was without any hearing whatsoever and in violation of constitutional mandate and hence suspension order could not be enforced.



DISPOSITION: Ordered accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner utility applied for a removal to the court of the matter of its proposed new tariffs for the adjustment of telephone rates with respect to eight communities. On the same day, respondent New Mexico Corporation Commission entered its order of removal. The Commission had entered an order directing an investigation of the rates throughout the State of New Mexico, and suspended the proposed tariffs pending its later determination.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the Commission's order of suspension was within its authority under N.M. Const. art. XI. The Commission based its order upon a rule that it had adopted permitting the suspension of rates. The court determined that it had jurisdiction over the case as a "prospective refusal" on the part of the utility to obey the order, which was an equivalent of a failure or refusal to obey the order. The court opined that during the entire day that the matter was before the Commission for a hearing, not a single witness was sworn, nor was any evidence of any nature submitted to or by the Commission. In the court's view, that was not the full and complete hearing contemplated by N.M. Const. art. XI, § 8, and the order of the Commission could not be enforced. Further, the provision in the Commission's rule allowing for suspension of rates was a substantive matter that the Commission was without power to exercise under the New Mexico Constitution. Before the entry of any order of suspension, the Commission was required to holding a full and complete hearing, after which the Commission was expected to be in a position to finally rule as to the rates.


OUTCOME: The court held that the suspension order of the Commission was invalid and was not entitled to enforcement.

State v. Nelson


No. 6462


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


65 N.M. 403; 1959-NMSC-023; 338 P.2d 301; 1959 N.M. LEXIS 920

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 14, 1959.

From adverse judgment of the District Court, Valencia County, Paul Tackett, D. J., the defendant appealed. The Supreme Court, Compton, J., held that court did not err in quoting to jury constitutional provision relative to Governor's power to pardon and reprieve and statutory provisions concerning authority of Parole Board.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the District Court of Valencia County (New Mexico), which convicted him of murder and sentenced him to death even though the jury returned a verdict of guilty without specifying life imprisonment in lieu of death. The trial court denied defendant's motions to set aside the verdict and for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The district court convicted defendant of murder. The court reversed. The district court again convicted defendant. The court affirmed. After the jury had been out for deliberation, they inquired about whether defendant could ever be released from prison or his life term commuted to a lesser term. The district court quoted the jury the constitutional provision relative to the governor's power to pardon and reprieve and statutory provisions concerning the authority of the parole board. The court held that the response was fair and did not indicate what the jury should or should not do. The court held that finding of the body in Valencia County and the police officer's testimony were sufficient to warrant the jury in concluding the deceased was killed in Valencia County. The record supported the conviction of a first-degree murder conviction upon the theory that the killing was done in the perpetration of a robbery. The court found no error in the jury instructions. The criminal acts of defendant were admitted. The court held the acts were relevant to prove identity. The court held that the district court judge could not be ousted of jurisdiction to preside over the new trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

 

348 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Chapman v. City of Albuquerque


No. 6421


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


65 N.M. 228; 1959-NMSC-012; 335 P.2d 558; 1959 N.M. LEXIS 894



February 9, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY: Class action was brought against city to have stand-by ordinances of city making assessments against unconnected property by which water or sewer pipes ran declared illegal and void. The District Court, Bernalillo County, D. A. Macpherson, Jr., D. J., entered judgment enjoining enforcement of the ordinances, and the city appealed, and the plaintiffs cross-appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that there was authority for sewer stand-by charge, but that there was no authority for water stand-by charge, and that there was no authority for exemptions or distinctions in ordinances, and that unauthorized exemptions and distinctions did not invalidate ordinance dealing with sewer stand-by charge, and that such ordinance should stand and only exemptions and distinctions should be declared invalid, and that there was a benefit to property subject to sewer stand-by charge, and that statute authorizing such charge was constitutional.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action by plaintiff property owners, appellant City of Albuquerque, New Mexico disputed a judgment of the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which declared Albuquerque, N.M., Ordinances 1075, 1085 illegal and void. The issues included whether N.M. Stat. §§ 14-40-38, 14-39-2 (1953) authorized the ordinances, whether exemptions or distinctions in the ordinances were authorized, and whether § 14-40-38 was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The ordinances were so-called standby ordinances under which the City was authorized to make assessments against unconnected property by which water or sewer pipes ran, i.e., the water and sewer mains stood by ready to serve the property. Ordinances 1075 and 1085 were purportedly enacted under the authority of §§ 14-40-38, 14-39-2, respectively. On appeal, the court held that, as to the water standby fees, the legislature never intended, in enacting § 14-39-2, that standby charges were to be levied against nonusers of facilities constructed under N.M. Stat. §§ 14-39-7 through 14-39-13 and 14-39-17 through 14-39-25, the water and sewer revenue bond act. But, the sewer standby fees were permitted by § 14-40-38, as amended by 1941 N.M. Laws 17. Nevertheless, there was no statutory authority for the exemptions from the fees or for distinctions between platted or subdivided property and unplatted or unsubdivided property. Finally, the court held that, because § 14-40-38 conferred a benefit upon the property subject to the sewer standby charge, the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded with instructions to the effect that the sewer standby charge was authorized, the water standby charge was not, there was no authority for the exemptions or distinctions but that fact did not invalidate the sewer standby ordinance itself, and the statute was constitutional.

350 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State Highway Comm'n v. Southern Union Gas Co.


No. 6425


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


65 N.M. 84; 1958-NMSC-124; 332 P.2d 1007; 1958 N.M. LEXIS 1383; 75 A.L.R.2d 408



November 14, 1958 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 30, 1958. Leave to File Second Motion for Rehearing Denied February 3, 1959. See 334 P.2d 1118.


PRIOR HISTORY: Declaratory judgment action. The District Court, Santa Fe County, David W. Carmody, D. J., rendered the judgment challenged by plaintiffs' appeal. The Supreme Court, Shillinglaw, J., held that construction of highways is a public governmental function but that relocation of utility's facilities is not; and that insofar as 1957 legislation provided for reimbursing utilities for costs of relocations necessitated by highway construction it was invalid for repugnancy to constitutional prohibition against donation of state funds in aid of private corporations.

See also, 65 N.M. 98, 332 P.2d 1017.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff highway commission (commission) brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant gas company to determine the constitutionality of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 55-7-18 and the obligations of the commission to reimburse the gas company for relocation costs. The District Court Santa Fe County (New Mexico) determined that the statute was constitutional. The commission appealed.


OVERVIEW: N.M. Stat. Ann. § 55-7-18 obligated the commission to reimburse the gas company for the cost of relocating its gas lines because of the widening and improving of a state highway. The commission refused to reimburse the gas company, contending that § 55-7-18 was unconstitutional. The gas company argued that the legislature determined that relocation costs were part of highway construction and the court was precluded from determining the reasonableness of that conclusion. The construction of highways was a public government function, but the relocation of utilities was not. Section 55-7-18 was unconstitutional. The legislature could not force the commission to reimburse the gas company for relocation of utility facilities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the gas company and remanded with instructions for the trial court to enter a judgment declaring that the commission was under no obligation to reimburse the gas company for its relocation costs.

Edmunds v. Bureau of Revenue


No. 6404


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


64 N.M. 454; 1958-NMSC-112; 330 P.2d 131; 1958 N.M. LEXIS 1360



September 24, 1958 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: September 24, 1958


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by vendor of chemical reagents against bureau of revenue to recover two per cent sales tax paid. The District Court, Santa Fe County, James M. Scarborough, D. J., dismissed complaint and vendor appealed. The Supreme Court, Shillinglaw, J., held that Legislature's selection of resident vendors for imposition of two per cent sales tax and of purchasers for imposition of compensating tax is reasonable in view of impossibility of subjecting nonresident vendor to sales tax, although statute imposing compensating tax contains provisions releasing purchasers of chemical reagents from obligation of paying tax.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant resident vendor sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Santa Fe County, (New Mexico), which dismissed the vendor's refund complaint against appellee Bureau of Revenue of New Mexico to recover two per cent sales tax paid pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16-4(D) (1953).


OVERVIEW: The vendor sold chemical reagents, and complained that although it was subject to the two percent tax under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16-4(D) of the Emergency School Tax Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-16-1 et seq., nonresident sellers were not, and that while under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-17-3 (1953) of the New Mexico Compensating Tax Act of 1939, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-17-1 et seq., purchases from nonresident vendors normally were taxed, pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 72-17-4(l) (1953), the specific reagents were excepted from the Compensating Tax. In affirming the judgment the court held that while the preference accorded by the Compensating Act might be unconstitutionally against the purpose of the Compensating Act that did not mean that the Emergency Act was. The court held that the legislature was free to impose the Emergency Act tax on the seller and the Compensating Act tax on the purchaser, and that this classification did not violate equal protection. Similarly the court noted that in granting exemptions the legislature was again free to classify according to the substances involved, thus the quirk that purchases of reagents from nonresidents went untaxed was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied a refund to the vendor.

Town of Farmington v. Miller


No. 6389


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


64 N.M. 330; 1958-NMSC-088; 328 P.2d 589; 1958 N.M. LEXIS 1341



July 18, 1958 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 25, 1958.


PRIOR HISTORY: Defendant was found guilty in police magistrate court of violation of city ordinance levying occupation tax and defendant appealed. The District Court, San Juan County, David W. Carmody, D. J., on trial de novo found defendant guilty and he appealed. The Supreme Court, Lujan, C. J., held that town tax in amount of $ 1 per thousand for each $ 1,000 gross volume of business levied on all occupations, professions, trades, pursuits or corporations and other institutions and businesses of whatever name or character impinged equally on all, sought to enforce equality in the market place, was not excessive, and was not unconstitutional as applied to foreign drummer who solicited orders in state.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of The District Court, San Juan County (New Mexico), which found him guilty of failing to pay an occupation tax.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a traveling salesman who took orders for tailor made clothes which were then shipped to the customer. Defendant was a resident of California. The town denied defendant's application for an occupation license. Defendant continued to solicit orders without the occupation license and was arrested and convicted. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the ordinance did not violate the commerce clause because the tax was assessed against all merchants and not just solicitors, and was not excessive. The court found that the ordinance did not impinge interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

353 of 795 DOCUMENTS


City of Albuquerque v. Burrell


No. 6398


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


64 N.M. 204; 1958-NMSC-070; 326 P.2d 1088; 1958 N.M. LEXIS 1322; 35 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P71,612



June 13, 1958 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: June 13, 1958


PRIOR HISTORY: Action to enjoin state labor commissioner from enforcing minimum wage rates for public contracts. The District Court of Santa Fe County, C. C. McCulloh, D. J., dismissed the complaint and plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that the suit was not a suit against the state and the state was not a necessary party.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed a decision from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which dismissed its complaint against defendant state labor commissioner in the city's action to enjoin the state labor commissioner from enforcing minimum wage rates for public contracts pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 6-6-6 (1953).


OVERVIEW: The city sought an injunction against the state labor commissioner to prevent him from insisting upon certain minimum wage rates. The trial court dismissed the city's complaint and the city appealed. The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to vacate its previous order and enter an order denying the motion to dismiss. The court held that the city had standing to bring the action because it alleged injury when the state labor commissioner set an arbitrary wage scale. Section 6-6-6 did not give the state labor commissioner the power to set a minimum scale of what he thought the wages should have been. The state labor commissioner's duty was to determine the prevailing ways in the locality for like work. Section 6-6-6 did not require that he hold hearings, but he had to investigate and determine the prevailing scale as a result of his own investigation. The state was not an indispensable party to the action. Because the city alleged that the state labor commissioner disregarded the requirements of § 6-6-6, the matter was properly subject to judicial review. The court found that § 6-6-6 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to vacate a previous order and to enter another order denying the state labor commissioner's motion to dismiss.

 

354 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Weiser v. Albuquerque Oil & Gasoline Co.


No. 6309


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


64 N.M. 137; 1958-NMSC-061; 325 P.2d 720; 1958 N.M. LEXIS 1307



May 9, 1958 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: May 9, 1958


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by motel guest against partnership, owner and operator of motel, for loss of sample case which allegedly contained jewelry and which had been deposited at front desk of motel. The District Court, Bernalillo County, Robert W. Reidy, D. J., entered summary judgment for motel as to excess of claim over $ 1,000.00 and guest appealed. The Supreme Court held that "motel" which consisted of two story building and additional guest buildings and which furnished maid service, telephone in each room, bellboy service, parking space and which was open 24 hours a day with meals served in rooms if desired, was a hotel within statute providing that hotel keepers shall be liable to their guests for loss of property brought by such guests into hotel when such loss is caused by theft or negligence of hotel keeper or his servants, not to exceed sum of $ 1,000.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant salesman sought review of a summary judgment from the District Court, Bernalillo County (New Mexico), entered for appellee motel to the extent the salesman's claim against the motel for the loss or theft of his personal property exceeded the limit of liability set in N.M. Stat. Ann. § 49-6-1 (1953).


OVERVIEW: The salesman stopped to stay a few nights in the motel. He deposited with the front desk for safekeeping his case of jewelry. The case was stolen, and the salesman sued to recover the value of the jewelry, but the district court held that under § 49-6-1 the motel's liability was limited to $ 1,000. In affirming the judgment the court held that the motel was a hotel within the meaning of § 49-6-1. The court held that it was not the name of the business but rather the services it provided in determining whether it was a hotel. The court noted that the motel had all of the most salient features of any hotel, only on a smaller scale, and thus was embraced within the act. The court then held that the limitation of liability pertained to articles deposited with the motel for safekeeping. Finally the court held that § 49-6-1 did not violate equal protection noting that the salesman was wrong in supposing that the motel's liability was limited in the event its personnel stole articles deposited with the motel and was unlimited in the event the articles were stolen by a third person.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment that limited the motel's liability.

Wallace v. Wallace


No. 6229


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


63 N.M. 414; 1958-NMSC-014; 320 P.2d 1020; 1958 N.M. LEXIS 1262



January 23, 1958 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: January 23, 1958


PRIOR HISTORY: Divorce action by wife against husband. The District Court, Bernalillo County, Robert W. Reidy, D. J., entered decree granting divorce to wife, and the husband appealed. The Supreme Court, Lujan, C. J., held that under servicemen's divorce statute, New Mexico District Court had jurisdiction of wife's divorce action against serviceman, notwithstanding that neither of parties was domiciled in New Mexico, where serviceman and wife had both resided continuously in state for more than a year.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged the judgment of the District Court, Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which entered a judgment of divorce upon an action by appellee wife. The husband also challenged a custody order that was a part of the divorce decree.


OVERVIEW: The husband was a member of the armed forces. The parties were married in Texas, spent several months in Arkansas, and were living in New Mexico when the wife sought divorce. The husband proceeded to file an action for divorce in Arkansas. Though the parties' counsel agreed upon dismissal of both actions, the Arkansas court granted a divorce. The wife sought to have that judgment set aside, claiming that it was obtained by fraud. The trial court, refusing to grant full faith and credit to the Arkansas judgment, entered a judgment of divorce for the wife. The court found that, as the husband was in the military service at the time the action was brought and, as both the parties had resided continuously in the state for more than one year, the trial court had jurisdiction to enter a divorce decree. The husband argued that the parties were not domiciled in the state. The court found that the servicemen's divorce statute, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 22-7-4 (1953), permitted the trial court's judgment by giving it jurisdiction of over such actions as that filed by the wife. Thus, the trial court had in personam jurisdiction over the parties and its judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of divorce.

Harriett v. Lusk


No. 6234


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


63 N.M. 383; 1958-NMSC-006; 320 P.2d 738; 1958 N.M. LEXIS 1256



January 13, 1958 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: January 13, 1958


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by members of county school board of education against superintendent of public instruction and others seeking injunctive and declaratory relief based on consolidation of public schools within rural districts and to restore to account of county board of education funds originally allocated to it by original budget. The District Court, Santa Fe County, C. C. McCulloh, D. J., dismissed action and members of county board of education appealed. The Supreme Court, Lujan, C. J., held that under amendment to school act which related to consolidation of schools and provided that it was effective for duration of war and one full school term thereafter, original act would continue and entire act had not expired by its own terms due to ending of war.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county school board of education members, filed an action against defendants, superintendent of public instruction and others, seeking injunctive and declaratory relief based on consolidation of public schools within rural districts. The District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) dismissed the action and county board members appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county board members argued that the order of consolidation of the state board of education on February 5, 1954, under 1945 N.M. Laws ch. 38, § 1, was invalid as the act providing authority for such consolidation had expired by its own terms due to ending of the war with Germany and Japan some years prior. The court disagreed, holding that when the entire act was read together, the only possible construction that could be made to harmonize its parts was that the legislature intended that the amendment of 1945 was to be effective for the duration of the war and one full school term thereafter, and that following this period the amendment was to end and the original act would then continue unamended. In addition, the court held that the superintendent had full authority to complete the consolidation of the schools in question under the order of February 5, 1954. The additional resolution by the state board in 1955 was unnecessary to effect the consolidation, but was merely an additional stimulus for her to act. The requirements of 1955 N.M. Laws ch. 100, § 1, did not have to be complied with in order for the consolidation to be valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

Ballew v. Denson


No. 6275


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


63 N.M. 370; 1958-NMSC-002; 320 P.2d 382; 1958 N.M. LEXIS 1252



January 7, 1958 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: January 7, 1958


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceeding brought by judgment debtor in ejectment wherein defendants filed counterclaim to quiet their title to premises. The District Court, Lea County, John R. Brand, D. J., entered judgment dismissing complaint in ejectment and quieting title in defendants and debtor appealed. The Supreme Court, Compton, J., held that where judgment creditors instituted cause against other judgment creditors to foreclose their liens, debtor was in possession and was personally served but allowed judgment to go against him by default, debtor made no objection to foreclosure proceedings, and outstanding judgments against him were partially reduced from proceeds of foreclosure sale, debtor ratified alleged irregular foreclosure proceedings and was estopped from attacking validity of judicial sale.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judgment debtor appealed an order of the District Court for Lea County (New Mexico), which dismissed his complaint in ejectment and quieted title to the property in defendant judgment creditors after the creditors instituted foreclosure proceedings against the debtor pursuant to 1933 N.M. Law ch. 7, §§ 24-1-22 to 24-1-25. The debtor contended that the act was unconstitutional and that the trial court lacked jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: After the creditors filed foreclosure proceedings on liens against the debtor pursuant to 1933 N.M. Law ch. 7, §§ 24-1-22 to 24-1-25, the debtor filed an ejectment suit. The creditors counterclaimed to quiet their title. The trial court dismissed the debtor's action and quieted title in favor of the creditors. The debtor appealed and contended that the Act was unconstitutional because its title did not clearly express the subject of the bill and that it embraced more than one subject, in violation of N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16. The court affirmed and held that the act clearly expressed its single subject. The court rejected the debtor's argument that the Act attempted to revise substantive law by reference in violation of N.M. Const. art. IV, § 18, and held that the Act granted an optional procedure for the enforcement of judgment liens. The court also rejected the debtor's argument of various irregularities in the foreclosure proceedings. Following the entry of judgment and during the time the debtor was trying to redeem the property, he remained in possession as a tenant of the foreclosure purchaser and made no objection to the proceedings, and, therefore, ratified them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Hinds v. Velasquez


No. 6252


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


63 N.M. 282; 1957-NMSC-092; 317 P.2d 899; 1957 N.M. LEXIS 969



November 6, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: November 6, 1957


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceeding to set aside default judgment against garnishee. The District Court, Santa Fe County, David W. Carmody, D. J., entered order setting aside judgment and judgment creditor appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that statute providing that sheriff who has execution in his hands may serve written notice upon any person indebted to debtor not to pay indebtedness but to appear before court out of which execution issued and make true answer under oath concerning such indebtedness does not allow the court to enter judgment against a garnishee for more than could be recovered against him by the principal debtor or to enter judgment solely because of garnishee's default in answering within time required by law.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on condition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judgment creditor sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which entered an order setting aside the judgment against appellee garnishee.


OVERVIEW: Execution was issued and placed in the hands of the sheriff for collection of the judgment. The sheriff served written notice upon the garnishee in accordance with N.M. Stat. Ann. § 24-1-3, to not pay the indebtedness to the judgment debtor, but to appear before the trial court out of which the execution issued and make true answer under oath concerning such indebtedness. The garnishee did not answer timely and default judgment was entered against the garnishee for the full amount of the judgment. Nine days thereafter, the garnishee answered, saying he owed the defendant the sum of $ 16.66. Execution was issued against the garnishee who then filed a motion for stay of execution. The motion was granted and an order issued setting aside the judgment against the garnishee. The judgment creditor appealed. The court affirmed on condition. The court held that there was no provision in the law that would allow a court to render judgment against a garnishee for more than could be recovered against him by the principal debtor, and none for judgment solely because of default.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed on condition the garnishee deposited the sum of $ 16.66 within 10 days with the clerk of the court for the benefit of the judgment creditor.

State ex rel. Murphy v. Morley


No. 6222


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


63 N.M. 267; 1957-NMSC-087; 317 P.2d 317; 1957 N.M. LEXIS 966



October 17, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: October 17, 1957


PRIOR HISTORY: Action to enjoin theater owner from showing allegedly immoral motion pictures. The District Court, Bernalillo County, Paul Tackett, D. J., entered judgment enjoining theater owner and he appealed. The Supreme Court, Lujan, C. J., held that under statute providing for abatement of nuisances connected with lewdness, assignation or prostitution, "lewdness" does not include acts not connected with assignation or prostitution.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant theatre owner appealed a judgment from the District Court, Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which, pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-34-15 (1953), enjoined him from showing allegedly immoral motion pictures.


OVERVIEW: Section 40-34-15 provided for the abatement of a nuisance connected with "lewdness," "assignation," or "prostitution." The court reversed the trial court's judgment, holding that "lewdness" as used in the statute did not apply to the showing of motion pictures in a regular business establishment because lewdness did not include acts not connected with assignation or prostitution; and that the injunction constituted a prior restraint of the press, impermissible under N.M. Const. art. 11, § 17, and the First and Fourteenth Amendments to the U.S. Constitution. The court relied on several maxims of statutory construction in reaching its conclusion, including that where two meanings were possible and one would make a statute unconstitutional, it could be presumed that the legislature did not intend to legislate unconstitutionally; and that where general and specific words in a statute were associated together, the general words were restricted to a sense analogous to the less general. In addition the term "lewdness" if dissociated from "assignation or prostitution" would be too vague and indefinite to comply with the due process requirements of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with directions to dissolve the injunction and to dismiss the complaint.

Skaggs Drug Ctr. v. GE


No. 6204


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


63 N.M. 215; 1957-NMSC-083; 315 P.2d 967; 1957 N.M. LEXIS 959



September 27, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: September 27, 1957


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by retailer against distributor for declaratory judgment with respect to Fair Trade Act. Distributor answered and counterclaimed for injunction against further sales by retailer at prices below those fixed by distributor. Second distributor brought suit against retailer for injunction to restrain sales at prices less than those established by second distributor. The two cases were consolidated. The District Court, Bernalillo County, Robert W. Reidy, D. J., held the Fair Trade Act constitutional and entered injunctions. The retailer appealed. The Supreme Court, Carmody, District Judge, held that section two of the Fair Trade Act which provides that sale of trade-marked items at a price less than that stipulated to is a violation of the Act whether the seller is a party to the stipulated price contract or not, is unconstitutional and void as an arbitrary and unreasonable exercise of the police power without a substantial relation to the public health, safety or general welfare insofar as it concerns persons who are not parties to the price contract.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff drug store sought review of a judgment rendered by the District Court, Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which held that defendants, manufacturer and distributor, did not violate the Fair Trade Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 49-2-2 (1953), by restraining sales at prices less than those fixed by the distributor.


OVERVIEW: The drug store sued the manufacturer and distributor under the Fair Trade Act, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 49-2-2 (1953), claiming that they engaged in unfair behavior by restraining sales at prices less than those fixed by the distributor. The trial court dismissed the case and the drug store appealed. The court held that the restraint of prices below those fixed by the distributor harmed consumers and did not protect any right of the distributor or manufacturer. The court also stated that refusing to allow the drug store to sell at prices below minimum prices was anti-competitive and violated the Fair Trade Act. Finally, the court concluded that the distributor and manufacturer violated the drug store's rights because it denied them life, liberty, or property without due process of law since it was not a party to any contract with the distributor. The court reversed the trial court's ruling and remanded for the trial court to enter judgment in conformity with the court's opinion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.
