Leavell v. Town of Texico


No. 6215


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


63 N.M. 233; 1957-NMSC-081; 316 P.2d 247; 1957 N.M. LEXIS 961



September 18, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 21, 1957.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by owners of property, which was annexed to municipality, contesting annexation. The District Court, Curry County, E. T. Hensley, Jr., D. J., dismissed action, and owners appealed. The Supreme Court, Lujan, C. J., held that where statute, authorizing annexation of territories to municipality by resolution of municipal council provided that property owners in territory to be annexed had right to appeal to District Court within thirty days after adoption of resolution, but did not require notice of resolution, thirty day period began after resolution annexing owner's property was passed, and although resolution was not given the usual publicity, action brought by owners more than thirty days after passage of resolution was barred.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged the judgment of the District Court of Curry County (New Mexico), which dismissed, as barred by the statute of limitations, the property owners' action against appellees, a municipality and its officials, that contested annexation of the property owners' land to the municipality pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 14-6-8 (1953).


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to § 14-6-8, the right of appeal was limited to 30 days after a resolution's adoption. The property owners' complaint was not timely. They first argued that § 14-6-8 was unconstitutional. The court noted that the power to enlarge the boundaries of municipal corporations was universally held to be exclusively the exercise of legislative power. Such statutes were to be liberally construed in favor of the municipality. The property owners also argued that appellees committed fraud by not giving the resolution the usual publicity. The court noted that notice was not required by § 14-6-8. Statutes could provide for annexation without notice. If notice were required, the recorded actions of the municipality provided constructive notice. Although § 14-6-8 provided that certain conditions such as contiguity, platting, and description had to be met before annexation, it also provided that a determination of the existence of those conditions only could be had if an appeal was timely taken. Where a statute limited the time for appeal from a municipal act, the action was barred if not brought in that period. Pursuant to N.M. Stat. Ann. § 23-1-17 (1953), the court had no jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment dismissing the action for lack of jurisdiction.

 

362 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Hovey Concrete Prods. Co. v. Mechem


No. 6264


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


63 N.M. 250; 1957-NMSC-075; 316 P.2d 1069; 1957 N.M. LEXIS 964



August 30, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 15, 1957.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding in mandamus to compel Governor to appoint Commissioners to administer provisions of Workmen's Compensation Act of 1957. The Supreme Court, Compton, J., held that Workmen's Compensation Act of 1957 authorizes Commission to decide questions of fact between private litigants and to render decisions which have the force and effect of judgments and thereby delegates judicial power to Commission in violation of constitutional provision vesting in courts alone the right to determine controversies between individual litigants.



DISPOSITION: Writ discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent governor of New Mexico to administer the provisions of the Workmen's Compensation Act of 1957 (Act), N.M. Stat. Ann. § 59-10-36 et. seq., and appoint commissioners to a commission that would hold a hearing and make findings of fact and conclusions of law that would have the force and effect of judgments in workmen's compensation claims.


OVERVIEW: The governor decided to appoint the commission because he doubted the validity of the Act. Upon review, the court found that the provisions of the Act for the commission were an unlawful invasion of the New Mexico Constitution under N.M. Const. art. 3, § 1. Administrate boards and commissions could be created to administer regulatory laws that affected the general public, but the rights and liabilities of private individuals were fixed by law and to be determined by judicial inquiry. Further, N.M. Const. art. 6, § 1 placed a limitation on the creation of inferior courts. The function to be performed by the commission under the Act was clearly a judicial function. The commission was called upon to decide questions of fact between private litigants and was empowered to render decision that had the force and effect of judgments. The New Mexico Constitution did not permit the commission to be clothed in such judicial power. The power to determine controversies between individual litigants rested alone with the courts.


OUTCOME: The court discharged the alternative writ and declined to compel the governor to appoint commissioners to a workmen's compensation commission under the Act.

State ex rel. Bliss v. Potter Co.


No. 6150


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


63 N.M. 101; 1957-NMSC-066; 314 P.2d 390; 1957 N.M. LEXIS 940



August 12, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: August 12, 1957


PRIOR HISTORY: Suit by State Engineer to enjoin use of water on certain parts of farm. The District Court, Chaves County, George T. Harris, D. J., denied injunction and engineer appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that as to one tract of land on farm, trial court erred in finding that tract had a valid water right by continued use of water for irrigation purposes before passage of law regulating same, but as to other tract, evidence sustained finding of court that a valid water right had been established.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state engineer appealed a judgment entered in the District Court of Chaves County (New Mexico), which denied his request to enjoin the use of water on certain parts of defendant farm owner's property.


OVERVIEW: The state engineer sought to enjoin a property owner from using water from an artesian basin for tracts on its farm. On one tract, the district court held that the owner had a definite water right, but the court reversed based on an error as to acreage. On the remaining tracts, A and B, the state engineer showed that there was no evidence that tract A was irrigated. The owner urged that tract A had been irrigated from a well that it sought to plug. Its application for a new well was granted, but caused an investigation that showed only 176.7 acres out of 240 were cultivated. On review, the court held that the evidence presented by the owner as to the use of water on tract A was vague when weighed against a hydrographic survey that showed tract A as unirrigated salt grassland. The court found that the survey and former owners' acquiescence for a new well permit compelled the court to hold that tract A did not have a valid water right. However, the owner produced a witness who farmed tract B and neighbors that saw the land being worked, which established a water right and supported denial of the injunction. Claims of unconstitutionality as to well permit statutes were not preserved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court judgment in part, and reversed in part.

 

364 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Mechem v. Hannah


No. 6239


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


63 N.M. 110; 1957-NMSC-065; 314 P.2d 714; 1957 N.M. LEXIS 943



August 8, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 11, 1957.


PRIOR HISTORY: The State of New Mexico, on the relation of the Governor of the State of New Mexico and the president of the State Board of Finance, brought an original mandamus proceeding in the Supreme Court against the State Auditor and the State Treasurer to compel the State Auditor and the State Treasurer to make available to the State Board of Finance $ 200,000 appropriated by statute. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that act making appropriations to State Board of Finance for "federal-state cooperative agreement for the roughage drought feed program" violates section of the constitution providing that the state shall not directly or indirectly make any donation to or in aid of any person.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ of mandamus quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the State of New Mexico, on behalf of the governor and the president of the state finance board, brought an original proceeding against respondents, the state auditor and treasurer. The State sought a peremptory writ of mandamus to compel the auditor and treasurer to make available to the finance board a certain sum that had been appropriated by 1957 N.M. Laws ch. 22, § 1, to aid ranchers affected by a drought.


OVERVIEW: New Mexico had been afflicted by a severe drought, which denuded its ranges in almost every area. The livestock industry was in distress. The appropriation was made to pay part of the State's share of emergency hay and roughage certificates, issued to ranchers for their livestock pursuant to a contract between the governor and U.S. Department of Agriculture. The auditor and treasurer had refused to disburse the funds after the state attorney general opined that 1957 N.M. Laws ch. 22 was unconstitutional. The court held that the statute contravened N.M. Const. art. IX, § 14, because the grants to participants in the roughage program constituted donations to private persons. New Mexico had no voice in issuing the certificates to applicants. Rather, direct grants of state funds were made to persons declared eligible by federal agents. Also, participation in the program was not limited to persons who were sick or indigent within the meaning of art. IX, § 14, nor were the funds to be given to the ranchers to prevent them from becoming so. The fact that state contributions were promised under the contract was insufficient to save the appropriation.


OUTCOME: The alternative writ of mandamus was quashed.

 

365 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Torres v. Grant


No. 6267


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


63 N.M. 106; 1957-NMSC-061; 314 P.2d 712; 1957 N.M. LEXIS 942



July 12, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 16, 1957.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding in mandamus for a peremptory writ directing the state treasurer to honor and pay a certain warrant drawn on him. The Supreme Court, Compton, J., held that statute providing warrants on state funds may be drawn only by the Director of the Department of Finance and Administration was not unconstitutional on any theory that it removed from the state auditor substantially all the powers and duties of that office.



DISPOSITION: Petition for peremptory writ of mandamus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner capitol custodian filed a proceeding seeking a writ of mandamus from the court (New Mexico) requiring respondent State Treasurer to honor and pay a warrant drawn on him and payable to the custodian or to show why he had not done so.


OVERVIEW: The State Treasurer had previously honored warrants presented by the custodian but, citing N. M. Stat. Ann. § 4-4-2 (1953), refused to continue doing so. The custodian filed his petition for a writ, which the court denied. The court held that, because N.M. Const. art. V, § 1, in designating the executive officers of the State government, was silent as to the duties of the State Auditor, the legislature had the power to transfer the statutory duties of the State Treasurer to the State Auditor. The court noted that the legislature could not abolish a constitutional office or deprive the office of any prescribed constitutional duty but that the transfer of a statutory duty was within the legislature's power.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for the writ.

 

366 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Tauch v. Ferguson-Steere Motor Co.


No. 6156 (Nos. 5817, 5847, 5959)


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


62 N.M. 429; 1957-NMSC-039; 312 P.2d 83; 1957 N.M. LEXIS 919



May 14, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 20, 1957.


PRIOR HISTORY: Actions to recover damages for wrongful deaths resulting from collision between automobile in which decedents were riding and oncoming truck owned by defendant. From adverse judgments entered in District Court, Otero County, John R. Brand, D. J., defendant appealed. The Supreme Court, Sadler, J., held that the personal representatives of unmarried adults who had no dependent parents, brothers or sisters could recover amount specified in wrongful death statute for death caused by negligence of common carrier.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a commercial carrier, appealed from the judgments of the District Court, Otero County (New Mexico). Actions to recover damages for wrongful deaths were brought against it by plaintiffs, administrators of the estates of the decedents, who died in a collision between the automobile in which they were riding and the carrier's truck. Judgment was entered in favor of the administrators. The three actions were consolidated for review.


OVERVIEW: The three causes of action arose out of a collision between the carrier's truck and an automobile in which the three decedents, all of whom died instantly in the accident, were riding. The highway was hazardous at the time because of iced conditions. There were no witnesses to the accident. However, the automobile was found on its proper side of the highway. The administrators sought recovery under N.M. Comp. Stat. § 22-20-4 (1953). The carrier urged that the decedents lacked the capacity to sue under § 22-20-4. It argued that, at the time of their death, they were over 21 years of age, unmarried, and had no surviving heirs or other persons dependent on them, partially or totally, for their support and maintenance within the meaning of § 22-20-4. The court affirmed the judgment. The decedents had suffered wrongful death within the purview of § 22-20-4 and, though they left no heirs or dependents, the administrators of their estates had the right to sue under the statute to recover the stipulated damage authorized therein for death caused by the carrier's negligence. Further, the carrier failed in its burden to show that the driver of the automobile was contributorily negligent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments.

 

367 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Burch v. Foy


No. 6117


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


62 N.M. 219; 1957-NMSC-017; 308 P.2d 199; 1957 N.M. LEXIS 890; 31 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P70,507



February 7, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 28, 1957.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suit by owner of variety store to enjoin district attorney from enforcing criminal provisions of Wage and Hour Act and to have Act declared unconstitutional. The District Court, Luna County, A. W. Marshall, D. J., entered order declaring act unconstitutional and permanently enjoined district attorney from enforcing act, and State appealed. The Supreme Court, Lujan, C. J., held that Act which requires variety store employees to be paid minimum wage of 75 cents per hour, but permits drug store employees doing substantially same type of work to be paid 50 cents per hour, is unconstitutional insofar as it refers to drug store employees as it denys equal protection of law and classification is arbitrary and oppressive, but remaining provisions of act are valid.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and in part reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a variety store owner, filed a suit against defendant district attorney to enjoin him from enforcing the criminal provisions of the Wage and Hour Act, 1955 N.M. Laws ch. 220, and to have the Act declared unconstitutional. The District Court, Luna County (New Mexico) entered an order declaring the Act unconstitutional and permanently enjoining the district attorney from enforcing the Act. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The variety store was located in the same block as two drug stores. All three stores employed more than four employees and handled the same type of merchandise. The drug stores both maintained a fountain and lunch counter but the variety store did not sell food or drink for consumption at the store. Pursuant to 1955 N.M. Laws ch. 220, § 2(c)(1) of the Wage and Hour Act, drug store employees were classified as "service employees" whether or not they actually served food and drink. Pursuant to § 3 of the Act, service employees were required to be paid a minimum wage of 50 cents per hour while all other employees were required to be paid a minimum wage of 75 cents per hour. The variety store owner filed a suit to enjoin the district attorney from enforcing the criminal provisions of the Act against him and to declare the Act unconstitutional. On appeal of a judgment in his favor, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The Act's classification of all drug store employees in § 2(c)(1) as service employees was a denial of equal protection. The classification was arbitrary, oppressive, and without any rational basis. The remaining provisions of the Act were valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. It held that the Act was unconstitutional insofar as it related to drug store employees but that the remaining provisions were valid.

 

368 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Dickson v. Saiz


Nos. 6071, 6072


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


62 N.M. 227; 1957-NMSC-010; 308 P.2d 205; 1957 N.M. LEXIS 892



January 23, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 4, 1957.


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceedings in review of action of Chief of Liquor Control Division revoking retail liquor licenses. The District Court, Santa Fe County, James M. Scarborough, D. J., entered orders setting aside revocation on ground of unconstitutionality of liquor control act. The State appealed. The Supreme Court held that under constitutional provision authorizing governor to approve or disapprove any part or parts, item or items, of any bill appropriating money, governor properly vetoed provisions of 1939 liquor control bill allowing Sunday sales, even though bill was general legislation which only incidentally contained item of appropriation.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed and causes remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State, on behalf of the Chief of the Liquor Control Division of the Bureau of Revenue (New Mexico), appealed orders by the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which set aside the Division's revocation of the retail liquor licenses of appellee sellers. The main issue was whether N.M. Const. art. IV, § 22, which gave the governor the power to item veto, limited the governor's exercise of the power to general appropriation bills.


OVERVIEW: The licenses were revoked because the sellers sold liquor on Sunday in violation of the provisions of 1939 N.M. Laws 236, the Liquor Control Act (Act), which was enacted on the last day of the legislature's regular session. The trial court set aside the revocations upon the ground that the governor's action in exercising a partial veto of the part of the Act prohibiting Sunday sales nullified the whole Act. On appeal, the court reviewed the provisions of art. IV, § 22, noting that a later amendment was not material to the issues at bar. The court held that there was nothing in the last sentence of the Act that required the governor, once he acted on a measure submitted to him within the last three days of the legislative session, to return the measure to the legislature. The parts of the bill approved became a law without further action by the legislature. There was no language in the Act synonymous with the phrase "general appropriation bills," which the framers of art. IV, § 22, being familiar with such language, could have used if they had so intended. Further, there was a presumption that the Act, like any act, was valid. The court held that the Act was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with a direction to the trial court to set aside its order revoking the action of the Division and enter another in lieu thereof affirming the cancellation of the licenses.

State ex rel. W. v. Thomas


No. 6170


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


62 N.M. 103; 1956-NMSC-124; 305 P.2d 376; 1956 N.M. LEXIS 1140



December 21, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: December 21, 1956


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus proceeding to compel county clerk to furnish relator with an absentee ballot. The District Court, Curry County, E. T. Hensley, Jr., D. J., entered judgment dissolving alternative writ, and relator appealed. The Supreme Court, Lujan, J., held that the Absentee Voting Act violated constitutional provision which requires qualified voter's personal presence at the polls when voter offers to vote.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator voter sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Curry County (New Mexico) that was rendered in favor of respondent county clerk and dissolved the Alternate Writ that was granted to compel the county clerk to provide the voter an absentee ballot.


OVERVIEW: The voter sought an absentee ballot. He asserted that he would be absent from his voting precinct during an upcoming election, that he made an application for a ballot within the required time, and that he was a qualified elector and was entitled to the absentee ballot. The county clerk refused the voter's request to furnish a ballot as contemplated by N.M. Stat. Ann. § 3-5-10 (1953). The voter sought and the trial court granted his petition for an alternate writ and issued an order to show cause why the county clerk should not give the voter his absentee ballot. The trial court held after the show cause hearing that the alternative writ should be dissolved and found that the Absentee Voting Act was unconstitutional. The court affirmed and found that the Act violated the provisions of N.M. Const. art. VII, § 1, which required that a voter actually be present at a polling place in his precinct when he cast his ballot. The court held that the Absentee Voting Act, ch. 256 Laws of 1955 was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Smith


No. 6094


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


62 N.M. 84; 1956-NMSC-122; 304 P.2d 883; 1956 N.M. LEXIS 1137



December 14, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: December 14, 1956


PRIOR HISTORY: Prosecutions for embezzlement of public funds of a city. The District Court, Roosevelt County, George T. Harris, D. J., granted defendants' motion to dismiss the information and the State appealed. The Supreme Court, Sadler, J., held that statute providing that any public official, "or any person having in his possession any money or other property" belonging to city, "who shall convert to his own use in any way or manner whatever," any part of said moneys shall be guilty of embezzlement, is not unconstitutional or void on account of uncertainty in meaning, vagueness or indefiniteness or for failure to define the offense of embezzlement, since conversion of public funds to one's own use can only be by fraud.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order of the District Court of Roosevelt County (New Mexico), which granted defendants' motion to dismiss an information charging defendants' with the crime of embezzling public funds, a violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-45-22 (1953).


OVERVIEW: The State filed an information against defendants and charged them with the offense of embezzling public funds. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss the information on the ground that the statute under which the prosecution was initiated, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-45-22 (1953), was uncertain in meaning, vague, indefinite, and failed to define the offense of embezzlement. On review, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case. In reaching its decision, the court held that the statute was not unconstitutional or void on account of uncertainty in meaning, vagueness or indefiniteness, or for failure to define the offense of embezzlement, because conversion of public funds to one's own use could only be by fraud.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause.

Vill. of Deming v. Hosdreg Co.


No. 6023


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


62 N.M. 18; 1956-NMSC-111; 303 P.2d 920; 1956 N.M. LEXIS 1126



November 20, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: November 20, 1956


PRIOR HISTORY: Village's action for declaratory judgment to determine validity of statute authorizing municipality to issue revenue bonds to acquire industrial sites. The District Court, Luna County, A. W. Marshall, D. J., entered judgment declaring statute to be constitutional and defendant appealed. The Supreme Court, Sadler, J., held that statute authorizing municipality to issue revenue bonds for the purpose of acquiring or constructing industrial buildings for sale or lease to industries wishing to locate within proximity of municipality and providing that by issuance of bonds municipality may not incur pecuniary liability or charge upon its general credit or against its taxing power, does not violate constitutional provision prohibiting municipality from making any donation to or in aid of any private corporation.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation appealed a judgment of the Supreme Court, Luna County (New Mexico), which held in favor of defendant city in an action for declaratory judgment to determine validity of a statute authorizing the city to issue revenue bonds to acquire industrial sites.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted a statute authorizing it to issue revenue bonds for the purpose of acquiring or constructing industrial buildings for sale or lease to industries wishing to locate within proximity of municipality. The corporation brought an action for declaratory judgment to determine the validity of the statute authorizing the city to issue revenue bonds to acquire industrial sites. The trial court declared the statute to be constitutional, and the corporation appealed. The court ruled that the legislature could enact any law which the constitution did not prohibit and that the courts could not strike down one of its statutes unless it clearly appeared that such statute did contravene some provision of the constitution. The court affirmed the judgment declaring the statute constitutional, concluding that the statute did not violate a provision of fundamental law.


OUTCOME: The judgment upholding the constitutionality of the statute was affirmed.

 

372 of 795 DOCUMENTS


First Thrift & Loan Ass'n v. State


No. 6091


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


62 N.M. 61; 1956-NMSC-099; 304 P.2d 582; 1956 N.M. LEXIS 1133



October 8, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 28, 1956.


PRIOR HISTORY: Quo warranto proceeding to oust, enjoin and restrain defendant from exercising its purported corporate powers to transact a banking business. The District Court, Bernalillo County, John B. McManus, Jr., D. J., entered judgment barring defendant from acting as a bank and it brought error. The Supreme Court, Sadler, J., held that a corporation could not organize under the general corporation law, rather than under statutes relating to incorporation of companies to engage in the banking business, or under legislation providing for mercantile companies and thereafter conduct a banking business whether or not said corporation had two departments.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation sought review of a judgment rendered by the District Court, Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which enjoined it from conducting any banking activities on the grounds that the corporation was not authorized by law to act like a bank.


OVERVIEW: The state attorney general filed a proceeding by quo warranto ousting, enjoining, and restraining the corporation from bank activities. The trial court enjoined the corporation and it appealed the ruling. The court held that under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 48-14-01 (1953) a corporation may be permitted to undertake bank activities if it undertook an incorporation of a mercantile company and organized in a town of less than 1500 people. The court stated that the corporation here did not operate in a town of less than 1500 people and did not incorporate a mercantile company. The court determined that the trial court correctly enjoined the corporation from acting as a bank. Further, the court observed that an attorney general opinion did not support the corporation and in any event, the court was not bound to follow the opinion of the Attorney General. Finally, the court concluded that the State Banking Act was not unconstitutional or that the state was barred by laches or estoppel from taking any action against the corporation. The court upheld the trial court's ruling and denied the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State ex rel. State Hwy Comm'n v. Walker


No. 6081


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


61 N.M. 374; 1956-NMSC-080; 301 P.2d 317; 1956 N.M. LEXIS 1099



September 4, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: September 4, 1956


PRIOR HISTORY: The State, on the relation of the State Highway Commission of New Mexico, brought action against the Commissioner of Public Lands of the State of New Mexico for a declaratory judgment. The District Court of Santa Fe County, James M. Scarborough, D. J., entered judgment adverse to the State Highway Commission, and it appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that the Commissioner of Public Lands of New Mexico could charge the State Highway Commission of New Mexico for rights of way or easements for state highways across lands, which had been granted and confirmed to the State of New Mexico in trust for various state institutions and agencies by the Enabling Act when New Mexico was admitted to statehood, and for sand and gravel removed from such lands for use in constructing public highways across the lands.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, State Highway Commission of New Mexico, contested an order of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) that entered judgment for appellee, Commissioner of Public Lands of the State of New Mexico, in a declaratory action over whether appellee could charge appellant for rights of way or easements for state highways across lands which were given to the state in trust and for sand and gravel removed when building public highways.


OVERVIEW: The general rule was that an agency of the state was not to be charged for the use of state property unless specific provision was made. The Enabling Act of June 20, 1910, 36 Stat. 557, provided that the land would be administered and any proceeds would go for the benefit of the various state institutions for which the lands were granted. No part of the proceeds could be diverted to any other purpose. Thus, the court affirmed the trial court and found that the state public lands commissioner must charge the state highway commission for rights of way or easements for state highways across lands that were granted to the state in trust by the Enabling Act when New Mexico was admitted to statehood. The state public lands commissioner must also charge for sand and gravel removed from such lands for use solely in constructing public highways across the trust lands.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the state public lands commissioner in a declaratory action on the issue of whether the state public lands commissioner could charge state highway commission for rights of way or easements for state highways across state land.

N.M. State Bd. of Pub. Accountancy v. Grant


No. 6042


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


61 N.M. 287; 1956-NMSC-068; 299 P.2d 464; 1956 N.M. LEXIS 1085



July 19, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: July 19, 1956


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by State Board of Public Accountancy against State Treasurer and others seeking to restrain defendants from transferring on their books to the credit of the general fund in the state treasury, the Board's credit balance at the close of the fiscal year. The District Court, Santa Fe County, David W. Carmody, D. J., entered judgment denying permanent injunction and Board of Accountancy appealed. The Supreme Court, Sadler, J., held that the 1953 General Appropriations Act under which it was required that balance to Board's credit at the end of fiscal year must be transferred to the general fund, was not unconstitutional, even though some of the funds remaining to the credit of the Board were voluntary contributions.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State Board of Public Accountancy, filed an action against appellees, the State Treasurer and the State Auditor, seeking to restrain them from transferring on their books to the credit of the general fund in the state treasury, the Board's credit balance at the close of the fiscal year. The District Court, Santa Fe County, (New Mexico), entered a judgment denying the permanent injunction. The Board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that all funds collected by the Board under authority of N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 67-23-1 to 67-23-29 (1953) were public funds that had to be deposited with the State Treasurer. Of the funds standing to the credit of the Board at the end of the 1954-1955 fiscal year, $ 740 had been contributed by individual accountants to assist in the operations of the Board for the current year. The trial court also found that the General Appropriations Act, 1953 N.M. Laws, ch. 156, was not unconstitutional in requiring the reverter to the general fund of balances remaining to the credit of any of enumerated boards at the end of the fiscal year. The Board contended that the court could not apply the mandate found in § 5 of the Act to the credit that represented the voluntary contributions by its member accountants to enable the Board to carry on its operations. The court held that, once those funds were deposited in the state treasury and became commingled with the Board's other funds, they could only be withdrawn through appropriations made by the legislature upon warrants drawn by the proper officer, N.M. Const. art. IV, § 30.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

375 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Collins


No. 6045


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


61 N.M. 184; 1956-NMSC-046; 297 P.2d 325; 1956 N.M. LEXIS 1068



April 25, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 23, 1956.


PRIOR HISTORY: Prosecution for violation of statute prohibiting any person from using words "drug store" or "drug sundries" or any words of similar or like import in advertising place of business unless such business was actually a drug store in which a registered pharmacist was constantly employed on regular basis. The District Court, Lincoln County, W. T. Scoggin, D. J., held statute to be unconstitutional and State appealed. The Supreme Court, Lujan, J., held that such statute is a valid exercise by Legislature of police power and is constitutional.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of the decision of the District Court of Lincoln County (New Mexico), which held that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 67-9-15 (1953) was unconstitutional. The statute proscribed advertising a drug store unless a pharmacist were employed full time.


OVERVIEW: Defendant operated a business that contained the term "drug sundries" in its name. No pharmacist was employed on the premises. Defendant was charged with violating N.M. Stat. Ann. § 67-9-15, which prohibited the use of such terms unless a pharmacist were constantly employed on a regular basis. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute as a deprivation of his private property rights, as an unreasonable exercise of the police power, and as creating a monopoly by pharmacists. The court held that the regulation of selling drugs and medicines was so intimately connected with the health, safety, and welfare of the public that it fell within the lawful exercise of the State's police power. The statute did not create monopoly or restrain trade because it expressly permitted the sale of other products by non-pharmacists under certain conditions. In reversing the judgment, the court held that the statute did not prevent citizens from following a calling because it only placed conditions and requirements on that exercise of liberty. The statute offended neither the federal or State constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and upheld the constitutionality of the statute.

Toledo Soc'y for Crippled Children v. Toledo Trust Co. (In re Will of Hickok)


No. 6012


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


61 N.M. 204; 1956-NMSC-035; 297 P.2d 866; 1956 N.M. LEXIS 1070



March 12, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 25, 1956.


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceedings by charities under a testamentary trust to set aside a final decree in ancillary probate proceedings upon the estate of testator. From a judgment of the District Court, Lincoln County, W. T. Scoggin, D. J., denying their motion to set aside such decree, the charities appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held, inter alia, that statute vesting in district courts jurisdiction concurrent with that of probate courts over administration of estates is not unconstitutional on theory that the word "exclusive" should be read into constitutional provision that probate court, until otherwise provided by law, shall have same jurisdiction as is exercised by probate courts of the territory of New Mexico.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant charities sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Lincoln County (New Mexico), which denied their motion to set aside a final decree upon the decedent's estate.


OVERVIEW: The charities filed a motion challenging the final accounting of the decedent's estate. The basis for the motion was that while the charities were devised, a remainder interest in the properties of the decedent situated in New Mexico, they were not served with notice of the pendency of the estate nor of the hearing upon the final account. The trial court denied the charities' motion and they sought review. Affirming the trial court's judgment, the court held that upon examination of the interests claimed by the charities under the decedent's will, the matters complained about respecting the final account and report resulted in no detriment to them. The court further held that because the charities had no interest in the income from the trust properties, under the express terms of the will, the failure of the executors to report income received from New Mexico properties, if any, did not work to their detriment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that denied the charities' motion to set aside the final account of the decedent's estate.

Elephant Butte Irrigation Dist. v. Gatlin


No. 5938


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


61 N.M. 58; 1956-NMSC-030; 294 P.2d 628; 1956 N.M. LEXIS 1049



February 27, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 22, 1956.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action by an irrigation district against subordinate officials of Department of Interior to enjoin diversion of river water to federal game refuge on grounds that all rights to river water in state had been appropriated and that such diversion was consequently unlawful. The District Court, Dona Ana County, W. T. Scoggin, D. J., entered judgment of injunction for the plaintiff, and defendants appealed. The Supreme Court, Lujan, J., held that in view of facts that game refuge had been lawfully established in aid of treaties and that without continued application of water to refuge, its operation would become impossible, judgment would expend itself upon United States and where United States was not made party and had not consented to be sued, judgment would be reversed.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with directions to dismiss.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant officers of the United States Department of the Interior appealed from an order of the trial court (New Mexico), granting relief requested by plaintiff Elephant Butte Irrigation District of New Mexico, and ordering that the officers were enjoined from diverting waters from the Rio Grande into a federally-protected refuge. The officers argued that the trial court erred denying their motion to dismiss for lack of an indispensable party.


OVERVIEW: The district was organized by the water users of the Rio Grande project for providing irrigation to their lands in cooperation with the federal government under federal reclamation laws. The district brought an action against the officers to enjoin their diversion of its waters to a federally-protected refuge. The refuge was administered by the Secretary of the Interior. The officers filed a motion for summary judgment on the grounds that there was a lack of indispensable parties. The trial court denied the motion, and granted the requested relief. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's ruling and directed the trial court to enter judgment dismissing the action. The court held that the granting of the relief sought reached beyond the right to the waters owned by the district, affected the public domain and treasury, and interfered with public administration. The court determined that the judgment would have directly affected the United States, its properties and administration, therefore, the United States was an indispensable party not before the court and that it had not consented to be sued.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and ordered the trial court to enter judgment dismissing the district's action against the officers.

Seismograph Serv. Corp. v. Bureau of Revenue


No. 5895


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


61 N.M. 16; 1956-NMSC-028; 293 P.2d 977; 1956 N.M. LEXIS 1041



February 17, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: February 17, 1956


PRIOR HISTORY: Suit by seismograph company, a Delaware corporation with principal office and place of business in Oklahoma and no branch office or agencies within New Mexico, for recovery of amount paid for certain taxes on portions of company's gross receipts allegedly attributable to New Mexico operations. The District Court, Santa Fe County, David W. Carmody, D. J., rendered judgment for company, and appeal was taken. The Supreme Court, Kiker, J., held that where company made geophysical surveys for oil in New Mexico pursuant to contracts entered into outside New Mexico and principally with nonresidents, and took resulting data to its Oklahoma office for analysis and formulation of opinions for clients, and where no part of company's receipts could be definitely declared as receipts from New Mexico operations, company was not engaged in intrastate business in New Mexico, and tax upon its gross receipts, although pertaining to surveys in New Mexico, was invalid.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, a Delaware corporation, brought suit against appellant, the Bureau of Revenue of the State of New Mexico (Bureau), for recovery of amount paid for certain taxes on portions of the company's gross receipts allegedly attributable to New Mexico operations. The Bureau appealed from a judgment of the District Court, Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which rendered judgment for company.


OVERVIEW: The company filed suit for recovery of an amount paid under protest to the Bureau of Revenue, for taxes levied under the Emergency School Tax Act of the state. The company claimed that the taxes were illegally levied for the reasons: (1) the levies were a burden upon interstate commerce in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 8; (2) the levies constituted a taking of private property without due process of law in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment; and (3) the levies, being prohibited by the United States Constitution, were expressly prohibited by the provisions of the Emergency School Tax Act. On appeal, the Bureau of Revenue claimed that the business of the company was interstate commerce so that the tax levied and collected was a violation of the Commerce Clause. The court rejected this argument and affirmed the judgment in favor of the company. The court held that the company's business, as conducted, was interstate. Thus, the tax laid upon the gross receipts of the company from the preparation of opinions and supporting data in Oklahoma, which were delivered to its clients in other states, was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment rendered in favor of the company.

Rubalcava v. Garst


No. 6008


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


61 N.M. 10; 1956-NMSC-017; 293 P.2d 656; 1956 N.M. LEXIS 1040



January 25, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 1, 1956.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for breach of an administrator's bond. The District Court, Socorro County, C. Roy Anderson, D. J., granted defendants' motion for summary judgment and the plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that the evidence supported the judgment for defendant.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff heir appealed a judgment of the District Court, Socorro County (New Mexico), which granted a motion for summary judgment filed by defendants, the administrator of an estate, a surety company, and an attorney in fact, in a suit brought by the heir for breach of the administrator's bond.


OVERVIEW: The heir was given to the decedents, who were childless, in consideration of decedents' promise to raise her as their child and leave her all their property. After decedents' deaths, the final probate decree named the heir as the sole heir at law. The heir brought a complaint against the administrator and the surety alleging a breach of the administrator's bond in that the administrator had sold certain estate property for a price that was lower than another buyer was willing to pay. The trial court granted a motion for summary judgment against the heir because it concluded as a matter of law that the final decree in the probate of the estate barred the litigation. On appeal, the heir argued that the final decree was conditional and that until the conditions of the discharge were complied with, the decree had no operation as a final decree. The court disagreed and affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court found that the heir had failed to object to the sale of the estate property during the probate proceedings in spite of the fact that she had notice that at least one buyer was interested in bidding a higher price for the property. The court dismissed the heir's complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment and the dismissal of the heir's complaint.

 

380 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Schware v. Bd. of Bar Examiners


No. 5847


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


60 N.M. 304; 1955-NMSC-081; 291 P.2d 607; 1955 N.M. LEXIS 1099



September 7, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Dissenting Opinion September 30, 1955. Rehearing Denied December 19, 1955.


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceeding on original petition to review denial by State Board of Bar Examiners of application to take examination for admission to practice law on grounds of applicant's use of aliases, his former connection with subversive organizations and his record of arrests. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that action was warranted by record.



DISPOSITION: Application to take bar examination denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant sought review of the decision of respondent State Board of Bar Examiners (board), which denied the applicant the right to take the examination for admission to practice law.


OVERVIEW: The board denied the applicant permission to take the examination to practice law on the ground of his use of aliases, his former connection with subversive organizations including the Communist party, and his record of arrests. The applicant argued that his right to practice law was a property right protected by U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV. The court stated that granting that bar membership was a species of property as that word was employed in the Constitution: it did not follow, and the court did not take it as contended by the applicant, that the right to its enjoyment was absolute and unfettered by any mode of regulation. The court denied the applicant's application to take the bar examination because to hold otherwise would have been to state that the applicant proved to the court that he was a man of good moral character for the purpose of being given the office of attorney.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that the applicant's application to take the bar examination must be denied.

 

381 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lawson


No. 5903


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


59 N.M. 482; 1955-NMSC-069; 286 P.2d 1076; 1955 N.M. LEXIS 1053



August 10, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: August 10, 1955


PRIOR HISTORY: Defendant was convicted of possessing burglar tools. The District Court of Lea County, John R. Brand, D. J., entered judgment, and defendant appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that criminal intent is an element of the crime defined by act entitled "An Act Defining the Crime of Making, Causing to be Made, or Possessing Any Implements or Things Adapted, Designed or Commonly Used for the Commission of Burglary, Larceny, Safe-Cracking or Other Crime, and Providing a Penalty Therefor", and that therefore the statute is not unconstitutional on ground that the offense is not encompassed in the title, on ground that it granted to the judiciary powers reserved to the Legislature, or on ground that the state was not required by the statute to prove criminal intent and that therefore the statute was void for indefiniteness and uncertainty.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court, Lea County (New Mexico), that convicted him of possession of things adapted, designed, or commonly used to commit burglary, larceny, safe-cracking, or other crimes under circumstances evincing an intent to use, employ, or allow them to be used or employed in the commission of a crime or knowing that the same were intended to be so used. At issue was the constitutionality of 1925 N.M. Laws 63.


OVERVIEW: The defense's constitutional arguments had three variations, and one of them was that 1925 N.M. Laws 63 violated the N.M. Const. art. II, § 18 because the State was not required to prove criminal intent but had only to show possession of statutorily described tools or articles under circumstances that evinced an intent to use or employ them in the commission of a crime. The court ruled that the legislature did not intend for ch. 63 to be a malum prohibitum crime, that was, the State was required to prove specific intent. This interpretive conclusion was partly based on the lack of any language in ch. 63 that clearly indicated that criminal intent was not required and also on the language of ch. 63 regarding evincing an intent. A statute was to be construed with common law in mind, and the existence of a criminal intent was to be regarded as required for conviction albeit the terms of the statute construed did not say it.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and the sentence imposed.

 

382 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Phillips Mercantile Co. v. City of Albuquerque


No. 5889


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


60 N.M. 1; 1955-NMSC-065; 287 P.2d 77; 1955 N.M. LEXIS 1059



July 29, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 12, 1955.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action to set aside vacation of an alley and to have deeds which were issued to abutting owners declared void. The District Court, Bernalillo County, Edwin L. Swope, D. J., found in favor of the plaintiffs and defendants appealed. The Supreme Court, Compton, C. J., held that an owner of property abutting upon the end of a cul-de-sac or dead-end alley but not upon the side thereof had no right in the alley which he shared in common with the public but had only a private and exclusive right, and had no such substantial right as would prevent enactment of a valid ordinance vacating the alley without notification or compensation to him.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions to enter judgment for defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a corporation and a married couple, sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which found in favor of plaintiff partnership in the partnership's action to set aside the vacation of a dead-end alley by defendant City of Albuquerque (New Mexico).


OVERVIEW: The City passed an ordinance vacating an alleyway and deeding one-half each to the corporation and the couple. The partnership, which had purchased the property abutting the end of the alley, filed a petition seeking to set aside the vacation. The trial court declared the ordinance invalid, finding that the City's divestiture had been procedurally defective, and that the partnership had been deprived of a property right without due process of law. Defendants sought review. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and remanded to the trial court. The court found that the City had acted properly in disencumbering itself of property that it had determined was no longer of public use, and that there was no evidence supporting the trial court's determination that the City had adopted and was bound by the provisions of the Planning Commission Act, N.M. Comp. Stat. §§ 14-2-14 et seq. (1953). Moreover, the court found that the partnership, as abutter to the alleyway's dead-end, had no substantial private property right that would have prevented the ordinance's enactment, despite a lack of notification or compensation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter to the trial court with directions to enter judgment for defendants.

 

383 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Hitchcock v. N.M. State Bd. of Registration for Prof'l Eng'rs & Land Surveyors


No. 5875


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


60 N.M. 242; 1955-NMSC-067; 290 P.2d 1077; 1955 N.M. LEXIS 1092



July 29, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 13, 1955 and January 3, 1956.


PRIOR HISTORY: Engineers, whose certificates of registration had been revoked by the New Mexico State Board of Registration for Professional Engineers and Land Surveyors, brought certiorari proceedings to have the order of the board cancelling the licenses of the engineers annulled and to have the board ordered to reinstate the licenses. The District Court of Santa Fe County, David W. Carmody, D. J., entered judgment adverse to the board, and the board appealed. The Supreme Court, Sadler, J., held that statute providing that board shall have power to revoke certificate of registration of any registrant who is found guilty of "gross negligence, incompetency, or misconduct" in practice of professional engineering or land surveying as a registered professional engineer or land surveyor, is not unconstitutional on ground that it is an unlawful attempt to delegate legislative powers to an administrative board, though it does not define "gross negligence", "incompetency" or "misconduct".



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state board of registration for professional engineers and land surveyors (board) sought review of the decision of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which reversed the board's order that cancelled appellee engineers' licenses and order the board to reinstate the licenses in the engineers' action challenging the board's decision to cancel their engineering licenses.


OVERVIEW: The board revoked the engineers' certificates of registration pursuant to N.M. Comp. Law § 67-21-21 (1935), which gave the board the authority to revoke certificates of registration for any registrant who was found guilty by the board of gross negligence, incompetency, or misconduct. The engineers filed an action seeking review of the board's decision, contending that § 67-21-21 was unconstitutional as an unlawful attempt to delegate legislative powers to an administrative board. The trial court reversed the board's decision and ordered that the engineers be reinstated. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court with directions to set aside its judgment and enter judgment affirming the board's order revoking the engineers' licenses. The court found that similar legislative schemes regulating other professions and from other jurisdictions were found to be constitutional, even though they failed to define terms, such as misconduct. Therefore, the court held that § 67-21-21 was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority because it failed to define the terms gross negligence, incompetency, or misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court with directions to set aside its judgment and enter judgment affirming the board's order revoking the engineers' licenses in the engineers' action challenging the boards revocation of their certificate of registration.

 

384 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nolan


No. 5915


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


59 N.M. 437; 1955-NMSC-059; 285 P.2d 798; 1955 N.M. LEXIS 1046



July 5, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: July 5, 1955


PRIOR HISTORY: Defendant was convicted of embezzlement. The District Court of Mora County, Luis E. Armijo, D. J., imposed sentence, and defendant appealed. The Supreme Court, Kiker, J., held that statute dealing with embezzlement of public funds was constitutional.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the District Court of Mora County (New Mexico), which convicted him of embezzlement in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-45-22 (1953).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the county treasurer when a shortage was found in his accounts. He was charged with embezzlement of public funds. On appeal from his conviction, defendant argued that § 40-45-22 was unconstitutionally vague and not a reasonable exercise of the police power and that no formal demand was made for the missing funds. In affirming, the court held that § 40-45-22 required entrustment of the funds as an element of the offense and that the meaning of "entrustment" was clear from its context and in its plain meaning. The court also held that the element and fact of fraud was implied in the conversion to one's own use of public moneys. The court found that the prohibition of embezzlement was a proper exercise of the police power and that § 40-45-22 was complete and clear and unambiguous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

385 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Doyal


No. 5831


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


59 N.M. 454; 1955-NMSC-060; 286 P.2d 306; 1955 N.M. LEXIS 1048



July 5, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 16, 1955.


PRIOR HISTORY: Defendant was convicted of voluntary manslaughter. The District Court, Lea County, Luis E. Armijo, D. J., entered judgment of conviction and defendant appealed. The Supreme Court, Sadler, J., held that action of district judge in holding for trial in District Court minor defendant charged with two murders committed at 14 1/2 years of age, as against remanding case to Juvenile Court for disposition by judge of such court, was not error requiring reversal.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a minor, appealed from the judgments of his convictions of the District Court, Lea County (New Mexico). In prior proceedings in juvenile court, an order issued binding him over to the district court for trial, wherein two new criminal complaints were filed and later consolidated. His motions to quash the complaint and transfer the case back to juvenile court were overruled. A jury convicted him of voluntary manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot to death his stepmother and his young half-sister when he was 14 and 1/2 years of age. Both victims died instantly. Initially, he had forced his stepmother, at gunpoint, to write checks for him as part of his plan to run away. Thereafter, he attempted to confine the victims but the stepmother suddenly had turned toward him. He fired at them in a state of panic. He left the scene planning to escape, but drove to the sheriff's office and confessed the crimes. He urged as error the district court's failure to remand his case to the juvenile court. He claimed, inter alia, that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 13-8-7 (1953) unconstitutionally gave district courts unbridled discretion in deciding whether to try an accused person as an adult or as a juvenile. The court affirmed his convictions, as § 13-8-7 was constitutional. It was not too vague and indefinite for enforcement, and vested jurisdiction in the district court to try juveniles under the age of 18 years for crimes. Defendant's crimes were atrocious and heinous in the extreme. The jury gave full weight to his youth as well as to all other mitigating circumstances as evidenced by the verdict of manslaughter, rather than murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of defendant's convictions.

Fischer v. Rakagis


No. 5913


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


59 N.M. 463; 1955-NMSC-057; 286 P.2d 312; 1955 N.M. LEXIS 1049



June 29, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY: Contractor's action for compensation due under contract for construction of bar in defendants' building. The District Court, Chaves County, C. Roy Anderson, D. J., entered judgment for defendants, and plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, Compton, C. J., held, inter alia, that statute prohibiting unlicensed contractor from suing for compensation is not violative of constitutional guarantees of due process of law or equal protection of laws.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractor sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Chaves County (New Mexico), which entered judgment for defendant building owners in the contractor's action for compensation.


OVERVIEW: The contractor and building owners entered into a contract by which the contractor would build a bar and do carpentry work in the building. The building owners failed to pay the contractor. The contractor brought an action to enforce the contract. The trial court held that because the contractor did not allege that he was licensed, under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 67-16-14 (1953), he could not pursue the action. The contractor appealed. The court held that the action was barred. The court rejected the argument that the bar was personalty and not subject to § 67-16-14, because the bar was built into the building. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional and did not deny the contractor due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

387 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Klantchnek


No. 5893


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


59 N.M. 284; 1955-NMSC-036; 283 P.2d 619; 1955 N.M. LEXIS 1019



May 3, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: May 3, 1955


PRIOR HISTORY: Prosecution for driving a motor vehicle upon a public highway while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. The District Court, Roosevelt County, E. T. Hensley, Jr., D. J., entered judgment of conviction. Accused appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that under statute prohibiting drunken driving and providing that penalty shall be imprisonment for not less than 30 days nor more than one year, but that justices of peace shall have jurisdiction to accept a plea of guilty to first offense and impose a fine of $ 100, the offense was a felony, and section giving jurisdiction to justices of peace conflicted with constitutional grant to District Court of exclusive jurisdiction over felonies, but such section was severable, and portion of statute the accused was tried and sentenced under in District Court was valid, and conviction was proper.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the District Court of Roosevelt County (New Mexico), which convicted him of driving a motor vehicle upon a public highway while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, in violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 64-22-2 (1953), and sentenced him to a term of 90 days in jail, a part of which was ordered suspended upon payment of costs.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a motion to quash the information against him on the basis that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 64-22-2 (1953) coerced persons to plead guilty before a justice of the peace, impermissibly delegated judicial power to an administrative officer, deprived persons of due process of law, and lacked standards for determination of which forum the information should be filed. Appellant argued that the statute violated the Fourteenth Amendment and N.M. Const. art. II, § 18 by denying equal protection under the law because a defendant brought into a justice court could be fined $ 100 on a plea of guilty while in the district court, the offense was punishable by a sentence of one year imprisonment. The court affirmed. The court found that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 40-1-3 (1953), which defined a felony, and N.M. Stat. Ann. § 42-1-37 (1953), which provided that persons sentenced for more than six months be imprisoned in the penitentiary, were applicable to the N.M. Stat. Ann. § 64-22-2 (1953). The court held that the offense was a felony, but that § 4-22-2(e), which pertained to the jurisdiction of justices of the peace to accept a guilty plea and impose a fine, was severable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving a motor vehicle upon a public highway while under the influence of intoxicating liquor.

State ex rel. Prater v. State Bd. of Fin.


No. 5859


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


59 N.M. 121; 1955-NMSC-013; 279 P.2d 1042; 1955 N.M. LEXIS 997



February 9, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: February 9, 1955


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus action by state on relation of State Board of Barber's Examiners and certain members of its board individually against State Board of Finance, to compel latter Board to grant a supplemental budget in the amount of the balance remaining in the Barber Examiners' fund. From an adverse judgment of the District Court, Sante Fe County, David W. Carmody, D. J., the Finance Board appealed. The Supreme Court, Compton, C. J., held that the section of 1953 General Appropriations Act providing that balances remaining to credit of named boards shall revert to general fund, is not, except insofar as it purports to dispose of balances beyond biennium, unconstitutional either as an amendment of Barber's Board Act or as converting latter act from regulatory measure into revenue producing legislation in a general appropriations bill.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with direction to discharge writ.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent State Board of Finance, the Governor of New Mexico, the State Auditor of the State of New Mexico, and others, sought review of a decision of the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which ruled in favor of petitioner, the State Board of Barber Examiners and individuals, in their mandamus action to compel the Finance Board to grant a supplemental budget in the amount of the balance remaining in the Barber Examiners' fund.


OVERVIEW: The Barber Examiners brought a mandamus action against the Finance Board to compel the Finance Board to grant a supplemental budget in the amount of their balance. The district court ruled in favor of the Barber Examiners and the Finance Board appealed. The court reversed. The court found that the General Appropriations Act (Act), 1953 N.M. Laws ch. 156, § 5, did not amend the New Mexico State Barber Examiners' Act, 1937 N.M. Laws ch. 220, § 21; it superseded the appropriations contained in the Act for the biennium mentioned. The court found that 1937 N.M. Laws. ch. 156, § 9 appropriated all unexpended monies to the general fund to meet the Act, except those previously appropriated for specific purposes, contrary to the Barber Examiners' claim. The court found no merit in the argument that the transfer of surplus funds belonging to the Barber Examiners to the General Fund converted the Barbers' Act from a regulatory to a revenue raising act, thereby antagonizing N.M. Const. art. IV, § 16, as such surpluses were germane to general appropriation acts, and the transfer did not alter its regulatory character, except insofar as it purported to dispose of balances beyond biennium.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision.
