State v. Sandoval


No. 5848


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


59 N.M. 85; 1955-NMSC-007; 279 P.2d 850; 1955 N.M. LEXIS 991



February 2, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: February 2, 1955


PRIOR HISTORY: Defendant was convicted, by a jury in the District Court, Bernalillo County, Swope, D. J., of the crime of assault with intent to rape and he appealed. The Supreme Court, Compton, C. J., held that evidence was sufficient to support conviction.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court, Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which convicted him of the crime of assault with intent to rape.


OVERVIEW: Defendant followed his victim in his car, and finally succeeded in getting her to pull her car over to a stop. Then he dragged her out of her car by her hair, beating her. He asked her where she wanted it, in his car or hers. She managed to escape and fled. Her story was corroborated by persons who saw her bruises and heard her screams. Defendant was also found to have cut his hand. In affirming defendant's conviction the court held that the evidence was sufficient to prove that the assault was in furtherance of an attempted rape. The court held that the evidence did not warrant any lesser-included offense instructions. The court also held that the district court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the prosecutor to comment on defendant's failure to testify. The court noted that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-12-19 (1953) authorized these comments and held that § 41-12-19 did not violate defendant's N.M. Const. art. II, § 15, privilege against self-incrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of assault with intent to rape.

 

390 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Chavez


No. 5809


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


58 N.M. 802; 1954-NMSC-114; 277 P.2d 302; 1954 N.M. LEXIS 1202



November 23, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: November 23, 1954


PRIOR HISTORY: Defendant was convicted of embezzlement. The District Court, Bernalillo County, Edwin L. Swope, D. J., rendered judgment on the jury's verdict, and defendant appealed. The Supreme Court, Compton, J., held that the Act providing in the first section thereof that any public official converting to his own use moneys entrusted to him by virtue of his office is guilty of embezzlement was not rendered unconstitutional and void by the provision therein that the existence of a shortage in money for which such an officer is accountable shall be prima facie evidence of his conversion and embezzlement of such money to the extent of the shortage, nor by the Supreme Court's holding that the second section of the Act, declaring any person converting to his own use another's property in such person's possession guilty of embezzlement, and the repealing clause of the third section, are unconstitutional and void because of omission of the elements of entrustment and fraudulent conversion.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a former county treasurer, sought review of his conviction, by the trial court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), for the crime of embezzlement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in changing the venue from the county in which he had been an official; that N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4522 (1941), making the existence of a shortage in the money or property for which public officials are accountable, prima facie evidence of embezzlement by such officials, was unconstitutional and void; and that a fair and impartial jury could not be obtained in the county to which venue was transferred due to inflammatory and prejudicial newspaper articles published there, which were later made the subject of radio broadcasts. The court affirmed the judgment. It held that no abuse of discretion under N.M. Stat. Ann. §§ 19-503, 19-504 (1941) could be found in the trial court's findings of fact regarding local prejudice and its decision to transfer venue. The court also held that even though a portion of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4519 had been found unconstitutional, N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4522, related to embezzlement by public officials, was separable and constitutional. The court also held that defendant's showing of the newspaper articles and radio broadcasts alone was not sufficient proof to entitle him to a change of venue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

391 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Clary v. Denman Drilling Co.


No. 5814


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


58 N.M. 723; 1954-NMSC-105; 276 P.2d 499; 1954 N.M. LEXIS 1189



November 9, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY: Workmen's compensation proceeding. The District Court, San Juan County, Robert E. Fox, D. J., entered judgment denying claim of workman for 50 per cent penalty against employer who had allegedly failed to provide safety device for rig on which claimant was injured, and claimant appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, C. J., held that court will not look behind enrolled and engrossed bill to determine contents of legislative act, and where enrolled and engrossed bill amending workmen's compensation statute provided that where employer fails to provide safety devices required by law, "or prescribed by Labor Industrial Commission as hereafter provided" compensation shall be increased by 50 per cent, fact that journal entries indicated that quoted provision as well as provisions detailing authority of Commission to prescribe devices had been deleted and that act had been amended to award increased compensation when employer fails to supply devices "reasonably necessary" could not be considered.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of the judgment of the District Court, San Juan County (New Mexico), which denied his claim for a 50 percent penalty in his workmen's compensation action against appellees, an employer and an insurer, for the employer's alleged failure to provide a safety device for the rig on which the employee was injured, pursuant to N.M. Comp. Stat. § 57-907 (1941), as amended by 1953 N.M. Laws ch. 96.


OVERVIEW: The employee's claim stated a cause of action for the 50 percent penalty for an employer who had failed to provide a safety device under N.M. Comp. Stat. § 57-907 (1941), prior to its amendment by 1953 N.M. Laws ch. 96. However, as enrolled, engrossed, and published, 1953 N.M. Laws ch. 96 did not contain a floor amendment which contained the penalty provision for employers. On review, the court noted that, even though the omission of the penalty provision was presumably due to an error or neglect of someone charged with including it in the bill as finally signed, the act was valid, workable, and the only law on safety devices. It penalized workmen who came under the Workmen's Compensation Act whose injuries were caused by a failure to follow statutory safety regulations or the failure to use a safety device provided by the employer. The employer was penalized only where such devices were required by statute. Some language left in the bill by inadvertence did not constitute a grant of power to the New Mexico Labor Industrial Commission to prescribe increased compensation for an employer's failure to provide a safety device but rather was to be treated as surplusage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

392 of 795 DOCUMENTS


McCormick v. Bd. of Educ. of Hobbs Mun. Sch. Dist. No. 16


No. 5707


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


58 N.M. 648; 1954-NMSC-094; 274 P.2d 299; 1954 N.M. LEXIS 1175



September 14, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: September 14, 1954


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition by an elementary grade school teacher for writ of mandamus against local board of education, and its members, which had refused to abide by order of the State Board of Education which sustained petitioner's appeal from action of local board in deciding to discontinue petitioner's services. The District Court, Lea County, John R. Brand, D. J., entered a judgment adverse to defendants and defendants appealed. The Supreme Court, Seymour, J., held that petitioner was on tenure when local board attempted to discharge her.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, local school board and members, challenged an order from the District Court, Lea County (New Mexico) that entered a judgment against them in plaintiff teacher's petition for a writ of mandamus. The board had refused to abide by an order of the state board which sustained the teacher's appeal after her discharge.


OVERVIEW: Defendants adopted rules requiring all teachers to have the equivalent of a major in education, and the teacher completed enough courses to bring her credits up to the requirement. The teacher received notice that her contract would not be renewed based on rule infractions. The state board sustained the teacher's appeal, and when defendants' motion to reopen the appeal was denied, the teacher offered to accept employment. Defendants refused to abide by the state board's order and refused to enter into a contract with the teacher. The trial court ruled against defendants in the teacher's petition for a writ of mandamus, and on appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the teacher was entitled to perfect the required qualifications during her probationary period. Thus, the teacher had tenure at the time the controversy arose. The court also found that the teacher had made the required acceptance of employment within the statutory period. A careful reading of the charges and findings led the court to the conclusion that the state board was entirely correct in its decision. N.M. Stat. Ann. § 55-1111 (1941), known as the Teacher's Tenure Act, was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that entered a judgment against defendants in the teacher's petition for a writ of mandamus after the board refused to abide by an order of the state board which sustained the teacher's appeal from her discharge.

 

393 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Crownover v. Crownover


No. 5787


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


58 N.M. 597; 1954-NMSC-092; 274 P.2d 127; 1954 N.M. LEXIS 1170



September 9, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: September 9, 1954


PRIOR HISTORY: Naval officer brought suit for divorce. The District Court of Bernalillo County, Waldo H. Rogers, D. J., entered judgment in favor of naval officer, and his wife appealed. The Supreme Court, Seymour, J., held that where naval officer arrived in the state on September 18, 1952 under military orders directing permanent change of station to base within the state, and on April 17, 1953 he left the base on temporary duty orders placing him physically with the Pacific Fleet and directing his return to base on completion of temporary duty, and temporary duty was completed and he returned to base on November 6, 1953, and on November 11, 1953, he filed suit for divorce, he came within provision of statute dealing with residence requirement for divorce that persons serving in any military branch of the United States government, who had been continuously stationed in any military base or installation in the state for one year shall be deemed residents in good faith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant ex-wife sought review of a judgment rendered by the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico), which held that plaintiff ex-husband met the residence requirement before filing for divorce.


OVERVIEW: The ex-husband, a military officer, filed for and obtained a divorce from the ex-wife. The ex-wife appealed, arguing that the ex-husband did not meet the residency requirement under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 25-704 (1941) before filing for divorce and that § 25-704 was unconstitutional. The court held that § 25-704 was not unconstitutional as violating the New Mexico constitutional provision prohibiting local or special laws and guaranteeing equal protection of the laws, N.M. Const. art. 7, § 4, because it did not discriminate between those living on a military base and those who were not. The court also stated that the statute operated uniformly through the state and did not interfere with federal jurisdiction over military bases. Finally, the court concluded that even though the ex-husband left the state for military duties, he was permanently and continuously stationed in the state, and the statute did not require that the ex-husband had to be physically present for the entire time. The court upheld the trial court's ruling and denied the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

394 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Hudgins v. Public Employees Ret. Bd.


No. 5793


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


58 N.M. 543; 1954-NMSC-084; 273 P.2d 743; 1954 N.M. LEXIS 1162



August 23, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: August 23, 1954


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus proceeding was brought against the Public Employees Retirement Board to compel payment of annuities. The District Court of Santa Fe County, David W. Carmody, D. J., entered judgment adverse to board, and board appealed. The Supreme Court, Lujan, J., held that 1953 act which repealed the 1947 Retirement Act, and which increased benefits to public employees by permitting those employees, who had annuitant status under the 1947 Retirement Act to participate therein provided that they elected to do so by paying an additional lump sum of money equivalent to one and one half per cent of the total salary received during the last five years immediately preceding retirement, did not violate certain sections of the constitution.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public employees retirement board sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which granted appellee participants a writ of mandamus compelling the board to pay annuities to the participants.


OVERVIEW: The participants had been government employees who were retried under existing retirement laws. Pursuant to N.M. Comp. Stat. § 10-602(2.1)(6) (1941), enacted after they retired, the participants were permitted to gain the benefit of a new and enhanced retirement benefit by making a lump-sum payment into the new retirement fund, and the participants did so. In affirming the judgment compelling the board to pay the participants annuities, the court held that the retirement contract between the board and the participants was changed by mutual consent when the participants' deposits were accepted by the board. The court held that § 10-602(2.1)(6) did not violate N.M. Const. art. IV, §§ 27 and 31 or art. IX, § 14, because the payment of the annuity was supported by the consideration received in the form of additional voluntary contributions by the participants. In so holding the court distinguished the annuity from a pension.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that compelled the board to pay annuities to the participants.

 

395 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Abram


No. 5791


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


58 N.M. 404; 1954-NMSC-061; 271 P.2d 1010; 1954 N.M. LEXIS 1141



June 7, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: June 7, 1954


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for writ of habeas corpus to test legality of confinement of accused convicted of embezzlement. The Supreme Court, Lujan, J., held that a misreference to the statute under which accused was charged was not fatal to the information filed against him.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner filed for a writ of habeas corpus to test the legality of his confinement following his conviction for embezzlement under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4524 (1941). The prisoner claimed that because he was charged under an information that cited N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4519 (1941) (repealed), the information was fatally defective and that he was not fully informed of the charges contrary to N.M. Const. art. II, § 14.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner's petition collaterally attacked the judgment of conviction. The court found that the trial court had jurisdiction of the person of the prisoner and of the subject matter of the charge. The applicable embezzlement statute was N.M. Stat. Ann. § 41-4524 (1941). The question was whether the information stated the crime of embezzlement with sufficient particularity under § 41-4524. Under N.M. Stat. Ann. § 42-607 (1941), the information was sufficient if it charged the offense by using the name given to the offense by the common law or by statute. The information charged the prisoner with embezzlement, a common law and statutory offense. Because the offense was otherwise sufficiently charged, the incorrect statutory reference did not render the information invalid or fatally defective. The prisoner was represented by counsel, pled guilty without objecting to the information, and took no appeal. He was not misled as to the charge against him. He was formally accused as required under N.M. Const. art. II, § 14. He was not deprived of his liberty without due process of law or equal protection of law guaranteed under N.M. Stat. Ann. art. II, § 18.


OUTCOME: The prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus that challenged his confinement for an embezzlement conviction was denied.

 

396 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Southern Union Gas Co.


No. 5720


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


58 N.M. 197; 1954-NMSC-033; 269 P.2d 745; 1954 N.M. LEXIS 1110



April 9, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: April 9, 1954


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceedings to determine gas rate that plaintiff, who was operator of a cafe and tourist court, was required to pay, to enjoin defendant from turning off plaintiff's gas and to recover damages for alleged discrimination. The District Court, Curry County, E. T. Hensley, Jr., D. J., dismissed plaintiff's petition and plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, C. J., held that, Public Utility Act requirement that administrative remedy be exhausted before resort is had to the courts is not repugnant to constitutional provision granting general jurisdiction to the District Courts except as elsewhere limited in Constitution.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff customer appealed an order from the District Court for Curry County (New Mexico), which dismissed his petition to enjoin defendant utility from turning off his gas and to recover damages for discrimination in that he was not properly charged for gas under the rates set forth in N.M. Comp. Stat. § 72-301. The customer contended that his business, to which where the gas service was provided, was not properly classified.


OVERVIEW: The customer operated a cafe, at which he received natural gas service from the utility. The customer refused to pay his gas bill because his business was not properly classified; therefore, he argued that he was paying a higher rate than other customers in the same or similar circumstances. The customer filed an action, which alleged discrimination and sought to enjoin the utility from shutting off the gas to the business. The trial court held that the customer had not exhausted his administrative remedies and dismissed the case. The customer appealed, and the court affirmed. The Public Utility Act, N.M. Comp. Stat. § 72-801, provided for a hearing before the commission concerning any rate complaint. The court rejected the customer's argument that relief from discrimination by a public utility was a judicial function. The Act was not a deprivation or ouster of jurisdiction of the courts in violation of N.M. Const. art. VI, § 13, but a postponement until the commission had passed upon the complaint. The court held that the customer failed to exhaust his administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

397 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State v. Roessler


No. 5602


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


58 N.M. 102; 1954-NMSC-017; 266 P.2d 351; 1954 N.M. LEXIS 1093



January 29, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: January 29, 1954


PRIOR HISTORY: Prosecution for contributing to delinquency of female under age of eighteen. Defendant pleaded guilty and was sentenced, and later moved to vacate judgment. The District Court, Santa Fe County, David W. Carmody, D. J., vacated judgment, and state appealed. The Supreme Court, Federici, District Judge, held that information which charged defendant with contributing to delinquency of female under age of eighteen years and which referred to statute making such conduct criminal, was sufficient under statute requiring that indictments and informations define offense or use common law or statutory name of offense and providing that indictments or informations may incorporate statutes by reference.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a plea of guilty to the offense of contributing to the delinquency of a female under the age of 18, a violation of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 44-116 (1941). Subsequently, on defendant's motion, the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico) vacated the judgment. The State sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with contributing to the delinquency of a female under the age of 18. He entered a plea of guilty and the trial court imposed sentence accordingly. Subsequently, defendant moved to vacate the judgment on the ground that the information filed against him was insufficient and invalid. The trial court granted defendant's motion to vacate. The State appealed. On review, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for reinstatement of the original judgment. In reaching its decision, the court held that the information was not fatally defective because the victim's name was not included in it. Moreover, the court held that it was not necessary for the information to include a recitation of the particulars of the offense. Thus, the court concluded that the information was valid and sufficient under the provisions of N.M. Stat. Ann. § 42-607 (1941). Lastly, the court held that N.M. Stat. § 44-116 (1941), the statute under which defendant was charged, was not invalid as being so vague, indefinite, and uncertain as to be incapable of interpretation and enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for reinstatement of the original judgment.

 

398 of 795 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Swope v. Mechem


No. 5723


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


58 N.M. 1; 1954-NMSC-011; 265 P.2d 336; 1954 N.M. LEXIS 1081



January 20, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: January 20, 1954


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding in mandamus by three district judges against governor, involving issue as to expiration date of petitioners' terms of office. The Supreme Court, Seymour, J., held that in view of constitutional provisions evidencing an intent on part of framers of Constitution that the six year terms of office of all district judges within state should run concurrently, terms of office of petitioners, each of whom was elected at first general election following his appointment pursuant to statute increasing number of judges in certain district, would not run for six years from date of election, but would expire upon the expiration date of terms of all other district judges in the state.



DISPOSITION: Writ made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner district court judges brought a mandamus action against respondent Governor of New Mexico seeking a declaration that their terms expired at the same time that the terms of all other district judges expired.


OVERVIEW: The Governor or his predecessors appointed the judges. All the judges were appointed to reflect an increase in the number of judges. It was the contention of the Governor that each judge held his respective office for six years from the date of his election. The judges contended that their terms expired at the same time of all other district judges. They sought a writ enforcing their position. After reviewing the law, the court granted the judge's petition for a writ of mandamus. The court agreed with the judges that their appointments were authorized and controlled by N.M. Const. art. 20, § 4. The court held that the effective application of the last sentence of art. 20, § 4 was addressed to the offices of district attorney and district judge. The court rejected the Governor's argument that art. 20, § 4 applied only in those cases where there was an incumbent in office. The court ruled that under all equations of vacancy in the offices of district attorney and district judge, excepting only a vacancy occurring by the creation of a new judge or district attorney, the terms of district judges and district attorneys would have begun and ended at the same time.


OUTCOME: The court made the judges' writ of mandamus permanent.

 

399 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Wiggs v. City of Albuquerque


No. 5661


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


57 N.M. 770; 1953-NMSC-111; 263 P.2d 963; 1953 N.M. LEXIS 1053



December 2, 1953 


PRIOR HISTORY: Suit to enjoin city from using revenues obtained from tax on gasoline and motor fuel sold in city to pay electric current for street lighting. The District Court, Bernalillo County, Waldo H. Rogers, D. J., dismissed complaint with prejudice, and plaintiff appealed. The Supreme Court, Seymour, J., held that street lighting was an improvement within city ordinance providing for expenditure of revenues from gasoline and motor fuel tax for purpose of street maintenance, improvement, opening and widening only.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a city resident seeking to enjoin defendant city's use of funds collected under Albuquerque, N.M., Ordinance 784, § 6 (1952), appealed the dismissal of his complaint by the District Court of Bernalillo County (New Mexico).


OVERVIEW: Under Albuquerque, N.M., Ordinance 784, § 6 (1952), the city collected taxes on the sale of gasoline and motor fuel in order to fund electric current used for street lighting in the city's downtown area. The city resident filed suit to enjoin the city from using revenue in this manner, asserting that such a use of the funds was a misuse and contrary to the terms of the ordinance. The trial court dismissed the resident's complaint with prejudice, and the resident appealed. In affirming, the court concluded that the ordinance provided for the collection of taxes upon gasoline or motor fuel to fund street improvement projects and that the payment for electric current for street lighting fell within the scope of the word "improvement" as used in § 6 of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

400 of 795 DOCUMENTS


Beatty v. City of Santa Fe


No. 5615


SUPREME COURT OF NEW MEXICO


57 N.M. 759; 1953-NMSC-110; 263 P.2d 697; 1953 N.M. LEXIS 1052



November 19, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: November 19, 1953


PRIOR HISTORY: Wholesalers of cigarettes brought suit against city and city clerk to enjoin enforcement of city ordinance levying a stamp tax on sale of cigarettes within city, on ground that act, under which ordinance was passed, and which empowers municipalities to fix and collect a tax on sale of cigarettes sold within their limits, is unconstitutional. The District Court of Santa Fe County, Edwin L. Swope, D. J., entered judgment adverse to wholesalers, and they appealed. The Supreme Court, McGhee, J., held that the act is not unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cigarette wholesalers appealed a judgment from the District Court of Santa Fe County (New Mexico), which found for defendants, a city and a city clerk, in the wholesalers' action against defendants to enjoin the enforcement of city ordinance levying a stamp tax on sale of cigarettes within the city.


OVERVIEW: The city sought to enact Santa Fe, N.M., Ordinance No. 1046, which levied a stamp tax on sale of cigarettes within city limits. The wholesalers commenced an action against the city and the city clerk to enjoin the enactment of the ordinance, arguing that 1951 N.M. Laws ch. 92, under which Santa Fe, N.M. Ordinance No. 1046 was passed, was unconstitutional. The trial court found for defendants, and the wholesalers appealed. The court held that 1951 N.M. Laws ch. 92 contemplated and empowered municipalities to impose but a single tax, as evidenced by the repeated use of the word "tax" in singular form and meaning. Even if ch. 92 could be construed to authorize a tax levy at each level of sale, there still would be no double taxation in the prohibited sense because, each time a sale occurred, whether by the distributor, wholesaler, or retailer, there was a taxable act. Chapter 92 was not penal because the punitive provision was inseparably tied to the specifications of ordinances to be adopted under ch. 92. While the levy, collection, and enforcement of the tax were given to the city, the subject of the legislation was not changed and was clearly expressed in the title.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.
